Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Following the Imam in Sujud al-Sahw
Explaining the obligation to follow the imam's sujud al-sahw and the distinction between masbuq and lahiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that following the imam's sujud al-sahw is wajib, distinguish between the masbuq and lahiq, and apply the conditions under which the obligation is maintained or dropped.

Core Idea
Following the imam's sujud al-sahw is wajib, but the masbuq follows immediately while the lahiq delays until after completing missed rak'ahs.

In this passage, Imam Ibn Nujaym expands on the second cause of sujud al-sahw: the imam's forgetfulness. The follower is bound to follow the imam in his sujud, but this general rule has important exceptions based on whether the follower is a mudrik (caught the whole prayer), masbuq (caught part), or lahiq (joined late and will complete his own prayer separately). We will examine the proof, the general duty, and the critical distinction between masbuq and lahiq, as well as cases where the obligation drops.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two causes of sujud al-sahw
The matn states sujud al-sahw is required either for leaving a wajib or due to the imam's forgetfulness. Understand that this lesson covers the second cause.
2
Analyze the dalil for following
The text cites the Prophet's own sujud al-sahw with the companions following, and the principle that the follower is bound by the imam's actions. Identify that this establishes obligation (wujub).
The dalil is a combination of the Prophet's practice (fi'l) and the general maxim 'the follower follows the imam'.
3
Distinguish the three categories of followers
The passage mentions mudrik (caught whole prayer), masbuq (caught one or more rak'ahs but not all), and lahiq (joins late, misses some rak'ahs, but is considered a follower for the remainder). Understand that all are bound by the imam's sujud, but the timing differs.
The key is that the lahiq has committed to follow the imam in the entire prayer, so he completes his own prayer first.
4
Apply the ruling to masbuq and lahiq
The masbuq follows the imam immediately in sujud al-sahw before completing his own prayer. The lahiq does NOT follow immediately; he first makes up his missed rak'ahs, then performs sujud al-sahw at the end of his own prayer.
The difference stems from the nature of their connection to the imam's prayer.
5
Handle exceptions and consequences
If the imam's sujud is dropped (due to talking, hadath, etc.), the follower is not required to do it. If a lahiq incorrectly follows, it does not suffice and he must repeat, but his prayer is not invalidated. If a masbuq follows and then discovers the imam had no forgetfulness, his prayer is invalidated unless he was unaware.
Istihsan applies when the masbuq does not follow and stands up: he performs sujud at the end nonetheless.

Source Text

قوله : (وبسهو إمامه لا بسهوه معطوف على قوله بترك واجب» فأفاد أن السجود له سببان : إما ترك الواجب أو سهو إمامه فإنه يجب عليه متابعته إذا سجد لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام سجد له وتبعه القوم ولأنه تبع لإمامه فيلزمه حكم فعله كالمفسدونية الإقامة. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان مقتدياً به وقت السهو أو لم يكن وما إذا سجد سجدة واحدة ثم اقتدى به فإنه يتابعه في الأخرى ولا يقضي الأولى كما لا يقضيهما لو اقتدى به بعد ما سجدهما لأنه حين دخل في تحريمة الإمام كان النقص قد انجبر بالسجدتين أو بإحداهما، ولا يعقل وجوب قوله : (وأما التشهد الرابع قال الرملي هذا جواب سؤال مقدر كأنه قيل قدر تقرر أنه لا تشهد في سجود التلاوة فأجاب بقوله وأما التشهد الخ ) قوله : (الأن سجود التلاوة رفع الخ) قال جابر من غير نقص. وقيد بأن يكون الإمام سجد لأنه لو سقط عن الإمام بسبب من الأسباب بأن تكلم أو أحدث متعمداً أو خرج من المسجد فإنه يسقط عن المقتدي بخلاف تكبير التشريق حيث يأتي به المؤتم وإن تركه الإمام لكونه لا يؤدي في حرمتها. وشمل كلامه المدرك والمسبوق واللاحق فإنه يلزمهم بسهو إمامهم لكن اللاحق لا يتابع الإمام في سجود السهو إذا انتبه في حال اشتغال الإمام بسجود السهو أو جاء إليه من الوضوء في هذه الحالة، وإنما يبدأ بقضاء ما فاته ثم يسجد في آخر صلاته والمسبوق والمقيم خلف المسافر يتابعان الإمام في سجود السهو ثم يشتغلان بالإتمام والفرق أن اللاحق التزم متابعة الإمام فيما اقتدى به على نحو ما يصلي الإمام وأنه اقتدى به في جميع الصلاة فيتابعه في جميعها على نحو ما أدى الإمام والإمام أدى الأول فالأول وسجد لسهوه في آخر صلاته، فكذا اللاحق، فأما المسبوق فقد التزم بالاقتداء متابعته بقدر ما هو صلاة الإمام وقد أدرك هذا القدر فيتابعه فيه ثم ينفرد، وكذا المقيم المقتدي بالمسافر فلو كان مسبوقاً بثلاث ولاحقاً بركعة فسجد إمامه للسهو فإنه يقضي ركعة بغير قراءة لأنه لا حق، ويتشهد ويسجد للسهو لأن ذلك موضع سجود الإمام، ثم يصلي ركعة بقراءة ويقعد لأنها ثانية صلاته ولو كان على العكس سجد للسهو بعد الثالثة. كذا في المحيط. ولو سجد اللاحق مع الإمام للسهو ولم يجزه لأنه في غير في حقه فعليه أن يعيد إذا فرغ من قضاء ما عليه ولكن لا تفسد صلاته لأنه ما زاد إلا سجدتين بخلاف المسبوق إذا تابع الإمام في سجود السهو ثم تبين أنه لم يكن على الإمام سهو حيث تفسد صلاة المسبوق لكونه اقتدى في موضع الانفراد لا لزيادة السجدتين ولم يوجد في اللاحق لأنه مقتد في جميع ما يؤدي. كذا في البدائع. أوانه وفصل في المحيط بين أن يعلم أنه ليس على إمامه سهو فيفسد، وبين أن لا يعلم أنه لم يكن عليه فلا يفسد لأن كثيراً ما يقع الجهلة الأئمة فسقط اعتبار المفسد هنا للضرورة ا هـ . ولو لم يتابع المسبوق إمامه وقام إلى قضاء ما سبق به فإنه يسجد في آخر صلاته استحساناً لأن التحريمة متحدة فجعل كأنها صلاة واحدة.
His statement: (And due to his imam's forgetfulness, not due to his own forgetfulness) is coordinated with his statement 'by leaving an obligatory act.' So it indicates that prostration has two causes: either leaving an obligatory act or the imam's forgetfulness. For it is obligatory upon him to follow him when he prostrates, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated for it and the people followed him, and because he follows his imam, so the ruling of his action applies to him, like the nullifier of the prayer by facing the qibla? (unclear). He made it absolute, so it includes whether he was following him at the time of forgetfulness or not, and whether he prostrated one prostration and then followed him—he follows him in the other and does not make up the first, just as he would not make up both if he followed him after he had prostrated them, because when he entered the imam's tahrima, the deficiency had already been compensated by the two prostrations or by one of them, and it is not reasonable that obligation... His statement: (As for the fourth tashahhud...) al-Ramli said this is an answer to an implied question, as if it was said: It is established that there is no tashahhud in the prostration of recitation, so he answered by saying: 'As for the fourth tashahhud...' His statement: (Because the prostration of recitation lifted...) He said: Jabir without deficiency. And he restricted it to the condition that the imam prostrated, because if it is dropped from the imam due to some reason, such as he spoke or intentionally caused an event or left the mosque, then it is dropped from the follower, unlike the takbir of tashriq where the follower performs it even if the imam leaves it, because it is not performed in its sacredness. And his statement includes the one who catches the entire prayer, the masbuq, and the lahiq, for it is binding on them due to their imam's forgetfulness. But the lahiq does not follow the imam in sujud al-sahw if he notices while the imam is occupied with sujud al-sahw or comes from wudu in that state; rather, he begins by making up what he missed, then prostrates at the end of his prayer. The masbuq and the resident following a traveler follow the imam in sujud al-sahw, then occupy themselves with completing the prayer. The difference is that the lahiq committed to following the imam in what he followed him in, in the same manner as the imam prays, and he followed him in the entire prayer, so he follows him in all of it in the manner that the imam performed, and the imam performed the first first and prostrated for his forgetfulness at the end of his prayer, so likewise the lahiq. As for the masbuq, he committed to following him to the extent that is the imam's prayer, and he caught this amount, so he follows him in it, then becomes independent. Likewise, the resident following a traveler. So if one is a masbuq by three and a lahiq by one rak'ah, and his imam prostrates for forgetfulness, he makes up one rak'ah without recitation because he is a lahiq, and he performs tashahhud and prostrates for forgetfulness because that is the place of the imam's prostration, then he prays one rak'ah with recitation and sits because it is the second of his prayer. And if the opposite, he prostrates for forgetfulness after the third. This is in al-Muhit. And if the lahiq prostrates with the imam for forgetfulness, it does not suffice him because it is not in his right, so he must repeat when he finishes making up what is due upon him, but his prayer is not invalidated because he only added two prostrations, unlike the masbuq if he follows the imam in sujud al-sahw and then it becomes clear that there was no forgetfulness on the imam, for then the masbuq's prayer is invalidated because he followed in a place of independence, not due to the increase of two prostrations, and this is not found in the lahiq because he follows in all that he performs. This is in al-Bada'i'. And it is detailed in al-Muhit between if he knows that there is no forgetfulness on his imam, then it invalidates, and if he does not know that there was no forgetfulness, then it does not invalidate, because often ignorant imams occur, so the consideration of invalidation is dropped here due to necessity. End quote. And if the masbuq does not follow his imam and stands up to make up what he preceded with, then he prostrates at the end of his prayer by istihsan, because the tahrima is one, so it is made as if it is one prayer.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, explaining the second cause of sujud al-sahw: following the imam's forgetfulness. The commentator, Imam Ibn Nujaym, begins by stating the ruling from the matn: sujud al-sahw is required either for leaving a wajib or due to the imam's forgetfulness. He then provides the proof: the Prophet (saw) prostrated for forgetfulness and the companions followed him. The follower is bound by the imam's action, similar to other rulings. The rule is absolute: any follower, whether he was with the imam at the time of forgetfulness or not, must follow. If the imam prostrates one sajdah and then someone joins, the follower only does the second sajdah and does not make up the first, because the deficiency was already compensated. The commentator then discusses a subtle point about the fourth tashahhud in complex scenarios, quoting al-Ramli. He then clarifies a condition: the obligation to follow only applies if the imam actually prostrates; if the imam's sujud is dropped due to speech, intentional hadath, or leaving the mosque, the follower is not required to do it. This differs from takbir al-tashriq, where the follower still performs it even if the imam leaves it. The passage then distinguishes between three categories: mudrik (catches whole prayer), masbuq (catches part), and lahiq (joins after having missed some rak'ahs but still is considered a follower for the rest). All are bound by the imam's forgetfulness, but the lahiq does not follow the imam in sujud al-sahw immediately; rather, he first makes up his missed rak'ahs and then prostrates at the end of his own prayer. In contrast, the masbuq follows the imam in sujud al-sahw before completing his own prayer. The reason is that the lahiq has committed to follow the imam in the entire prayer, but the imam performed his sujud at the end, so the lahiq should also do his after completing what he missed. The masbuq only follows for the part he caught, so he follows the imam's sujud and then becomes independent. A practical example is given: if someone is a masbuq by three rak'ahs and a lahiq by one, and the imam does sujud al-sahw, he first makes up one rak'ah without recitation (as a lahiq), then does tashahhud and sujud, then continues. A ruling follows: if a lahiq incorrectly follows the imam in sujud al-sahw, it does not suffice; he must repeat it, but his prayer is not invalidated because he only added two sajdahs. However, if a masbuq follows the imam and then it becomes clear the imam had no forgetfulness, his prayer is invalidated because he followed in a place where he should have been independent. But if he was unaware, it does not invalidate due to necessity. Finally, if the masbuq does not follow the imam and stands up to complete his missed rak'ahs, he must perform sujud al-sahw at the end of his own prayer by istihsan, because the tahrima is one, making his prayer and the imam's effectively one prayer.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness (sahw) during prayer, due to leaving a wajib or following the imam's forgetfulness.
مسبوق (masbuq): A follower who did not catch the entire prayer with the imam; he catches at least one rak'ah with the imam and then completes his prayer independently.
لاحق (lahiq): A follower who joins the prayer late, such that he is considered following the imam for the remainder, but is responsible for making up missed parts in a specific order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a masbuq (follower who caught part of the prayer) does not follow the imam in sujud al-sahw and stands up to complete his missed rak'ahs, what must he do?
A) He does nothing extra; his prayer is valid without sujud al-sahw.
B) He must perform sujud al-sahw at the end of his own prayer by istihsan.
C) He must repeat the entire prayer.
D) He must perform sujud al-sahw immediately upon remembering.

Key Takeaway
Following the imam's sujud al-sahw is wajib, but the lahiq delays his sujud until after making up missed rak'ahs, while the masbuq follows immediately.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Followers Bound by Imam's Sajdah al-Sahw: Masbuq, Lahiq, and Mudrik
Explaining when each type of follower follows the imam in sajdah al-sahw.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings for the masbuq, lahiq, and mudrik regarding following the imam in sajdah al-sahw and apply them to given prayer scenarios.

Core Idea
The follower is bound by the imam's sajdah al-sahw, but the lahiq postpones it until after his qada.

The Hanafi school has detailed rules about how a follower must respond when the imam performs sajdah al-sahw. The key is to identify which category the follower falls into: mudrik (caught the entire prayer), masbuq (latecomer who missed part), or lahiq (one who missed some rak'ahs due to sleep or similar). Each has a different obligation. Let's unpack the rules from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of followers
Understand the definitions of mudrik (caught entire prayer), masbuq (caught part, missed part), and lahiq (caught part, then missed due to sleep etc.).
These categories determine the ruling on following sajdah al-sahw.
2
State the general rule
All three are bound by the imam's forgetfulness, meaning they must eventually perform sajdah al-sahw if the imam does.
But the timing differs.
3
Explain the masbuq ruling
The masbuq follows the imam in sajdah al-sahw immediately, then completes his missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam.
This is because he only followed in the portion he caught.
4
Explain the lahiq ruling
The lahiq does NOT follow the imam in sajdah al-sahw. He first makes up his missed rak'ahs (qada), then performs sajdah al-sahw at the end of his own prayer.
The lahiq's commitment to follow is total, so he must replicate the imam's order, including postponing sajdah.
5
Note the muqim behind a musafir
The muqim (resident) praying behind a musafir (traveler) who shortens prayer is like a masbuq: he follows in sajdah al-sahw, then completes his full prayer.
There is a difference of opinion within the school on whether he performs sajdah for his own forgetfulness later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو جابر من غير نقص. وقيد بأن يكون الإمام سجد لأنه لو سقط عن الإمام بسبب من الأسباب بأن تكلم أو أحدث متعمداً أو خرج من المسجد فإنه يسقط عن المقتدي بخلاف تكبير التشريق حيث يأتي به المؤتم وإن تركه الإمام لكونه لا يؤدي في حرمتها. وشمل كلامه المدرك والمسبوق واللاحق فإنه يلزمهم بسهو إمامهم لكن اللاحق لا يتابع الإمام في سجود السهو إذا انتبه في حال اشتغال الإمام بسجود السهو أو جاء إليه من الوضوء في هذه الحالة، وإنما يبدأ بقضاء ما فاته ثم يسجد في آخر صلاته والمسبوق والمقيم خلف المسافر يتابعان الإمام في سجود السهو ثم يشتغلان بالإتمام والفرق أن اللاحق التزم متابعة الإمام فيما اقتدى به على نحو ما يصلي الإمام وأنه اقتدى به في جميع الصلاة فيتابعه في جميعها على نحو ما أدى الإمام والإمام أدى الأول فالأول وسجد لسهوه في آخر صلاته، فكذا اللاحق، فأما المسبوق فقد التزم بالاقتداء متابعته بقدر ما هو صلاة الإمام وقد أدرك هذا القدر فيتابعه فيه ثم ينفرد، وكذا المقيم المقتدي بالمسافر فلو كان مسبوقاً بثلاث ولاحقاً بركعة فسجد إمامه للسهو فإنه يقضي ركعة بغير قراءة لأنه لا حق، ويتشهد ويسجد للسهو لأن ذلك موضع سجود الإمام، ثم يصلي ركعة بقراءة ويقعد لأنها ثانية صلاته ولو كان على العكس سجد للسهو بعد الثالثة. كذا في المحيط. ولو سجد اللاحق مع الإمام للسهو ولم يجزه لأنه في غير في حقه فعليه أن يعيد إذا فرغ من قضاء ما عليه ولكن لا تفسد صلاته لأنه ما زاد إلا سجدتين بخلاف المسبوق إذا تابع الإمام في سجود السهو ثم تبين أنه لم يكن على الإمام سهو حيث تفسد صلاة المسبوق لكونه اقتدى في موضع الانفراد لا لزيادة السجدتين ولم يوجد في اللاحق لأنه مقتد في جميع ما يؤدي. كذا في البدائع. أوانه وفصل في المحيط بين أن يعلم أنه ليس على إمامه سهو فيفسد، وبين أن لا يعلم أنه لم يكن عليه فلا يفسد لأن كثيراً ما يقع الجلة الأئمة فسقط اعتبار المفسد هنا للضرورة ا هـ . ولو لم يتابع المسبوق إمامه وقام إلى قضاء ما سبق به فإنه يسجد في آخر صلاته استحساناً لأن التحريمة متحدة فجعل كأنها صلاة واحدة. ولو سها فيما يقضي ولم يسجد لسهو إمامه كفاه سجدتان، ولو سجد مع الإمام ثم سها فيما يقضي فعليه السهو ثانياً لما أن ذلك أداء مر السهو في صلاتين حكماً فلم يكن تكراراً. ثم المسبوق إنما يتابع الإمام في السهو لا في السلام فيسجد معه ويتشهد فإذا سلم الإمام قام إلى القضاء، فإن سلم فإن كان عامداً فسدت وإلا فلا ولا سجود عليه إن سلم قبل الإمام أو معه، وإن سلم بعده لزمه لكونه منفرداً حينئذ. وعلى هذا لو أحدث الإمام بعد السلام قبل السجود فاستخلف مسبوقاً وارتكب خلاف الأولى وتقدم ينبغي أن يستخلف مدركاً ليسجد بهم ويسجد هو معهم، وإن لم يسجد مع خليفته سجد في آخر صلاته، فإن لم يجد المسبوق مدركاً وكانوا كلهم مسبوقين قاموا وقضوا ما سبقوا به فرادى ثم إذا فرغوا يسجدون ولو قام المسبوق إلى قضاء ما سبق به بعد ما سلم الإمام ثم تذكر الإمام أن عليه سجود السهو قبل أن يقيد المسبوق ركعة بسجدة فعليه أن يرفض ذلك ويعود إلى متابعة الإمام، ثم إذا سلم الإمام قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به ولا يعتد بما فعل من القيام والقراءة والركوع ولو لم يعد إلى الإمام ومضى على صلاته يجوز ويسجد للسهو بعد ما فرغ من القضاء استحساناً. ولو تذكر الإمام أن عليه سجدتي السهو بعد ما قيد المسبوق ركعته بسجدة فإنه لا يعود إلى الإمام ولا يتابعه في سجود السهو، ولو تابعه فيها تفسد صلاته لزيادة ركعة وقد ذكرنا بقية مسائل المسبوق في باب الحدث في الصلاة. ولو سها الإمام في صلاة الخوف سجد للسهو وتابعه فيها الطائفة الثانية، وأما الطائفة الأولى وإنما يسجدون بعد الفراغ من الإتمام لأن الثانية بمنزلة المسبوقين والأولى بمنزلة اللاحقين. وإنما لم يلزم المأموم سهو نفسه لأنه لو سجد وحده كان مخالفاً لإمامه إن سجد قبل السلام وإن أخره إلى ما بعد سلام الإمام يخرج من الصلاة بسلام الإمام لأنه سلام عمد لا سهو عليه ولو تابعه الإمام ينقلب التبع أصلاً. وشمل كلامه المدرك واللاحق فإنه مقتد في جميع صلاته بدليل أنه لا قراءة عليه فلا سجود لو سها فيما يقضيه مطلقاً، وأما المقيم إذا اقتدى بالمسافر ثم قام لإتمام صلاته وسها فذكر الكرخي أنه كاللاحق فلا سجود عليه بدليل أنه لا يقرأ، وذكر في الأصل أنه يلزمه السجود وصححه في البدائع لأنه إنما اقتدى بالإمام بقدر صلاة الإمام فإذا انقضت صلاة الإمام صارت منفرداً فيما وراء ذلك . وإنما لا يقرأ فيما يتم لأن القراءة فرض في الأوليين وقد قرأ الإمام فيهما.
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Sajdah al-Sahw. ... (full literal translation would be long) Summary: The general rule covers the one who catches the whole prayer, the latecomer, and the one who has to make up; they are bound by the imam's forgetfulness, but the lahiq does not follow the imam in sajdah al-sahw if he becomes aware during the imam's sajdah; he first makes up what he missed then prostrates at the end of his prayer. The masbuq and the muqim behind a musafir follow the imam in sajdah al-sahw and then complete their prayer...
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rules of sajdah al-sahw concerning the follower. The author begins by stating that the ruling covers three categories: al-mudrik (one who catches the entire prayer with the imam), al-masbuq (latecomer who misses some rak'ahs), and al-lahiq (one who catches part but then misses due to sleep or other reason). All are obligated by the imam's forgetfulness, meaning they must perform sajdah al-sahw if the imam does. However, the lahiq is an exception: if he becomes aware during the imam's sajdah al-sahw, he does not follow the imam but instead makes up what he missed first, then prostrates at the end of his own prayer. The masbuq and the muqim behind a musafir do follow the imam in sajdah al-sahw. The difference is that the lahiq has committed to following the imam in all aspects of his prayer, including the order, so he postpones his sajdah. The masbuq only follows in the portion he caught, so he follows in sajdah and then separates. Various subsidiary cases are discussed: if the imam forgets his sajdah, if the follower incorrectly follows, etc. The text also discusses cases of doubt and the ruling when the imam's forgetfulness is discovered later. The general principle is that the follower should not perform sajdah for his own forgetfulness because it would disagree with the imam, but if he does so after the imam's salam, it is okay. The passage ends with a discussion of whether the muqim behind a musafir is considered like a lahiq or not, with a difference between al-Karkhi and the author of al-Asl, with al-Bada'i' preferring the latter.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late and misses part of it. He catches up with the imam partway through.
لاحق (lahiq): A person who misses some rak'ahs due to sleep or other reason after having caught the imam, and then rejoins. He does not follow the imam in sajdah al-sahw; he performs it after his own qada.
مدرك (mudrik): One who catches the entire prayer from the beginning with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following followers does NOT follow the imam in sajdah al-sahw immediately?
A) Mudrik
B) Masbuq
C) Muqim behind a musafir
D) Lahiq

Key Takeaway
The masbuq and mudrik must follow the imam in sajdah al-sahw; the lahiq postpones his sajdah until after his qada.

When Must the Masbuq Follow the Imam in Sujud al-Sahw?
Rulings for a latecomer when the imam forgets and performs prostration of forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios of a masbuq following the imam in sujud al-sahw and apply the ruling of istihsan when the masbuq continues alone.

Core Idea
The masbuq must follow the imam in sujud al-sahw unless he has already tied his rak'ah with a sajdah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies when a latecomer (masbuq) must follow the imam in the prostration of forgetfulness. The ruling depends on whether the masbuq has completed his first rak'ah with a prostration. The Hanafi school uses istihsan to allow the masbuq to continue alone if he does not return to the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the masbuq's response when the imam remembers sujud al-sahw. The ruling is that he must follow the imam if he hasn't tied his rak'ah.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Determine whether the masbuq has completed his rak'ah with a sajdah or not. The text gives two distinct rulings.
3
Understand the istihsan ruling
If the masbuq does not return to the imam and continues alone, his prayer is valid but he must perform sujud al-sahw after finishing the makeup.
4
Trace the proof
The ruling is based on istihsan, preferring practical completion over strict analogy.

The book of prayer, chapter of prostration of forgetfulness. Then after the imam had said the salam, then the imam remembered that he owes the prostration of forgetfulness before the latecomer had bound his rak'ah with a prostration: then he must discard that and return to following the imam. Then when the imam says salam, he stands to make up what was missed and does not count what he did of standing, recitation, and bowing. And if he did not return to the imam and continued his prayer, it is permissible, and he performs the prostration of forgetfulness after finishing the makeup, as a matter of istihsan. And if the imam remembered that he owes the two prostrations of forgetfulness after the latecomer had bound his rak'ah with a prostration, then he does not return to the imam and does not follow him in the prostration of forgetfulness. And if he follows him in it, his prayer becomes invalid due to the addition of a rak'ah. And we have mentioned the remaining issues of the latecomer in the chapter on invalidating events in prayer. And if the imam forgets in the prayer of fear, he performs the prostration of forgetfulness and the second group follows him in it. As for the first group, they only prostrate after completing the prayer, because the second group is like latecomers and the first group is like those who join later. And the follower is not obligated for his own forgetfulness because if he prostrates alone, he would be opposing his imam if he prostrates before the salam, and if he delays it until after the imam's salam, he exits the prayer by the imam's salam because it is an intentional salam with no forgetfulness upon him. And if the imam follows him, the follower becomes the leader. His statement includes the one who joined from the beginning and the one who joins later, for he is a follower in all of his prayer, evidenced by the fact that he does not recite, so there is no prostration if he forgets in what he makes up absolutely. As for the resident who follows a traveler then stands to complete his prayer and forgets, al-Karkhi mentioned that he is like the latecomer, so no prostration upon him, evidenced by the fact that he does not recite. And it is mentioned in al-Asl that prostration is obligatory upon him, and it was corrected in al-Bada'i' because he only followed the imam to the extent of the imam's prayer. When the imam's prayer ends, he becomes alone in what is beyond that. And he does not recite in what he completes because recitation is fard in the first two rak'ahs, and the imam recited in them. And it includes the latecomer in what he performs with the imam. As for what he makes up, he is like one praying alone as previously mentioned. And upon this is based what if he says salam... al-Ramli: This is an answer arising from his first statement and it is not problematic what is in several fatawa... His statement: (he exits the prayer by the imam's salam) said in al-Nahr: one might say we do not accept that he exits by his salam, and there has passed a difference regarding forgetfulness upon him, so how about one upon whom there is forgetfulness? Then he can bring this restorative. His intent by the difference is what the author mentioned in the chapter on invalidating events in prayer from al-Muhit, that the statement: they exit the prayer by the imam's intentional invalidating event unanimously, and for this they do not say salam and do not exit by his salam according to the two, contrary to Muhammad. As for his speech, from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations. But it is mentioned in Nawagid al-Wudu': if the people laugh after the imam intentionally invalidates, there is no wudu upon them, and similarly after the imam speaks, and similarly after the imam's salam, it is the most correct. Such is al-Khulasah. And it is said: if they guffaw after his salam, their wudu is invalidated. The difference is based on whether after the imam's salam he is still in prayer until he says salam himself or not. Based on that, the implication of al-Khulasah is that the second is most correct, hence he firmly stated it here, and its apparent meaning is no distinction between one with forgetfulness and without, so the statement of al-Nahr falls. So ponder. And in al-Nahr also: then the implication of their statement is that he repeats it due to the confirmation of dislike with the unavailability of a restorative. His statement: (and the imam recited in them) in al-Nahr: by this it is known that he is like the latecomer only in the matter of recitation.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with the rulings of a masbuq (latecomer) when the imam forgets and must perform sujud al-sahw. The passage is a ruling with proof, expanding on the matn. The author presents several scenarios: (1) If the imam remembers the sujud before the masbuq has tied his first rak'ah (i.e., before completing it with a sajdah), then the masbuq must discard his own partial rak'ah and follow the imam. After the imam's salam, he stands to complete his missed rak'ahs. (2) If the masbuq does not return to the imam and continues alone, it is permissible, but he must perform sujud al-sahw after completing his makeup, based on istihsan. (3) If the imam remembers after the masbuq has already tied his rak'ah with a sajdah, the masbuq does not return to the imam and does not follow him in sujud al-sahw; if he follows, his prayer becomes invalid. The passage also discusses sahw in salat al-khawf, and then addresses the ruling for a muqim who follows a musafir and then completes his prayer alone: al-Karkhi says no sujud, but the relied-upon view is that sujud is required. The commentary includes extensive discussion from later scholars on related issues, such as whether one exits the prayer by the imam's salam when one owes sujud. The overall purpose is to clarify the fiqh of following the imam in cases of forgetfulness.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregation after the imam has already started, missing at least one rak'ah.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam remembers that he must perform sujud al-sahw after the masbuq has already completed his first rak'ah with a sajdah, what should the masbuq do?
A) He must return to follow the imam.
B) He should not follow the imam and should not perform sujud al-sahw.
C) He should not follow the imam in sujud al-sahw; if he follows, his prayer becomes invalid.
D) He must perform sujud al-sahw alone after the imam's salam.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq must follow the imam in sujud al-sahw only if he has not yet performed the sajdah of his current rak'ah; otherwise following invalidates the prayer.

Forgetting the First Sitting: Proximity as the Criterion
Determines when one who forgets the first tashahhud and stands up should return to sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of proximity to determine whether a person who forgets the first tashahhud should return to sitting or continue standing.

Core Idea
Proximity to sitting decides: if closer to sitting, return; if closer to standing, do not return.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common situation in prayer: a person forgets the first tashahhud (after the second rak'ah) and begins to stand for the third rak'ah. The Hanafi school has a detailed rule based on how far the person has progressed—whether they are closer to sitting or to standing. We will examine the ruling, the evidence from the Prophet's actions, and the key difference between the positions of Abu Yusuf and the apparent narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The first sitting (tashahhud) is a wajib in the Hanafi school. Forgetting it requires compensation (sujud al-sahw) or, if possible, returning to the sitting.
Wajib vs. fard: omitting a wajib requires sujud al-sahw, but prayer remains valid.
2
Define the condition: proximity
The passage states the criterion: 'if he is closer to it (the sitting), he returns; otherwise not.' Proximity is determined by how much of the standing motion is completed—whether knees still on ground, lower half not yet straight.
The ruling is conditional: the person must be in a state where the standing is not yet fully engaged.
3
Examine the evidence from hadith
Two narrations: the Prophet once returned when not fully stood, and once did not return after fully standing. The Hanafis reconcile by distinguishing between closeness to sitting vs. standing.
The hadith is ahad, zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf's view relies on proximity; the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) uses full standing as the cut-off. The muta'akhkhirin (later scholars) preferred Abu Yusuf's view.
The mufta bihi position is based on proximity.
5
Apply the rule to a practical scenario
If a worshipper lifts his buttocks but knees remain on ground, he is closer to sitting and should return. If he has straightened his legs fully, he is closer to standing and must not return.
Returning when prohibited may cause ikhtilaf on validity, but the correct view is prayer remains valid with sujud al-sahw.

by his forgetfulness. And if he forgets the first sitting and he is closer to it, he returns; otherwise not, and he performs the prostration for forgetfulness, even if he was forgetful. If it was before the imam or with him, then no prostration; if after him, then it is upon him as we mentioned. And in al-Muhit and others: It is recommended for the latecomer to wait a while after the imam finishes, then stand up, in case the imam has forgetfulness. Regarding his statement: (And if he forgets the first sitting and he is closer to it, he returns; otherwise not) meaning to the sitting, because the principle is that what is close to a thing takes its ruling, like the courtyard of a settlement and the precinct of a well. So if he is closer to sitting, such that he has lifted his buttocks from the ground but his knees are still on it, or he has not fully straightened the lower half—and it was corrected in al-Kafi that he is as if he never stood. If he is closer to standing, then he is as if he has stood, and standing is a fard that he has engaged in, so it is not permissible to discard it for the sake of a wajib which is the sitting. This detail is reported from Abu Yusuf and chosen by the scholars of Bukhara and approved by the authors of the matn. In al-Kafi, our mashayikh preferred his narration. And it is mentioned in al-Mabsut that the apparent narration is: if he has not fully stood, he returns; if he has fully stood, he does not return, because the hadith came from the Prophet that he stood from the second to the third before sitting, so they glorified to him and he returned. It is also narrated that he did not return, and that was after he had fully stood. This is because when he fully stands, he becomes occupied with the fard of standing, so he does not abandon it. The commentator corrected this. And in Fath al-Qadir, it is the apparent madhhab. Reconciling the two narrated actions by attributing them to the states of closeness to standing or not is not more preferable than attributing them to equality or its lack. Then if he returns in a situation where it is obligatory not to, they differed on the corruption of his prayer. The commentator corrected corruption due to completeness of impurity by discarding a fard after commencing it for the sake of what is not fard. In al-Muqtana (with aghayn mu'jama), it is said this is a mistake because it is not abandonment but rather delay, just like if one forgets the Surah and bows, he discards the bowing and returns to standing and recites for the sake of the wajib; and likewise if one forgets the qunut and bows, if he returns and recites qunut, it does not corrupt according to the most correct view. And it may be said that if he returns and recites the Surah, the Surah becomes fard, so he returns from fard to fard. And qunut has a resemblance to Quran, based on what is said that it was originally Quran and then abrogated, so he returns to something with a resemblance. The statement of the author: (and he is closer to it) said in al-Nahr: in his statement there is a muqaddam over ma'mul of af'al al-tafdil, which is forbidden according to them, but Sadr al-Afadil allowed it for broadening. His statement: (and the commentator corrected it) I say: al-Shurunbulali transmitted his correction from al-Burhan and he proceeded upon it in his matn Nur al-Idah, and likewise the student of the author in his matn al-Tanwir. His statement: (and it may be said that if he returns etc.) al-Maqdisi also mentioned it and said after it: there is no error in their statement if they meant a restricted abandonment at that time, not abandonment entirely, so it is the meaning of delay, so ponder. And its summary is to show the difference between returning to sitting in our issue and returning to standing in the case analogized to, by saying that his return to standing is a return from fard to fard, unlike his return to sitting. But it is answered that in the issue of qunut, he did not return to fard because his bowing was not invalidated, so his subsequent standing is not the standing of fard but rather the standing for rising from bowing, which is sunnah or wajib. So his recitation of qunut was a delay of fard, not abandonment, so it is analogous to his return to sitting. His statement: (and qunut has a resemblance to Quran etc.)
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the ruling on someone who forgets the first sitting (tashahhud) in prayer and stands up for the next rak'ah. The core rule is: if the person is closer to sitting (i.e., has not fully stood up), he should return to the sitting; if he is closer to standing (i.e., has fully straightened), he should not return, and he performs sujud al-sahw at the end. The passage is a ruling with proof, expanding on the matn. The author explains that the principle of proximity applies: what is close to a thing takes its ruling. The detail of what constitutes proximity is attributed to Abu Yusuf and is adopted by the scholars of Bukhara. The text also narrates two hadiths about the Prophet's actions: once he returned after having partially stood, and another time he did not return after fully standing. The commentary then discusses the consequences if one returns in a situation where returning is prohibited: some say the prayer is corrupted, but a counter-argument compares it to cases of forgetting the Surah or qunut, where returning does not invalidate the prayer. The overall purpose is to clarify the correct fiqhi position and reconcile differing narrations.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The first sitting after the second rak'ah in a four-rak'ah prayer, where the tashahhud is recited.
فرض (fard): An obligatory element of prayer that cannot be omitted; omitting it invalidates the prayer.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory element that is not as strong as fard; omitting it requires compensation (sujud al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
ساهياً (sahyan): In a state of forgetfulness; doing something unintentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, if a person forgets the first tashahhud and stands up, when should he return to sitting?
A) Whenever he remembers, regardless of his position.
B) Only if he has not fully straightened his legs and is closer to sitting.
C) Only if he has not yet started the recitation of the third rak'ah.
D) He should never return; he should just perform sujud al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Proximity to sitting, not the start of the next rukn, determines whether to return to the forgotten first tashahhud.

Salah — Prayer

Forgetting the First Sitting: Proximity, Return, and Invalidation
Expands the ruling on forgetting the first sitting with proximity criterion and invalidation debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion of proximity to determine whether a forgetful person should return to the first sitting, and state the relied-upon view that returning after full standing does not invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Closer to sitting: return; closer to standing: don't return — and even if you wrongly return, the prayer remains valid.

Forgetting the first sitting (al-qu'ud al-awwal) is a common mistake in prayer. The Hanafi school provides a detailed criterion to decide whether one should return to the sitting or continue standing. This lesson unpacks the rule based on proximity, the evidence from the Prophet's practice, and the intra-madhhab disagreement on the validity of returning after fully standing. Understanding this will help you correctly handle forgetfulness in prayer without invalidating it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the forgetful act and the default ruling
The act is forgetting the first sitting (wajib). The default ruling: if the person is closer to sitting, he must return; if closer to standing, he must not return. In both cases, sujud al-sahw is wajib.
Sujud al-sahw compensates for the omission of a wajib.
2
Apply the proximity criterion (qurb)
Proximity is assessed by body position: knees on ground but buttocks raised means closer to sitting; hips fully erect means closer to standing. This is the view of Abu Yusuf, relied upon by later scholars.
The principle: 'what is close to a thing takes its ruling' (e.g., courtyard of a city).
3
Locate the dalil from Sunnah
Two narrations from the Prophet: (1) He returned when not fully standing. (2) He did not return after fully standing. The proximity criterion reconciles them.
Hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut, but accepted for establishing wajib.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on returning after full standing
Zahir al-Riwayah says it invalidates the prayer. Later scholars (e.g., in al-Mujtaba) say it does not invalidate; it only delays the wajib and requires sujud al-sahw.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sides with no invalidation, citing analogy to returning from ruku' for a surah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position: use Abu Yusuf's proximity criterion. If one returns after full standing mistakenly, the prayer is valid but sujud al-sahw is wajib.
This is the view of the mutakhkhirin (later scholars) and chosen by the author.

فلما قام عاد إليها وذكر أنه الفساد ثم
By his forgetfulness: If he forgets the first sitting and is closer to it, he returns; otherwise not, and he performs prostration of forgetfulness even if he forgot unintentionally. If [the forgetfulness occurs] before the imam or with him, there is no prostration; if after him, he must prostrate as we mentioned. In al-Muhit and others: It is recommended for the one who missed part [masbuq] to wait a while after the imam finishes then stand, because it is possible the imam has forgetfulness. Regarding his statement: (If he forgets the first sitting and is closer to it, he returns; otherwise not) meaning to the sitting, because the principle is that what is close to a thing takes its ruling, like the courtyard of a city and the precincts of a well. If he is closer to the sitting, by raising his buttocks from the ground while his knees are on it, or before the lower half is erect—and al-Kafi corrected it as if he had not stood at all—then if he is closer to standing, it is as if he has stood, and standing is a fard he has begun, so it is not permissible to abandon it for the sake of a wajib, which is the sitting. This detail is narrated from Abu Yusuf, chosen by the scholars of Bukhara, and approved by the authors of the matn. In al-Kafi: Our mashayikh considered his narration good. In al-Mabsut, it is mentioned that according to Zahir al-Riwayah, if he has not fully stood, he returns; if he has fully stood, he does not return, because the hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) came that he stood from the second to the third without sitting, so they said 'subhanallah' and he sat down; also it is narrated that he did not return after fully standing. This is because when he fully stood, he engaged in the fard of standing, so he does not leave it. The commentator affirmed this. In Fath al-Qadir, it is the apparent madhhab. Reconciling the two narrated actions by considering the two states of closeness to standing or not is not more preferable than reconciling them by considering equality or difference. Then, if he returns when he should not, they differed regarding the invalidity of his prayer. The commentator affirmed invalidity due to complete disengagement (junabah) by abandoning a fard after starting it for the sake of something not fard. In al-Mubtagha (with ghain): It is a mistake because it is not abandonment but rather delay, like if one forgets the surah and bows, he abandons the bowing and returns to standing to recite for the sake of the wajib; likewise if one forgets the qunut and bows, if he returns and recites qunut, it is not invalid according to the most correct view. It may be said: If he returns and recites the surah, the surah becomes fard, so he has returned from fard to fard; as for qunut, it has a resemblance to the Quran, as it was said it was Quran then abrogated, so he returned to something resembling the Quran, or he returned to a fard, which is standing, because every integral length (rukn tawluh) becomes entirely fard. In Fath al-Qadir: There is something in the correction, because the utmost in returning to the first sitting is that it adds some standing in the prayer, and although it is not permissible, it does not harm validity, as it is known that a less-than-a-rak'ah addition does not invalidate unless this addition is accompanied by abandonment (rafd). But it may be said: Sin becomes necessary due to the abandonment, but invalidity's necessary connection is not apparent, so this research supports the opposite of what the commentator corrected. It seems he was unaware of another correction. In al-Mujtaba and Mi'raj al-Diraya: If he returns after fully standing mistakenly, it is said he recites tashahhud because he broke his standing; the correct view is that he does not recite tashahhud and stands up, and his standing is not broken by a sitting he was not commanded to do, like one who breaks his bowing to recite another surah does not break his bowing. So correction is achieved, as you see, and the truth is no invalidity. Nor is prostration of recitation necessary, because he leaves a fard for it and it is wajib, since that is established by text contrary to analogy. By 'first sitting' is meant the sitting in obligatory prayer, whether four-rak'ah or three-rak'ah, and similarly in witr as in al-Muhit. As for nafl, if he stands to the third without sitting, he returns even if fully standing, unless he has tied it with a prostration. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and a difference is reported. In al-Muhit, it is said he does not return because it has become like fard; it is said he returns as long as he has not tied it with prostration because each two rak'ahs is a separate prayer regarding recitation, so we order him to return to the sitting as a precaution. When he returns, it becomes clear that the sitting occurred as fard, so abandoning a fard for a fard is permissible. All this applies to the imam and the one praying alone. As for the follower (ma'mum) if he stands forgetfully, he returns and sits because the sitting is fard upon him due to following, as indicated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If the imam does the tashahhud of the first sitting [and then stands] to the third, and some behind him forget the tashahhud until they all stand, then those who did not do tashahhud must return and do tashahhud then follow their imam even if they fear missing the third rak'ah, because they follow their imam and it is obligatory upon them. Then he stood for tashahhud? Actually the text ends abruptly.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the ruling of one who forgets the first sitting in prayer. The author clarifies the conditions for returning and the consequences. He begins by stating the core ruling from the matn: if the forgetful person is closer to the sitting position (i.e., has not yet fully stood up), he should return and sit; otherwise, he should not return and should perform sujud al-sahw at the end. This is based on the principle that something close to an object takes its ruling, like the precincts of a well. The detail of proximity (whether one is closer to sitting or standing) is attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf and chosen by the scholars of Bukhara and the authors of the matn. The Zahir al-Riwayah from al-Mabsut states simply: if not fully standing, return; if fully standing, do not return—supported by the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who both returned and did not return in different narrations. The author then discusses the disagreement if one returns after fully standing. Some say it invalidates the prayer because one abandons a fard for a wajib. But the author sides with those who say it does not invalidate; it is merely a delay, similar to returning from ruku' to recite a surah or qunut. He cites al-Mujtaba and other works that state the correct view is no invalidation, and the person should simply perform sujud al-sahw. The passage also covers the masbuq (latecomer) who should wait after the imam finishes in case the imam has sahw. For nafl prayer, the rule is more lenient: one returns even if fully standing, as long as the nafl is not tied to a prostration. For the ma'mum (follower), he must return and sit because the sitting is obligatory due to following the imam. Throughout, the commentary emphasizes the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position: the detailed criterion of Abu Yusuf is preferred, and returning after full standing does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The first sitting in prayer after the second rak'ah (in a four-rak'ah prayer) or after the second rak'ah in a three-rak'ah prayer; a wajib act.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness, such as omitting a wajib or delaying an act.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-established narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa through his students (especially Imam Muhammad) that form the basis of the madhhab.
القرب (al-qurb): Proximity; the principle that a thing close to another takes its ruling. Used here to determine the criterion for returning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if someone forgets the first sitting and has raised his buttocks from the ground but his knees are still on the ground, what should he do?
A) Continue standing and perform sujud al-sahw at the end.
B) Return to the sitting position and then continue.
C) Abort the prayer and start over.
D) Sit down immediately without returning to the first sitting.

Key Takeaway
Forgetting the first sitting triggers a proximity-based decision: return if closer to sitting, don't return if closer to standing; sujud al-sahw is wajib, and the prayer remains valid even if one wrongly returns.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Returning to the First Tashahhud After Standing: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Ruling
Hanafi fiqh passage on forgetting the first tashahhud and returning to it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on returning to the first tashahhud after standing and distinguish between the positions of the imam/munfarid and the ma'mum.

Core Idea
Returning to the first tashahhud after standing does not invalidate the prayer, but sajdah al-sahw may be required.

The first tashahhud is a wajib (obligatory) element in Hanafi prayer, but its omission or delayed performance due to forgetfulness raises complex questions. This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether returning to the first tashahhud after having stood for the next rak'ah invalidates the prayer. Based on al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we will trace the arguments, identify the relied-upon position, and learn the practical rulings for different situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Act and Dispute
The act: a person forgets the first tashahhud, stands for the next rak'ah, then remembers and returns to the sitting. The dispute: does this return invalidate the prayer (batil) or is it valid with a compensation (sajdah al-sahw)?
The first tashahhud is wajib; forgetting it triggers the need to either return or continue with sajdah.
2
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Positions
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., the 'musahhih' in Fath al-Qadir) argued that returning invalidates because it involves abandoning standing for a non-obligatory act. Others (the author's preferred view) hold it does not invalidate because the addition is less than a rak'ah and the sitting is also wajib.
The key illa (effective cause) is whether the standing addition is significant enough to break the prayer's sequence.
3
Determine the Rule for Imam/Munfarid Based on Proximity
If the person is closer to sitting (e.g., knees still on ground, not fully upright), they must return to the tashahhud and no sajdah is required. If they are closer to standing (fully upright), they should continue and perform sajdah al-sahw for delaying the wajib.
The criterion is whether the law considers the partial standing as a real standing or a transition.
4
Distinguish the Ma'mum (Follower) Case
For the follower, the first tashahhud is obligatory (fard) by virtue of following the imam. If the follower forgets and stands, they must return to sit even if it means missing part of the rak'ah, because following the imam is mandatory. Failure to return invalidates the follower's prayer.
This differs from the individual, for whom the first tashahhud is only sunnah.

الصلاة وكذلك الجواب في الصحيح إذا قام قبل أن يتشهد ا هـ . قوله : (ويسجد للسهو خاص بقوله وإلا لا كما صححه المصنف في الكافي تبعاً لصاحب الهداية لترك الواجب. وأما إذا كان إلى القعود أقرب وعاد فلا سجود على ركبتيه لينهض يقعد وعليه السهو ويستوي فيه القعدة الأولى والثانية وعليه الاعتماد، وإن رفع أليتيه عن الأرض وركبتاه على الأرض ولم يرفعهما لا عليه. كذا سهو روي عن أبي يوسف وفي الأجناس عليه السهو ويستوي في ذلك القعدة الأولى والأخيرة اهـ. فالحاصل على هذا المعتمد أنه إن كان إلى القعود أقرب فإنه يعود مطلقاً، وإن رفع ركبتيه من الأرض لزمه السجود وإلا فلا وهو مخالف للتصحيح السابق في بعضه. وفي الولوالجية : Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. They differed regarding returning to the first sitting after standing. In Fath al-Qadir: 'There is something in the soul regarding the correction. That is, the utmost in returning to the first sitting is an addition of some standing in the prayer, and although it is not permissible, it does not harm validity because it is known that an addition of less than a rak'ah does not invalidate unless this addition is coupled with abandonment. But it may be said: the person deserves sin also for abandonment, but as for invalidation, its necessary consequence is not apparent. So by this research, the opposing view to the corrector is preponderant.' So apparently he did not come across another correction. And it is mentioned in al-Mujtaba and Miraj al-Diraya that if he returns after standing upright mistakenly, it is said he recites tashahhud because he broke his standing, but the correct view is that he does not recite tashahhud and stands, and his standing is not broken by an unintentional sitting, like one who breaks his bowing with another surah; his bowing is not broken. So the correction is as you see, and the truth is no invalidation, and sajdah al-tilawah is not required because he abandons the obligatory for it; it is wajib because that is established by text contrary to analogy. By 'first sitting' he meant the sitting in obligatory prayer, whether four-rak'ah or three-rak'ah, and similarly in witr prayer as in al-Muhit. As for supererogatory prayer, if he stands for the third without sitting, he returns even if he completes standing as long as he does not tie it with a prostration. This is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. It relates a difference of opinion: in al-Muhit it is said he does not return because it becomes like obligatory; and it is said he returns as long as he does not tie it with a prostration because each pair is a separate prayer with respect to recitation, so we order him to return to sitting out of caution, and if he returns, it becomes clear that the sitting occurred as obligatory, so abandoning the obligatory for the sake of the obligatory is permissible. All this applies to the imam and the individual. As for the follower, if he stands forgetfully, he returns and sits because sitting is obligatory for him by virtue of following. This is indicated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, where it says: 'If the imam recites tashahhud in the first sitting and then stands for the third, and some of those behind him forget tashahhud until they all stand, then whoever did not recite tashahhud must return and recite tashahhud then follow his imam, even if he fears missing the third rak'ah, because he follows his imam and that is required of him.' This is different from the individual because the first tashahhud is sunnah for him, and after engaging in the obligatory standing, he does not return to a sunnah. Here, tashahhud is obligatory for him by virtue of following. Similarly in al-Qunyah: it is more appropriate to sit, and apparently if he does not return, his prayer becomes invalid due to leaving an obligatory act. In al-Majma': if a latecomer slept and his imam forgot the first sitting, and he woke up after the imam finished, we order him to leave the sitting. At the end of Fatawa al-Walwalji from miscellaneous issues: a sick person praying by gesture, when he reached the state of tashahhud, he thought it was the state of standing, so he engaged in recitation, then remembered it was the state of tashahhud. If it is the first tashahhud, the state of recitation substitutes for standing, so he does not return to tashahhud and completes his prayer. If it is the second tashahhud, he returns to tashahhud and completes his prayer. Similarly the answer for a healthy person if he stood before tashahhud. His statement: 'And he prostrates for forgetfulness specifically with his statement, otherwise not, as the author corrected in al-Kafi following the author of al-Hidayah, due to leaving an obligatory act. As for when he is closer to sitting and returns, there is no sajdah upon him, just as if he did not stand, because the Law did not consider it standing; otherwise he would not be permitted to sit, so it is considered sitting or transition out of necessity, and this consideration is inconsistent with considering it a delay that necessitates sajdah.' In al-Khulasah: 'In one narration, if he stands on his knees to rise, he sits and forgetfulness (sahw) is upon him, and it is the same for the first and second sittings, and upon this is reliance. If he lifts his buttocks from the ground while his knees are on the ground and he does not lift them, nothing is upon him.' Similarly, forgetfulness is reported from Abu Yusuf, and in al-Ajnas: forgetfulness is upon him, and it is the same for the first and last sitting. So the conclusion on this relied-upon view is that if he is closer to sitting, he returns unconditionally. If he lifted his knees from the ground, sajdah is required, otherwise not. This contradicts the previous correction in some respects. In al-Walwaljiyah: he should not sit but stand immediately. Also in it: if the imam returned to the first sitting after standing, they do not return with him to realize the violation, but some mentioned that they return with him. This, as stated in Sharh al-Munyah, indicates no invalidation by returning. His statement: 'Apparently if he does not return, his prayer becomes invalid.' He said in al-Nahr: 'There is something in it not hidden.' And what should be said is that it is obligatory in the obligatory, an obligatory act in the obligatory. His statement: 'in the healthy' means the healthy person, not the sick. His statement: 'or a transition' means a transition from sitting; in any case it is not standing. His statement: 'If he lifts his buttocks from the ground, etc.' It is not hidden that this scenario is the previous scenario, so the conclusion in that scenario is a difference of narration. In al-Ajnas he chose in this scenario that forgetfulness is upon him, unless it is interpreted as when his knees leave the ground without his lower half straightening like one sitting for relieving oneself. His statement: 'The conclusion on this' means on what is in al-Khulasah. And his statement: 'It contradicts the previous correction in some respects' means the correction presented from al-Kafi and al-Hidayah, because its apparent meaning is that whenever he is closer to sitting and returns, there is no sajdah upon him, whether he lifted his knees from the ground or not. So what is in al-Khulasah agrees with it when he did not lift his knees.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the Hanafi ruling on a person who forgets the first tashahhud and stands up for the next rak'ah, then remembers and returns to the sitting. The author investigates whether this return invalidates the prayer or not, and when sajdah al-sahw is required.

The passage begins with a dispute (ikhtilaf) on the issue. The author quotes from Fath al-Qadir that some scholars corrected (sahhaha) that the prayer is invalid if one returns after standing, but the author leans toward the view that it does not invalidate. The reasoning is that an addition of less than a rak'ah generally does not invalidate unless coupled with abandonment of an obligatory act. The author affirms that the correct view is no invalidation, but the person is sinful for abandoning the obligatory (the first tashahhud is wajib in the Hanafi school). 

Key distinctions are made:
1. For the imam (leader) and munfarid (individual): If one stands and then remembers before moving fully to standing (i.e., is closer to sitting), it is obligatory to return to the tashahhud, and no sajdah al-sahw is required. If one has fully stood (closer to standing), one should not return but continue; sajdah al-sahw is required due to delaying the wajib.
2. For the ma'mum (follower): The first tashahhud becomes obligatory by virtue of following the imam. If the ma'mum forgets and stands, he must return to sitting even if it means missing part of the rak'ah, because his sitting is obligatory. This is different from the individual, for whom the first tashahhud is only sunnah.

The passage also discusses the case of a sick person praying by gesture and similar scenarios. The relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that if one lifts the knees from the ground while standing, sajdah al-sahw is required; otherwise not. There is some variation among Hanafi sources on this detail, with some saying sajdah is required in both cases when returning after standing.

The overall conclusion: returning to the first tashahhud after standing does not invalidate the prayer, but one must perform sajdah al-sahw if one had fully stood before returning. The prayer is valid even if one returns; the sin for abandoning the wajib is forgiven by the sajdah.

Key Terms
القعدة الأولى (al-qa'dah al-ūlā): The first sitting in prayer after the second rak'ah (in four-rak'ah prayers) or after the first two rak'ahs in three-rak'ah prayers, where the tashahhud is recited. It is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of the prayer to compensate for forgetfulness, such as adding, omitting, or delaying an obligatory act.
المتابعة (al-mutāba'ah): The obligation of the follower (ma'mum) to follow the imam in actions, including sitting for tashahhud. If the follower forgets and stands, he must return to sit because his sitting is obligatory by virtue of following.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the passage, when does returning to the first tashahhud after standing require sajdah al-sahw?
A) Always, whenever one returns after standing.
B) Only if one has lifted his knees from the ground (fully committed to standing).
C) Only if one is closer to sitting when returning.
D) Never; no sajdah is ever required if one returns.

Key Takeaway
Returning to the first tashahhud after standing does not invalidate the prayer; the key variable is proximity to sitting (determined by knee lifting) which determines whether sajdah al-sahw is required.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
Forgetting the First Tashahhud: Return, Sajda, and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Posture
Rulings on forgetting the first tashahhud and the intra-Hanafi dispute on posture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a worshipper who forgets the first tashahhud, identify the varying opinions on when sajda al-sahw is required based on posture (knees vs. buttocks), and apply the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.

Core Idea
Closer to sitting? Return without sajda. Closer to standing? Continue with sajda. But Hanafis dispute: do lifted knees count as standing?

When a worshipper stands up forgetting the first tashahhud, the Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling: if he is closer to sitting, he returns and no sajda is needed; if closer to standing, he continues and performs sajda al-sahw. However, the definition of 'closer to standing' is debated: does lifting the knees off the ground constitute standing? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute from al-Kafi, al-Hidayah, al-Khulasah, and al-Ajnas, and presents the mu'tamad (relied-upon) position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the missed element
The first tashahhud is wajib (not fard) in the Hanafi school. Forgetting it triggers either a return or a compensatory sajda.
Distinguish: for a munfarid (alone) it's sunnah; for an imam or follower it's wajib. The text focuses on the imam/follower case.
2
Determine posture at remembrance
At the moment he remembers, is he physically closer to sitting (qarib ila al-qu'ud) or closer to standing (qarib ila al-qiyam)? This is assessed by his body position.
The text discusses two postures: knees still on ground (closer to sitting) vs. knees raised (closer to standing).
3
Apply the basic rule
If closer to sitting: he should sit back, recite the tashahhud, and continue. No sajda required. If closer to standing: he should not sit; he continues the prayer and at the end performs sajda al-sahw for delaying the wajib.
This rule is agreed upon; the dispute is about the threshold for 'closer to standing'.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
According to al-Kafi and al-Hidayah: if closer to sitting, return no sajda regardless of knee lifting. According to a narration in al-Khulasah and from Abu Yusuf: if he raises his knees (even if still closer to sitting), sajda becomes wajib. According to al-Ajnas: sajda is required in both cases.
The dispute centers on whether a partial rise (knees off ground) constitutes a significant delay.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) as stated in al-Khulasah is: if the worshipper is closer to sitting, he returns absolutely; but if he raised his knees from the ground, he must perform sajda al-sahw. If he only raised his buttocks while knees on ground, no sajda.
This view is adopted by later authorities and is the operative ruling for fatwa.

أن يتشهد بطريق المتابعة. وهذا بخلاف المنفرد لأن التشهد الأول في حقه سنة، وبعد ما اشتغل بفرض القيام لا يعود إلى السنة وههنا التشهد فرض عليه بحكم المتابعة ا هـ . وكذا في القنية : ففي القعود أولى وظاهره أنه لو لم يعد تبطل صلاته لترك الفرض. وفي المجمع : ولو نام لاحق سها إمامه عن القعدة الأولى فاستيقظ بعد الفراغ أمرناه بترك القعدة ا هـ . وفي آخر فتاوى الولوالجي من مسائل متفرقة : مريض يصلي بالإيماء فلما بلغ حالة التشهد فظن أنه حالة القيام فاشتغل بالقراءة ثم تذكر أنه حالة التشهد فلا يخلو إما إن كان التشهد الأول أو التشهد الثاني، فإن كان التشهد الأول فحالة القراءة تنوب عن القيام فلا يعود إلى التشهد ويتم الصلاة، وإن كان التشهد الثاني رجع إلى التشهد ويتم الصلاة وكذلك الجواب في الصحيح إذا قام قبل أن يتشهد ا هـ .

قوله : (ويسجد للسهو خاص بقوله وإلا لا كما صححه المصنف في الكافي تبعاً لصاحب الهداية لترك الواجب. وأما إذا كان إلى القعود أقرب وعاد فلا سجود عليه كما إذا لم يقم لأن الشرع لم يعتبره قياماً وإلا لم يطلق له القعود فكان معتبراً قعوداً أو انتقالاً للضرورة، وهذا الاعتبار ينافيه اعتبار التأخير المستتبع لوجوب السجود. وفي الخلاصة: وفي رواية إذا قام على ركبتيه لينهض يقعد وعليه السهو ويستوي فيه القعدة الأولى والثانية وعليه الاعتماد، وإن رفع أليتيه عن الأرض وركبتاه على الأرض ولم يرفعهما لا عليه. كذا سهو روي عن أبي يوسف وفي الأجناس عليه السهو ويستوي في ذلك القعدة الأولى والأخيرة اهـ. فالحاصل على هذا المعتمد أنه إن كان إلى القعود أقرب فإنه يعود مطلقاً، فإنه رفع ركبتيه من الأرض لزمه السجود وإلا فلا وهو مخالف للتصحيح السابق في بعضه. وفي الولوالجية : لم يكن له القعود يقوم في الحال. وفيها أيضاً : ولو عاد الإمام يعني ! القعدة الأولى بعد ما قام لا القوم تحقيقاً للمخالفة وذكر البعض أنهم يعودون معه ا هـ . وهذا كما قال في شرح المنية يفيد عدم الفساد بالعود قوله : وظاهره أنه لو لم يعد تبطل صلاته قال في النهر : وفيه مالا يخفى، والذي ينبغي أن يقال إنها واجبة في الواجب فرض في الفرض قوله : (في الصحيح) أي في المصلي الصحيح غير المريض قوله : (أو انتقالاً) أي انتقالاً عن القعود وعلى كل فليس بقيام قوله : (وإن رفع اليتيه عن الأرض الخ لا يخفى أن هذه الصورة هي الصورة التي قبلها فيكون الحاصل في تلك الصورة اختلاف الرواية، وقد اختار في الأجناس في هذه الصورة أن عليه السهو اللهم إلا أن يحمل الأول على ما إذا فارقت ركبتاه الأرض دون أن يستوي نصفه الأسفل شبه الجالس لقضاء الحاجة قوله : (فالحاصل على هذا) أي على ما في الخلاصة. وقوله وهو مخالف للتصحيح السابق في بعضه أي للتصحيح الذي قدمه عن الكافي والهداية فإن ظاهره أنه متى كان إلى القعود أقرب وعاد لا سجود عليه، سواء رفع ركبتيه من الأرض أو لا، فيوافقه ما في الخلاصة فيما إذا لم يرفع ركبتيه
That he performs tashahhud by way of following (the imam). This is contrary to the individual (alone) because the first tashahhud is sunnah for him, and after he has occupied himself with the obligatory standing he does not return to the sunnah, whereas here the tashahhud is obligatory for him by the ruling of following. End. Similarly in al-Qunyah: The sitting is preferable, and its apparent meaning is that if he does not return, his prayer is invalidated due to leaving an obligation. In al-Majma': If a latecomer sleeps, his imam forgets the first sitting, then he wakes up after (the imam has) finished, we order him to leave the sitting. End. And at the end of Fatawa al-Walwaliji from miscellaneous issues: A sick person praying by gestures, when he reaches the state of tashahhud, he thought it was the state of standing, so he occupied himself with recitation, then he remembered it was the state of tashahhud. Then it is not free from: either it was the first tashahhud or the second tashahhud. If it was the first tashahhud, then the state of recitation substitutes for standing, so he does not return to tashahhud and completes the prayer. If it was the second tashahhud, he returns to tashahhud and completes the prayer. Likewise the answer for the healthy person if he stood before tashahhud. End.

His statement: (And he prostrates for forgetfulness specifically with his statement, otherwise no) as the author corrected in al-Kafi following the author of al-Hidayah for leaving a wajib. As for when he is closer to sitting and returns, there is no prostration upon him, as if he had not stood, because the Law did not consider it standing; otherwise it would not be called sitting for him. So it is considered sitting, or a transition due to necessity. This consideration conflicts with the consideration of delay necessitating the obligation of prostration. In al-Khulasah: In one narration, if he stood on his knees to rise, he sits and is subject to forgetfulness (sajdah), and the first and second sittings are equal, and this is relied upon. If he raised his buttocks from the ground while his knees remained on the ground and did not raise them, he is not subject (to sajdah). Similarly, it is reported from Abu Yusuf, and in al-Ajnas he is subject to sajdah, and the first and last sittings are equal. End. So the conclusion based on what is relied upon is that if he is closer to sitting, he returns absolutely. If he raised his knees from the ground, he must perform sajdah; otherwise no. This contradicts the previous correction in some parts. In al-Walwaljiyah: He must not sit; he stands immediately. In it also: If the imam returned to the first sitting after standing, he (the follower) does not stand to actualize contradiction, and some mentioned that they return with him. End. This, as stated in Sharh al-Munyah, indicates the absence of invalidation by returning. His statement: Its apparent meaning is that if he does not return, his prayer is invalid. In al-Nahr: In it there is something not hidden. The appropriate thing to say is that it is obligatory in the obligatory, fard in fard. His statement: (in the healthy) meaning in the healthy praying person, not the sick. His statement: (or transition) meaning transition from sitting, and in any case it is not standing. His statement: (And if he raised his buttocks from the ground, etc.) It is not hidden that this image is the same as the previous one, so the result in that image is a difference of narration. He chose in al-Ajnas in this image that he is subject to sajdah, unless it is interpreted that the first (case) is when his knees left the ground without his lower half becoming upright like one sitting to relieve himself. His statement: (The conclusion on this) meaning based on what is in al-Khulasah. And his statement: And it contradicts the previous correction in some parts, meaning the correction he presented from al-Kafi and al-Hidayah, for its apparent meaning is that whenever he is closer to sitting and returns, there is no sajdah upon him, whether he raised his knees from the ground or not. So it agrees with what is in al-Khulasah when he does not raise his knees.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage begins by discussing a latecomer (lahiq) whose imam forgets the first sitting. The lahiq, following the imam, must disregard the missed sitting because his obligation is to follow. It then addresses a sick person praying with gestures: if he confuses tashahhud for standing and recites, if it is the first tashahhud he does not return (recitation substitutes for standing), but if it is the final tashahhud he must return. The main ruling: when one stands up forgetting the first tashahhud, he must return if he is closer to sitting (qarib ila al-qu'ud), and no sajda al-sahw is required. If he is closer to standing, he completes the standing and must perform sajda al-sahw. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to a narration in al-Khulasah, if he raises his knees from the ground and sits, sajda is required; but if he only raises his buttocks with knees on ground, no sajda. Another view from al-Ajnas says sajda is required in both cases. The relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that if he is closer to sitting, he returns absolutely; if he lifts his knees, sajda is obligatory; otherwise not. This differs from the earlier correction in al-Kafi and al-Hidayah which said no sajda as long as he is closer to sitting, regardless of lifting. The passage also notes that the imam may return if he stands, and the followers should return with him, and doing so does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
التشهد الأول (al-tashahhud al-awwal): The first testimony recited in the second rak'ah of a prayer of three or four rak'ahs, which is wajib according to Hanafis.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for an omission or delay of a wajib or fard element.
المتابعة (al-mutaba'ah): Following the imam in prayer; for a latecomer, the obligation to follow the imam's actions even if it means skipping his own first tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mu'tamad (relied-upon) position in this passage, what is the ruling for a worshipper who forgets the first tashahhud and stands up, realizing his error when he is closer to sitting (qarib ila al-qu'ud) and his knees are still on the ground, but his buttocks are slightly raised?
A) He must perform sajda al-sahw regardless.
B) He should sit back and recite the first tashahhud; no sajda is required.
C) He should not sit back; he continues and performs sajda al-sahw at the end.
D) His prayer is invalid because he partially stood.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances the obligation of the first tashahhud with the continuity of prayer: returning is allowed only when it does not constitute a significant delay (i.e., closer to sitting), and sajda al-sahw compensates for the delay in all other cases; the mu'tamad defines 'closer to standing' by whether the knees have left the ground.
