Forgetting the Final Tashahhud: Return and Consequences
Ruling with proof for forgetting final tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for forgetting the final tashahhud and explain the consequences of returning before prostration versus after prostration.

Core Idea
Forgetting final tashahhud: return before prostration, but after prostration the fard becomes nafl.

In this passage, the author from al-Bahr al-Rai'q explains the ruling when a worshipper forgets the final tashahhud and either returns to sit or prostrates. The key distinction is whether the prostration of that rak'ah has occurred. Understanding this will help you know how to correct such a mistake in salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is forgetting the final tashahhud (qa'dah akhirah) in salah. The ruling is that one must return to the sitting if he has not yet prostrated, and then perform sajda al-sahw.
2
Determine the condition for return
The condition is that he has not prostrated (sajdah) of that rak'ah. If he has not placed his forehead on the ground for prostration, he can still return and correct his prayer.
The text specifies 'ma lam yasjud' (as long as he has not prostrated).
3
Understand the consequence of prostrating
If he has already prostrated, he cannot return. His fard prayer is invalidated (batala farduhu) and the prayer becomes nafl (voluntary). He continues the prayer as nafl and does not start over.
This is the chosen view (al-mukhtar) and the majority opinion.
4
Note the rationale
The final tashahhud is fard (obligatory). By standing and prostrating, he has completed the rak'ah but delayed a fard. If he returns before prostration, he can fix it with sajda al-sahw. After prostration, the rak'ah is complete but the omission of the fard cannot be fixed without breaking the sequence, so the prayer becomes nafl.
The text explains that by prostrating, his commencement in nafl is confirmed before completing the pillars of the fard, so he exits the fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن سها عن الأخير عاد ما لم يسجد وسجد للسهو فإن سجد بطل فرضه برفعه وصارت نفلاً عن المختار وجوب السجود لأنه بقدر ما اشتغل بالقيام صار مؤخراً واجباً وجب وصله بما قبله من الركن فصار تاركاً للواجب فيجب عليه سجدتا السهو ا.هـ. فاختلف الترجيح على أقوال ثلاثة والأكثر على الأول قوله : ( وإن سها عن الأخير عاد ما لم يسجد) لأن فيه إصلاح صلاته فأمكنه ذلك لأن ما دون الركعة بمحل الرفض. أراد بالأخير القعود المفروض ليشمل الفرض الرباعي والثلاثي والثنائي فإن قعوده ليس متعدداً إلا أن يقال إنه يسمى أخيراً باعتبار أنه آخر الصلاة لا باعتبار أنه مسبوق بمثله. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا لم يقعد أصلاً أو جلس جلسة خفيفة أقل من قدر التشهد وإذا عاد احتسب له الجلسة الخفيفية حتى لو كان كلا الجلستين مقدار التشهد ثم تكلم بعده جازت صلاته كما قدمناه في باب صفة الصلاة عن الولوالجية قوله : (وسجد للسهو) لتأخيره فرضاً وهو القعود الأخير. وعلله في الهداية بأنه أخر واجباً فقالوا : أراد به الواجب القطعي وهو الفرض وهو أولى مما في العناية من تفسير بإصابة لفظ السلام لأنه لم يؤخره عن محله لأن محله بعد القعود ولم يقعد وإنما أخر القعود والأولى أن يقال: أراد به الواجب الذي يفوت الجواز بفوته إذ ليس دليلها قطعياً.
قوله (فإن سجد بطل فرضه برفعه لأن استحكم شروعه في النافلة قبل إكمال أركان المكتوبة ومن ضرورته خروجه عن الفرض وهذا لأن الركعة بسجدة واحدة صلاة حقيقة بحنث في يمينه لا يصلي. وقوله (برفعه أي برفع الوجه عن الأرض إشارة إلى أن السجدة الأخيرة التي أتى بها هي سجدة الركعة وليست سجدة السهو.
His statement: (And if he forgets the final [tashahhud], he returns as long as he has not prostrated, and he performs sajda al-sahw. For if he prostrates, his fard is invalidated by raising himself, and it becomes nafl.) According to the chosen view, the obligation of sajda is because to the extent he occupied himself with standing, he became a delayer of a wajib that must be joined to the previous pillar (i.e., the prostration of the rak'ah), so he became a leaver of a wajib, thus two sajdas of forgetfulness are obligatory. End. So the tarjih differs among three sayings, and the majority is on the first. His statement: (And if he forgets the final [tashahhud], he returns as long as he has not prostrated) because in it is the correction of his prayer, so he is able to do so because that which is less than a rak'ah is subject to rejection. By 'final' he means the obligatory sitting to include the four-rak'ah, three-rak'ah, and two-rak'ah prayers, for its sitting is not multiple unless it is said it is called 'final' because it is the end of the prayer, not because it is preceded by another like it. He made it absolute, so it includes the case where he did not sit at all or sat a light sitting less than the measure of tashahhud. And if he returns, the light sitting is counted for him, such that even if both sittings were the measure of tashahhud, then he spoke after it, his prayer is valid, as we presented in the chapter on the description of prayer from al-Walwaljiyah. His statement: (And he performs sajda al-sahw) due to his delaying a fard, namely the final sitting. Al-Hidayah explained it as delaying a wajib. They said: He intended the definitive wajib, which is fard. This is more appropriate than what is in al-'Inayah of interpreting it as hitting the wording of taslim, because he did not delay it from its place, since its place is after sitting, and he did not sit. He only delayed the sitting. The more appropriate is to say: He intended the wajib whose omission invalidates the permissibility (of prayer), since its evidence is not definitive.
His statement: (For if he prostrates, his fard is invalidated by raising himself because his commencement in nafl is confirmed before completing the pillars of the obligatory prayer, and from its necessity is his exit from fard. This is because a rak'ah with one prostration is a real prayer; she breaks her oath that she does not pray.) His statement: (by raising himself) meaning raising his face from the ground, indicating that the last prostration he performed is the prostration of the rak'ah, not the sajda al-sahw.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage rules on forgetting the final tashahhud (qa'dah akhirah). If a person forgets it and stands up, he must return to the sitting as long as he has not yet performed the prostration (sajdah) of that rak'ah. He then performs sajda al-sahw for delaying the final sitting. If he prostrates, he has effectively completed the rak'ah with its prostration, but since he left the obligatory final sitting, his intent to continue in the obligatory prayer is broken; the prayer becomes nafl (voluntary). The ruling applies whether he never sat at all or sat briefly. The reason given is that the sitting is fard (obligatory) and its delay requires compensation via sajda al-sahw. The al-Hidayah explains this as delaying a 'wajib', but the commentator clarifies that this wajib is definitive (qat'i) in the sense that its omission invalidates the prayer if not compensated. The text notes that the condition for returning is that he has not yet prostrated by putting his forehead on the ground; if he has done that prostration, the return is too late.

Key Terms
التشهد الأخير (al-tashahhud al-akhir): The final testimony in the last rak'ah of the prayer, which is fard according to Hanafis (obligatory, not just essential for validity).
صارت نفلاً (sarat naflan): It becomes a voluntary (nafl) prayer; the intention of fard is nullified and the prayer counts as nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone forgets the final tashahhud and returns to sit after having already performed the prostration of that rak'ah?
A) He should still return and perform sajda al-sahw; his prayer is valid.
B) He cannot return; his prayer becomes nafl.
C) He must repeat the entire prayer.
D) His prayer is invalid and he must repeat it.

Key Takeaway
If the final tashahhud is forgotten and one has already prostrated, the fard prayer is invalidated and continues as nafl; return is only possible before prostration.

Forgetting the Final Sitting and the Extra Rak'ah: When Does the Fard Become Nafl?
Commentary on ruling for forgetting final sitting and extra rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the moment the extra rak'ah becomes nafl, and identify the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi) along with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Extra rak'ah becomes nafl only upon raising the head from sajdah, not upon placing the forehead.

When a worshipper forgets the final sitting and stands for an extra rak'ah, a critical question arises: at what point does the extra rak'ah become a separate nafl? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this moment. This lesson unpacks the dispute between Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), traces the reasoning behind each view, and identifies the mufta bihi position. Understanding this distinction is essential for ruling on cases where the worshipper remembers or experiences hadath during the extra rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the Sahibayn's ruling
Recognize the scenario: a person forgets the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah), stands for an extra rak'ah, and prostrates. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if he prostrates and raises his head, the fard becomes invalid and the extra rak'ah becomes nafl.
The invalidation is linked to the completion of the sajdah by raising the head.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's differing view and its basis
Abu Yusuf holds that invalidation occurs only upon raising the head, not upon placing the forehead. His reasoning: the completion of a thing is by its last part, and the last part of sajdah is the raising. Placing the forehead alone does not complete the sajdah, so the extra rak'ah is not yet a separate prayer.
This principle is supported by the analogy of prostrating before the imam and catching up – validity depends on raising.
3
Apply the thamarah (practical consequence) to a hadath scenario
If the worshipper experiences hadath (e.g., wudu breaks) during the sajdah of the extra rak'ah: According to Abu Yusuf, the prayer is invalid and he does not return to the forgotten sitting. According to Muhammad, he returns, performs wudu, and completes his fard.
This practical difference stems from the disagreement on whether the extra rak'ah is already a nafl that cannot be undone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو
١٨١
الأخير عاد ما لم يسجد وسجد للسهو فإن سجد بطل فرضه برفعه وصارت نفلاً عن
المختار وجوب السجود لأنه بقدر ما اشتغل بالقيام صار مؤخراً واجباً وجب وصله بما قبله من الركن فصار تاركاً للواجب فيجب عليه سجدتا السهو ا.هـ. فاختلف الترجيح على أقوال ثلاثة والأكثر على الأول قوله : ( وإن سها عن الأخير عاد ما لم يسجد) لأن فيه إصلاح صلاته فأمكنه ذلك لأن ما دون الركعة بمحل الرفض. أراد بالأخير القعود المفروض ليشمل الفرض الرباعي والثلاثي والثنائي فإن قعوده ليس متعدداً إلا أن يقال إنه يسمى أخيراً باعتبار أنه آخر الصلاة لا باعتبار أنه مسبوق بمثله. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا لم يقعد أصلاً أو جلس جلسة خفيفة أقل من قدر التشهد وإذا عاد احتسب له الجلسة الخفيفية حتى لو كان كلا الجلستين مقدار التشهد ثم تكلم بعده جازت صلاته كما قدمناه في باب صفة الصلاة عن الولوالجية قوله : (وسجد للسهو) لتأخيره فرضاً وهو القعود الأخير. وعلله في الهداية بأنه أخر واجباً فقالوا : أراد به الواجب القطعي وهو الفرض وهو أولى مما في العناية من تفسير بإصابة لفظ السلام لأنه لم يؤخره عن محله لأن محله بعد القعود ولم يقعد وإنما أخر القعود والأولى أن يقال: أراد به الواجب الذي يفوت الجواز بفوته إذ ليس دليلها قطعياً.
قوله (فإن سجد بطل فرضه برفعه لأن استحكم شروعه في النافلة قبل إكمال أركان المكتوبة ومن ضرورته خروجه عن الفرض وهذا لأن الركعة بسجدة واحدة صلاة حقيقة بحنث في يمينه لا يصلي. وقوله (برفعه أي برفع الوجه عن الأرض إشارة إلى أن ويخالفه فيما إذا رفعهما . وقوله وفي الولوالجية «الخ ) جعله قولاً ثالثاً لأن ظاهر أنه متى كان إلى القعود أقرب يلزمه السجود، سواء رفع ركبتيه من الأرض أو لا . قول المصنف : (عاد ما لم يسجد) قال في النهر : أي ما لم يقيد ركعته بسجدة وهذ أراد لا ما إذا سجد دون ركوع فإنه يعود أيضاً لعدم الاعتداد بهذا السجود قوله : (التأخيره فرضاً قال في النهر : لم يفصل بين ما إذا كان إلى القعود أقرب أو لا، وكان ينبغي أن لا يسجد فيما إذا كان إليه أقرب كما في الأولى لما سبق قال في الحواشي السعدية : ويمكن أن يفرق بينهما بأن القريب من القعود وإن جاز أن يعطى له حكم القاعد إلا أنه ليس بقاعد حقيقة فاعتبر جانب الحقيقة فيما إذا سها عن الثانية وأعطى حكم القاعد في السهو عن الأولى إظهاراً للتفاوت بين الواجب والفرض وبه علم أن من فسر الواجب بالقطعي فقد أصاب وإلا أشكل الفرق وقد يقال لم لا يجوز أن يفسر بالقوي من نوعيه وهو ما يفوت الجواز بفوته ولا يشكل بثبوت التفاوت بين نوعيه، نعم يشكل على من فسره بإصابة لفظ السلام أو التشهد قوله : (وهو أولى مما في العناية) اعترضه الشيخ إسماعيل بأن الذي في العناية تفسيره بالقطعي فليس النقل بصواب، نعم فسر في العناية الواجب بذلك في ما إذا أقعد الأخير قوله : (لأنه لم يؤخره عن الخ) قال في النهر : مدفوع بأن التأخير واقع فيهما فصح إضافة السجود إلى أيهما كان. قال الشيخ إسماعيل : يمكن نسبته إلى الأقوى وهو الفرض هذا مع إرخاء العنان وقد علمت أنه حصل سهو في المسألة الثانية وهي محله
١٨٢
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو
المختار الفتوى أنه لا يبطل بوضع الجهة كما هو مروي عن أبي يوسف لأن تمام الشيء بآخره وآخر السجدة الرفع إذ الشيء إنما ينتهي بضده، ولهذا لو سجد قبل إمامه فأدركه إمامه فيه جاز ولو تمت بالوضع لما جاز لأن كل ركن أداه قبل إمامه لا يجوز ولأنه لو تم قبل الرفع لم ينقضه الحدث لكن الاتفاق على لزوم إعادة كل ركن وجد فيه سبق الحدث بقيد البناء. وثمرة الاختلاف فيما إذا أحدث في السجود فانصرف وتوضأ ثم تذكر أنه لم يقعد في الرابعة. قال أبو يوسف : لا يعود إلى القعود وبطل فرضه. وقال محمد يعود ويتم فرضه. قالوا: أخبر أبو يوسف بجواب محمد فقال : زه صلاة فسدت يصلحها الحدث وهذا معنى ما يسأله العامة أي صلاة يصلحها الحدث فهي هذه الصلاة على قول محمد وزه كلمة استعجاب وإنما قالها أبو . يوسف تهكماً. وقيل: الصواب بالضم والزاي ليست بخالصة. كذا في المغرب. وفي فتح القدير : وهذا أعني صحة البناء بسبب سبق الحدث إذا لم يتذكر في ذلك السجود سجدة صلبية من صلاته فإن تذكر ذلك فسدت اتفاقاً اهـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه بل لا التقييد لأنه إذا سبقه الحدث وهو ساجد لم يخلط النفل بالفرض قبل إكماله عند محمد، سواء تذكر أن عليه سجدة صلبية أو لا، إذ لا فرق بين أن يكون عليه ركن واحد أو ركنان . وعبارة الخلاصة أولى وهي : ولو قيد الخامسة بالسجدة فتذكر أنه ترك سجدة صلبية من صلاته لا تنصرف هذه السجدة إليها لما أنه تشترط النية في السجدة وصلاته فاسدة اهـ. وإذا بطل فرض الإمام برفعة بطل فرض المأموم سواء كان قعد أو لا، ولذا ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه : ولو أن الإمام لم يقعد على رأس الرابعة وقام إلى الخامسة ساهياً وتشهد المقتدي وسلم أنه يصح ترك هذا النقل قوله : (فسدت اتفاقاً ا هـ قال الرملي قال المرحوم شيخ شيخنا علي المقدسي: لم ينته بل ذكر بعده ما يندفع به عنه الإشكال فإنه قال : لما سنذكره في تتمة نعقدها للسجدات وذكر هناك ما يوضحه اهـ . وذكر في النهر ما قرره في تلك التتمة وهو أنه إذا علم أنها من غير الركعة الأخيرة أو تحرى فوقع تحريه على ذلك أو لم يقع تحريه على شيء وبقي شاكاً في أنها من الأخيرة أو ما قبلها وجب عليه نية القضاء، وإن علم أنها من الركعة الأخيرة لم يحتج إلى نية، وعلى هذا ما ذكر فيمن سلم من الفجر وعليه السهو فسجد وقعد وتكلم ثم تذكر أن عليه صلبية من الأولى فسدت، وإن من الثانية لا ونابت إحدى سجدتي السهو عن الصلبية ا.هـ. قال في النهر : وهذا التقدير يقتضي نقض ما قدمه من دعوى الاتفاق على الفساد بتذكر الصلبية، وذلك أنه إذا علم أنها من الأخيرة فينبغي أن لا تفسد اتفاقاً لانصرافها إليها أو من غيرها أو لم يعلم وقد نواها فكذلك إلا أنه لا يعيدها لما مر، أما إذا لم ينوها فسدت عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد لعدم انصرافها إليها، وعلى هذا فما في الخلاصة ليس على إطلاقه بل فسادها إنما هو على قول الثاني فقط ا.هـ. وقوله لعدم انصرافها علة لقوله فسدت عند أبي يوسف وأما عدمه عند محمد فلما ذكره المؤلف . وبما قرره في النهر ظهر ما في
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness, page 181. [Regarding] the last [sitting]: he returns as long as he has not prostrated, and he prostrates for forgetfulness. If he prostrates, his obligatory prayer becomes invalid by raising his head, and it becomes supererogatory according to the chosen [view] being the obligation of prostration because to the extent that he engaged in standing, he delayed an obligatory [act] which had to be joined to what preceded it of the pillar, so he became a abandoner of the obligatory, so two prostrations of forgetfulness are obligatory upon him. End quote. So the preference differs according to three sayings, and most [scholars] are upon the first. His saying: 'If he forgets the last [sitting], he returns as long as he has not prostrated' because in it is the reform of his prayer, so that is possible for him because what is less than a rak'ah is a place of abandonment. He meant by 'the last' the obligatory sitting to include the four-, three-, and two-rak'ah prayers, for its sitting is not multiple except that it is said it is called 'last' in consideration that it is the end of the prayer, not in consideration that it is preceded by its like. He made it absolute, so it includes whether he did not sit at all or he sat a light sitting less than the amount of tashahhud, and if he returns, the light sitting is counted for him, so that even if both sittings were of the amount of tashahhud, then he spoke after it, his prayer is valid as we presented in the chapter of the description of prayer from al-Walwaljiyyah. His saying: 'And he prostrates for forgetfulness' because he delayed an obligatory [act], which is the last sitting. And al-Hidayah reasoned it by saying he delayed an obligatory [act], so they said: he meant by it the definitive obligatory (al-wajib al-qat'i), which is the fard, and this is more appropriate than what is in al-‘Inayah of interpretation by the expression of the salutation because he did not delay it from its place because its place is after sitting, and he did not sit; rather he delayed the sitting. The more appropriate is to say: he meant by it the obligatory whose permissibility is lost by its loss since its evidence is not definitive. His saying: 'If he prostrates, his obligatory prayer becomes invalid by his raising [his head]' because his commencement in the supererogatory became firm before completing the pillars of the obligatory, and from its necessity is his exit from the obligatory. This is because a rak'ah with one prostration is a true prayer; he breaks his oath by saying he does not pray. And his saying: 'by his raising [his head]' meaning by raising the face from the ground, indicating that [the invalidation occurs by raising] and he disagrees regarding if he raises both [knees]. And his saying: 'and in al-Walwaljiyyah, etc.' made it a third saying because it is apparent that whenever he is closer to the sitting, prostration is incumbent upon him, whether he raised his knees from the ground or not. The author's saying: 'he returns as long as he has not prostrated' – al-Nahr said: meaning as long as he has not tied his rak'ah with a prostration, and he intended by this not [the case] if he prostrated without bowing, for he also returns due to the lack of consideration of this prostration. His saying: 'the delay of the fard' – al-Nahr said: he did not distinguish between whether he is closer to the sitting or not, and it should be that he does not prostrate when he is closer to it as in the first [case] due to what preceded. Al-Hawashi al-Sa‘diyyah said: And it is possible to differentiate between them: the one close to the sitting, even if it is permissible to give him the ruling of the sitter, yet he is not a sitter in reality, so the aspect of reality is considered when he forgets the second [sitting] and the ruling of the sitter is given in the forgetfulness of the first to show the difference between the obligatory (al-wajib) and the fard. By this it is known that whoever interpreted al-wajib as al-qat‘i (definitive) was correct, otherwise the difference becomes problematic. And it may be said: why not allow that he interpret it as the strong of its two types, which is that whose permissibility is lost by its loss, and it is not problematic by establishing the difference between its two types; yes, it is problematic for one who interprets it by the expression of the salutation or tashahhud. His saying: 'and this is more appropriate than what is in al-‘Inayah' – Shaykh Isma‘il objected that what is in al-‘Inayah is its interpretation as al-qat‘i, so the narration is not correct. Yes, al-‘Inayah interpreted al-wajib by that in the case of the last sitting. His saying: 'because he did not delay it from...' – al-Nahr said: it is rebutted because the delay occurs in both, so it is correct to attribute the prostration to whichever one was. Shaykh Isma‘il said: it can be attributed to the stronger, which is the fard, with loosening the reins, and you have known that a forgetfulness occurred in the second issue, which is its place. Page 182. Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. The chosen fatwa is that it does not become invalid by placing the forehead, as is narrated from Abu Yusuf, because the completion of a thing is by its last part, and the last of the prostration is the raising, for a thing only ends by its opposite. For this reason, if he prostrated before his imam and his imam caught up with him in it, it is valid; if it were completed by placing, it would not be valid because every pillar performed before the imam is not valid. And because if it were completed before raising, hadath would not nullify it, but there is consensus on the necessity of repeating every pillar in which precedence of hadath occurred with the restriction of building. And the fruit of the difference is: if he has an hadath during the sajdah, so he leaves and performs wudu, then remembers that he did not sit in the fourth [rak'ah]. Abu Yusuf said: he does not return to the sitting and his obligatory prayer is invalid. And Muhammad said: he returns and completes his obligatory prayer. They said: Abu Yusuf was informed of Muhammad's answer and said: 'Zah! A prayer that has become invalid, hadath would rectify it?' And this is the meaning of what the common people ask: 'What prayer does hadath rectify?' It is this prayer according to Muhammad's saying, and 'Zah' is a word of wonder, and Abu Yusuf said it mockingly. And it was said: the correct [pronunciation] is with dammah and the zay is not pure. Thus in al-Mughrib. And in Fath al-Qadir: 'This – meaning the validity of building due to the prior hadath – [applies] if he does not remember during that sajdah a structural prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) from his prayer; if he remembers that, it is invalid by agreement, end quote.' And it is not hidden what is in it; rather, there is no restriction because if hadath overcame him while he is prostrating, he did not mix supererogatory with obligatory before completing it according to Muhammad, whether he remembers that he has a structural prostration or not, since there is no difference between having one pillar or two pillars. And the expression of al-Khulasah is more appropriate: 'And if he ties the fifth [rak'ah] with the prostration and remembers that he left a structural prostration from his prayer, this prostration does not turn to it because intention is required in the prostration, and his prayer is invalid, end quote.' And if the obligatory prayer of the imam becomes invalid by his raising [his head], the obligatory prayer of the follower becomes invalid whether he sat or not. For this reason, Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatwas: 'If the imam did not sit at the end of the fourth and stood to the fifth forgetfully, and the follower performed tashahhud and gave salutation, that it is valid...' leaving this narration. His saying: 'it is invalid by agreement, end quote' – al-Ramli said: the late shaykh of our shaykh, ‘Ali al-Maqdisi, said: he did not finish, but rather he mentioned after it what dispels the problem, for he said: 'as we will mention in a sequel we will devote to prostrations' and he mentioned there what clarifies it, end quote. And al-Nahr mentioned what he stated in that sequel: that if he knows it is from other than the last rak'ah or he attempted and his attempt fell on that or his attempt did not fall on anything and he remained doubtful whether it is from the last or what is before it, intention of making up is obligatory upon him; and if he knows it is from the last rak'ah, he does not need intention. Upon this is what was mentioned regarding one who gave salutation from Fajr while having forgetfulness, so he prostrated and sat and spoke, then remembered that he has a structural [prostration] from the first [rak'ah] – it is invalid; if from the second, it is not, and one of the two prostrations of forgetfulness substitutes for the structural [prostration], end quote. Al-Nahr said: this estimation requires breaking what he presented of the claim of consensus on invalidity by remembering the structural [prostration]; that is because if he knows it is from the last, then it should not be invalid by agreement due to its diverting to it; or from other than it or he does not know and he intended it, likewise except that he does not repeat it due to what passed. As for if he did not intend it, it is invalid according to Abu Yusuf contrary to Muhammad due to non-diversion to it. Upon this, what is in al-Khulasah is not absolute; rather, its invalidity is only according to the second saying, end quote. And his saying 'due to non-diversion' is the reason for his saying 'it is invalid according to Abu Yusuf', and as for its non-invalidity according to Muhammad, it is due to what the author mentioned. And by what al-Nahr stated, what is in it becomes clear.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on a person who forgets the final sitting (al-qa'dah al-akhirah) in prayer, stands up for an extra rak'ah, and then remembers during the extra rak'ah. The text explains that if he has not yet performed the sajdah (prostration) of the extra rak'ah, he must return to the sitting and complete his prayer with sujud al-sahw. However, if he has performed the sajdah and raised his head from it, his obligatory (fard) prayer becomes invalid and the extra rak'ah becomes a supererogatory (nafl) prayer. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The relied-upon fatwa (al-mukhtar li al-fatwa) is narrated from Abu Yusuf, who holds that the invalidation occurs only upon raising the head (raf'), not upon placing the forehead (wad' al-jabhah). The practical consequence (thamarah) arises when a person experiences a hadath (ritual impurity) during the sajdah of the extra rak'ah: according to Abu Yusuf, he does not return to the forgotten sitting and his prayer is invalid; according to Muhammad, he returns, performs wudu, and completes his prayer. The text also addresses the case where one remembers a structural prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) missing from the original prayer, leading to further disagreement about whether the extra sajdah can substitute for it. The overall discussion illustrates the Hanafi method of deriving rulings through careful analysis of the nature of actions (e.g., what constitutes completion of a prostration) and the hierarchy of obligations (fard vs. wajib).

Key Terms
الأخير (al-akhir): The final sitting of the prayer (al-qa'dah al-akhirah), which is fard in the Hanafi school.
سجد للسهو (sajada li al-sahw): To perform the prostration of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw), which is wajib for certain omissions or additions in prayer.
رفع (رأس السجدة) (raf' (ra's al-sajdah)): The act of raising the head from prostration; according to Abu Yusuf, this is what completes the sajdah and invalidates the fard if done in an extra rak'ah.
سجدة صلبية (sajdah salbiyyah): A structural prostration (one of the two sajdahs of a rak'ah) that is obligatory (fard) in the original prayer; forgetting it requires repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa in this passage, when does the extra rak'ah (due to forgetting the final sitting) become a supererogatory (nafl) prayer?
A) Immediately upon standing for the fifth rak'ah.
B) Upon placing the forehead on the ground for the sajdah.
C) Upon raising the head from the sajdah.
D) Upon completing the tashahhud of the extra rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi fatwa is that the extra rak'ah due to forgetting the final sitting becomes nafl only upon raising the head from sajdah – a distinction grounded in the principle that actions are completed by their last part.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
8 min
Completion of Sajdah and Effect of Remembering a Missed Sajdah during Sujud al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute with later tafsil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the completion of prostration and apply the tafsil from al-Nahr to determine the ruling when a missed obligatory sajdah is remembered during forgetfulness prostrations.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, prostration is completed by lifting, not placing; the effect of remembering a missed sajda during sahwi prostration depends on intention and knowledge of which rak'ah it belongs to.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on two interconnected issues: when exactly is a prostration (sajdah) considered complete, and what happens if during the prostration of forgetfulness (sujūd al-sahw) one remembers a missed obligatory prostration (sajdah ṣalbiyyah)? Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly applying the rulings of prayer correction and ensuring the validity of one's salah. The later Hanafi scholars, especially in al-Nahr, provide a detailed resolution that refines the absolute statements found in earlier texts.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed-upon principle
First, note the chosen fatwa (al-mukhtar al-fatwa) that prostration is not completed by placing the forehead (wad') but by lifting (raf'). The reasoning is that a thing ends by its opposite; lifting is the opposite of placing. Confirm this as the basis of the dispute.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute scenario
The fruit of the difference appears in the scenario: a person breaks wind (hadath) during prostration, leaves, makes wudu, then remembers he did not sit for the fourth rak'ah. Abu Yusuf says he does not return and his prayer is invalid; Muhammad says he returns and completes it. Understand each imam's dalil.
This scenario triggers the question of whether the sajdah was already complete before the hadath.
3
Analyze each imam's proof
Abu Yusuf's argument is based on strict analogy: the sajdah is incomplete until lifting, so the hadath nullified it. Muhammad's argument allows building upon the hadath because the sajdah's completion by lifting is not yet relevant. Note the asl (original case) and far' (new case) in their analogies.
Abu Yusuf mocked Muhammad's position ('Wow, a prayer that was spoiled and hadath fixes it!'), but this is a rhetorical point, not a proof.
4
Examine the effect of a missed obligator sajda
The text discusses whether remembering a missed sajda (sajdah salbiyyah) during the prostration of forgetfulness invalidates the prayer. Fath al-Qadir claims it does by consensus, but the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq rejects this based on the reasoning that the hadath did not mix nafl with fard before completion.
Al-Khulasa adds the requirement of intention for the sahwi prostration to count for the missed sajda.
5
Apply the later tafsil from al-Nahr
Al-Nahr resolves the dispute by considering the knowledge of which rak'ah the missed sajda belongs to. If it is known to be from the last rak'ah, no intention is needed; if from an earlier rak'ah or unknown, intention of qada (replacement) is required. This tafsil qualifies the earlier claim of consensus on invalidity.
Thus, the ruling is not absolute; it depends on the worshipper's certainty and intent.

كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو
المختار الفتوى أنه لا يبطل بوضع الجهة كما هو مروي عن أبي يوسف لأن تمام الشيء بآخره وآخر السجدة الرفع إذ الشيء إنما ينتهي بضده، ولهذا لو سجد قبل إمامه فأدركه إمامه فيه جاز ولو تمت بالوضع لما جاز لأن كل ركن أداه قبل إمامه لا يجوز ولأنه لو تم قبل الرفع لم ينقضه الحدث لكن الاتفاق على لزوم إعادة كل ركن وجد فيه سبق الحدث بقيد البناء. وثمرة الاختلاف فيما إذا أحدث في السجود فانصرف وتوضأ ثم تذكر أنه لم يقعد في الرابعة. قال أبو يوسف : لا يعود إلى القعود وبطل فرضه. وقال محمد يعود ويتم فرضه. قالوا: أخبر أبو يوسف بجواب محمد فقال : زه صلاة فسدت يصلحها الحدث وهذا معنى ما يسأله العامة أي صلاة يصلحها الحدث فهي هذه الصلاة على قول محمد وزه كلمة استعجاب وإنما قالها أبو يوسف تهكماً. وقيل: الصواب بالضم والزاي ليست بخالصة. كذا في المغرب. وفي فتح القدير : وهذا أعني صحة البناء بسبب سبق الحدث إذا لم يتذكر في ذلك السجود سجدة صلبية من صلاته فإن تذكر ذلك فسدت اتفاقاً اهـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه بل لا التقييد لأنه إذا سبقه الحدث وهو ساجد لم يخلط النفل بالفرض قبل إكماله عند محمد، سواء تذكر أن عليه سجدة صلبية أو لا، إذ لا فرق بين أن يكون عليه ركن واحد أو ركنان . وعبارة الخلاصة أولى وهي : ولو قيد الخامسة بالسجدة فتذكر أنه ترك سجدة صلبية من صلاته لا تنصرف هذه السجدة إليها لما أنه تشترط النية في السجدة وصلاته فاسدة اهـ. وإذا بطل فرض الإمام برفعة بطل فرض المأموم سواء كان قعد أو لا، ولذا ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه : ولو أن الإمام لم يقعد على رأس الرابعة وقام إلى الخامسة ساهياً وتشهد المقتدي وسلم أنه يصح ترك هذا النقل قوله : (فسدت اتفاقاً ا هـ قال الرملي قال المرحوم شيخ شيخنا علي المقدسي: لم ينته بل ذكر بعده ما يندفع به عنه الإشكال فإنه قال : لما سنذكره في تتمة نعقدها للسجدات وذكر هناك ما يوضحه اهـ . وذكر في النهر ما قرره في تلك التتمة وهو أنه إذا علم أنها من غير الركعة الأخيرة أو تحرى فوقع تحريه على ذلك أو لم يقع تحريه على شيء وبقي شاكاً في أنها من الأخيرة أو ما قبلها وجب عليه نية القضاء، وإن علم أنها من الركعة الأخيرة لم يحتج إلى نية، وعلى هذا ما ذكر فيمن سلم من الفجر وعليه السهو فسجد وقعد وتكلم ثم تذكر أن عليه صلبية من الأولى فسدت، وإن من الثانية لا ونابت إحدى سجدتي السهو عن الصلبية ا.هـ. قال في النهر : وهذا التقدير يقتضي نقض ما قدمه من دعوى الاتفاق على الفساد بتذكر الصلبية، وذلك أنه إذا علم أنها من الأخيرة فينبغي أن لا تفسد اتفاقاً لانصرافها إليها أو من غيرها أو لم يعلم وقد نواها فكذلك إلا أنه لا يعيدها لما مر، أما إذا لم ينوها فسدت عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد لعدم انصرافها إليها، وعلى هذا فما في الخلاصة ليس على إطلاقه بل فسادها إنما هو على قول الثاني فقط ا.هـ. وقوله لعدم انصرافها علة لقوله فسدت عند أبي يوسف وأما عدمه عند محمد فلما ذكره المؤلف . وبما قرره في النهر ظهر ما في قبل أن يقيد الإمام الخامسة بالسجدة ثم قيدها بالسجدة فسدت صلاتهم جميعاً اهـ.
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. The chosen position for fatwa is that it is not invalidated by placing the forehead, as narrated from Abu Yusuf, because the completion of a thing is by its end, and the end of prostration is the lifting, since a thing only ends by its opposite. For this reason, if one prostrated before his imam and the imam caught up with him in it, it is permissible. If it were completed by placing, it would not be permissible because every pillar performed before the imam is not permissible. And because if it were completed before lifting, a hadath (ritual impurity) would not nullify it. But there is consensus on the necessity of repeating every pillar in which hadath preceded, with the restriction of building upon it. The fruit of the difference is in the case where one breaks wind in prostration, then leaves and performs wudu, then remembers that he did not sit for the fourth (rak'ah). Abu Yusuf said: He does not return to sitting and his obligatory prayer is invalid. Muhammad said: He returns and completes his obligatory prayer. They said: Abu Yusuf was informed of Muhammad's answer and said: "Wow, a prayer that was spoiled and hadath fixes it!" This is the meaning of what the common people ask: "Which prayer does hadath fix?" It is this prayer according to Muhammad's statement. "Wow" is a word of astonishment, and Abu Yusuf only said it mockingly. It was said: The correct pronunciation is with dammah, and the zay is not exclusive. Thus in al-Mughrib. In Fath al-Qadir: This, meaning the validity of building due to precedence of hadath, applies if one does not remember in that prostration a solidary prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) from his prayer. If he remembers that, it is invalid by consensus. It is not hidden what is in it; rather it is not restricted, because if hadath preceded him while he was prostrating, he has not mixed supererogatory with obligatory before its completion according to Muhammad, whether he remembers that he owes a solidary prostration or not, since there is no difference between owing one pillar or two. The expression of al-Khulasa is more appropriate: "If he bound the fifth with the prostration then remembered that he left a solidary prostration from his prayer, this prostration does not serve for it because intention is required in the prostration, and his prayer is invalid." If the obligatory prayer of the imam is invalidated by his lifting, the obligatory prayer of the follower is invalidated, whether he sat or not. For this reason Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa: If the imam did not sit at the end of the fourth and stood for the fifth forgetfully, and the follower recited the tashahhud and gave salam, that it is valid to leave this transmission. His saying: (it is invalid by consensus) - al-Ramli said, the late teacher of our teacher Ali al-Maqdisi said: He did not finish, but rather mentioned after it what removes the difficulty, for he said: 'As we will mention in a supplement that we will dedicate to the prostrations,' and he mentioned there what clarifies it. Mentioned in al-Nahr his determination in that supplement: that if he knows that it is from other than the last rak'ah, or he makes an assessment and his assessment falls on that, or his assessment falls on nothing and he remains doubtful whether it is from the last or before it, it is obligatory upon him to intend qada'. If he knows that it is from the last rak'ah, he does not need intention. Upon this is what was mentioned about one who gave salam from Fajr while owing prostrations for forgetfulness, so he prostrated, sat, spoke, then remembered that he owes a solidary prostration from the first (rak'ah) - it is invalid. If from the second, it is not invalid, and one of the two forgetfulness prostrations suffices for the solidary prostration. He said in al-Nahr: This determination necessitates a refutation of what he presented of the claim of consensus on invalidity due to remembering the solidary prostration, because if he knows that it is from the last, it should not be invalid by consensus because the prostration applies to it, or from other than it, or he does not know and he intended it, similarly, except that he does not repeat it for what passed. If he did not intend it, it is invalid according to Abu Yusuf contrary to Muhammad, because it does not apply to it. Upon this, what is in al-Khulasa is not absolute; rather its invalidity is only according to the second (Abu Yusuf) only. His saying "because it does not apply" is the cause for his saying "it is invalid according to Abu Yusuf". As for its non-invalidity according to Muhammad, it is for what the author mentioned. And by what was determined in al-Nahr, what appears before the imam bound the fifth with the prostration, then bound it with the prostration, their prayer is invalid for all of them.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the completion of prostration and its effect when one remembers a missed obligatory prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) during Sajdah al-Sahw. The discussion begins with the chosen fatwa that prostration is not completed by placing the forehead (wad' al-jabhah) but by lifting (raf'), as narrated from Abu Yusuf. The reasoning is that an action is completed by its opposite—lifting is the opposite of placing, so the prostration ends with lifting. This is applied to the case of prostrating behind the imam: if one prostrates before the imam and the imam catches up, it is valid because the pillar is not complete until lifting. The practical difference (thamarah) appears in a scenario: someone breaks wind during prostration, leaves, performs wudu, then remembers that he did not sit for the fourth rak'ah. Abu Yusuf holds that he does not return to the sitting and his fard (obligatory prayer) is invalid. Muhammad holds that he returns and completes his fard. Abu Yusuf mocked Muhammad's position saying, 'Wow, a prayer that was spoiled and hadath fixes it!' The text then discusses the effect of remembering a sajda salbiyyah. According to Fath al-Qadir, if one does not remember a missed sajda during the sahwi prostration, building is valid, but if he remembers, it is invalid by consensus. However, the author notes that this is not restricted because if hadath preceded while prostrating, he has not mixed nafl with fard before completion according to Muhammad. Al-Khulasa states that if one performs a fifth rak'ah with a prostration and then remembers a missed sajda from the original prayer, that sahwi prostration does not serve for it because intention is required. The passage concludes with the imam's scenario from Qadi Khan: if the imam forgets the final tashahhud and stands for the fifth rak'ah, the follower's prayer depends on the imam's action. If the imam's fard is invalidated by lifting, so is the follower's. The commentary from al-Nahr clarifies the conditions regarding knowing which rak'ah the missed sajda belongs to.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.
سجدة صلبية (sajdah ṣalbiyyah): An obligatory prostration that is an integral part of the original prayer, distinct from the prostration of forgetfulness.
الخامسة (al-khāmisah): The fifth rak'ah added mistakenly during a four-rak'ah prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position stated in the text, when is the prostration (sajdah) considered complete?
A) When the forehead is placed on the ground (wad').
B) When the forehead is lifted (raf').
C) When the person remains still for a moment.
D) When the nose also touches.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, prostration is completed by lifting, and the effect of remembering a missed obligatory prostration during forgetfulness prostrations is determined by intention and knowledge of which rak'ah the omission belongs to.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Imam Adding Fifth Rak'ah on Follower's Prayer and Adding Sixth Rak'ah
Continuation of rulings on imam forgetting final tashahhud and adding fifth rak'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the follower's prayer when the imam returns before prostration in the fifth rak'ah, and explain the requirement of adding a sixth rak'ah when the prayer becomes nafl.

Core Idea
A follower's prayer is not invalidated by an extra prostration if the imam returns; a nafl prayer must be in pairs, so a sixth rak'ah is recommended.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two related issues when the imam forgets the final tashahhud and adds a fifth rak'ah: the validity of the followers' prayer and the transformation of the prayer into nafl. We will examine the conditions for the follower's prayer to remain valid and the necessity of adding a sixth rak'ah to avoid witr in nafl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The imam forgets the final tashahhud and stands for a fifth rak'ah. He then returns to the sitting before performing the prostration of the fifth rak'ah. The followers, unaware, prostrate.
This scenario is specific to the imam's forgetfulness in a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer like Zuhr.
2
Determine the Ruling on the Follower's Prayer
According to al-Muhit, the follower's prayer is not invalidated because the imam's return annuls his own bowing (ruk'u) and consequently the followers' bowing. The extra prostration performed by the followers does not invalidate their prayer.
The key is that the followers' bowing was built upon the imam's; when the imam returns, his bowing is annulled, so theirs is also annulled.
3
Distinguish Intentional vs. Forgetful Prostration
If the follower prostrated intentionally after the imam returned, the prayer is invalid. If forgetful, there is a difference of opinion; the precaution is to repeat the prayer.
This distinction comes from al-Mujtaba and is important for practical application.
4
When the Prayer Becomes Nafl: Adding a Sixth Rak'ah
If the imam does not return and completes the fifth rak'ah, the prayer becomes nafl (supererogatory). The follower must then add a sixth rak'ah to make the prayer even, because performing nafl as witr (odd) is not legislated.
Exceptions: For Asr and Fajr prayers, the sixth rak'ah is not added because voluntary prayer at those times is disliked.
5
Note the Intra-Madhhab Dispute
The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) requires adding a sixth rak'ah, while Muhammad holds that it is not necessary if the imam does not intend nafl. The relied-upon position is that the sixth is recommended (nadb), not obligatory.
The text in al-Bada'i favors recommendation, and this is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسواء كان المأموم مسبوقاً أو مدركاً كما في الظهيرية. وإذا لم يبطل فرض الإمام بعوده قبل السجود لم يبطل فرض المأموم وإن سجد لما في المحيط : لو صلى إمام ولم يقعد في الرابعة من الظهر وقام إلى الخامسة فركع وتابعه القوم ثم عاد الإمام إلى القعدة ولم يعلم القوم حتى سجد والسجدة لا تفسد صلاتهم لأنهم لما عاد الإمام إلى القعدة ارتفض ركوعه فيرتفض ركوع القوم أيضاً تبعاً له لأنه بناء عليه فبقي لهم زيادة سجدة وذلك لا يفسد الصلاة اهـ. وهذا مما يلغزبه فيقال : مصل ترك القعدة الأخيرة وقيد الخامسة بسجدة ولم تبطل صلاته، أنه ومصل قعد ولم يعتبر قعودة وبطلت بتركه . وقيد بقوله ولم يعلم القوم لما في المجتبي لو عاد الإمام إلى القعود قبل السجود وسجد المقتدي عمداً تفسد وفي السهو خلاف، والأحوط الإعادة .اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : ولا يخفى عدم متابعتهم له فيما إذا قام قبل القعدة وإذا عاد لا يعيد والتشهد.
قوله (فصارت نفلاً فيضم إليها سادسة لما سبق مراراً من أنه لا يلزم من بطلان الوصف بطلان الأصل عندهما خلافاً لمحمد فيضم سادسة لأن التنفل بالوتر غير مشروع ولو لم يضم فلا شيء عليه لأنه ظان وشروعه ليس بملزم وإذا اقتدى به إنسان في الخامسة ثم أفسدها فعلى قول محمد لا يتصور القضاء، وعندهما يقضي ستاً لشروعة في تحريمة الست بخلاف ما إذا عاد الإمام قبل السجدة فإنه يقضي أربعاً. ثم صرح المصنف في الوافي بأن السادسة مندوب وتركه في المختصر للاختلاف. وفي عبارة القدوري تبعاً لرواية الأصل إشارة إلى الوجوب فإنه قال : وكان عليه أن يضم إليها ركعة سادسة ووجهه في فتح القدير بعدم جواز التنفل بالوتر . وفي المبسوط وأحب إلي أن يشفع الخامسة لأن النفل شرع شفعاً لا وتراً. كذا في البدائع والأظهر الندب لأن عدم جواز التنفل بالوتر إنما هو عند القصد، ضم في أما عند عدمه فلا ولهذا لا يلزمه شيء لو قطعه . وفي السراج الوهاج : إن ضم السادسة سائر الصلوات إلا في العصر فإنه لا يضم إليها لأنه يكون تطوعاً قبل المغرب وذلك مكروه، وفي قاضيخان إلا الفجر فإنه لا يضيف إليها لأن التنفل قبلها وبعدها مكروه اهـ. وسيأتي أن
كلام الرملي عن المقدسي فتدبر قوله : ( ومصل قعد ولم يعتبر قعوده المراد به القعود الأخير وهذا مصور في فرع الخانية المذكور آنفاً ولكن قوله وبطلت بتركه لم يظهر لي فائدته تأمل قوله : (لأنه يكون تطوعاً قبل المغرب) لعل الأولى أن يقال لأنه يكون تطوعاً بعد العصر فتأمل قوله : (وفي قاضيخان إلا الفجر) قال في النهر وأنت خبير بأن ما اقتصر عليه قاضيخان من الفجر هو الصواب وذلك أن موضوع المسألة حيث كان فيما إذا لم يقعد وبطل فرضه كيف لا يضم في العصر ولا كراهة في التنفل قبله، ثم بعد مدة عن لي حين إقراء هذا بالجامع الأزهر أنه يمكن حمله على ما إذا كان يقضي عصراً
Whether the follower is a latecomer or a concurrent one as in al-Zahiriyyah. If the obligatory prayer of the imam is not invalidated by his return before prostration, the obligatory prayer of the follower is not invalidated even if he prostrated, as in al-Muhit: If an imam prayed and did not sit for the fourth of Zuhr and stood for the fifth, bowed, and the people followed him, then the imam returned to the sitting and the people did not know until they prostrated, the prostration does not invalidate their prayer because when the imam returned to the sitting, his bowing was annulled, so their bowing is also annulled following him, because it is built upon him. So they have an extra prostration, and that does not invalidate the prayer. This is used as an enigma: 'A worshipper who left the final sitting and bound the fifth with a prostration, and his prayer was not invalidated,' along with 'a worshipper who sat but his sitting was not considered, and it was invalidated by leaving it.' He restricted with his saying 'and the people did not know' because in al-Mujtaba: if the imam returned to the sitting before prostration and the follower prostrated intentionally, it invalidates; in forgetfulness there is difference, and the precaution is repetition. In Fath al-Qadir: It is not hidden that they do not follow him when he stood before the sitting, and if he returns, he does not repeat and the tashahhud. His saying (so it becomes supererogatory, so he adds a sixth to it, because it has passed repeatedly that the invalidation of the description does not necessitate the invalidation of the essence according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad, so he adds a sixth because performing supererogatory as witr is not legislated. If he does not add, nothing is upon him because he is uncertain and his commencement is not binding. If a person follows him in the fifth then invalidates it, according to Muhammad, qada' is inconceivable; according to both, he prays six (rak'ahs) because of his commencement in the tahrimah of six, unlike if the imam returned before prostration, then he prays four. Then the author stated in al-Wafi that the sixth is recommended, and he left it in al-Mukhtasar due to difference. In the expression of al-Quduri following the narration of the original, there is an indication of obligation, for he said: 'It was upon him to add a sixth rak'ah to it.' The justification in Fath al-Qadir is the impermissibility of performing supererogatory as witr. In al-Mabsut: 'I prefer that he makes the fifth even (shaf') because supererogatory is prescribed in pairs, not as witr.' Thus in al-Bada'i. The most apparent is that it is recommended (nadb) because the impermissibility of supererogatory as witr is only when intending it, but when not intending it, no. For this reason, nothing is required of him if he cuts it off. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The addition of the sixth applies to all prayers except in Asr, because it would be voluntary before Maghrib, and that is disliked. In Qadi Khan: except for Fajr, because voluntary before and after it is disliked. And it will come that the speech of al-Ramli about al-Maqdisi, so reflect. His saying: (and a worshipper who sat but his sitting was not considered) means the final sitting, and this is depicted in the branch of al-Khaniyyah mentioned earlier. But his saying 'and it was invalidated by leaving it' did not appear to me its benefit, ponder. His saying: (because it would be voluntary before Maghrib) perhaps it is better to say because it would be voluntary after Asr, so ponder. His saying: (And in Qadi Khan except for Fajr) al-Nahr said: And you are aware that what Qadi Khan confined to Fajr is correct, because the subject of the issue is where he did not sit and his obligatory prayer is invalid. How would he not add in Asr, and there is no dislike in voluntary before it? Then after a while it occurred to me while teaching this at al-Azhar Mosque that it can be interpreted as when he is making up an Asr prayer.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the imam's forgetfulness in prayer, specifically when he omits the final tashahhud and adds a fifth rak'ah. The first part discusses the follower's prayer. If the imam returns to the sitting (qadah) before performing the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah, the follower's prayer is not invalidated, even if he prostrated, because the imam's return annuls the bowing (ruk'u) and the follower's bowing is also annulled. The follower only has an extra prostration, which does not invalidate prayer. But if the follower prostrated intentionally, it invalidates; if forgetfully, there is a difference of opinion, and the precaution is repetition. The second part addresses the case where the imam's prayer becomes supererogatory (nafl) due to the addition of the fifth rak'ah. He must add a sixth rak'ah to make it an even number because performing witr (odd number) as nafl is not legislated. This is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, while Abu Hanifa may have a different basis. The text notes that the sixth is recommended (nadb) according to some, but al-Quduri's expression suggests obligation (wujub). The author prefers recommendation. Specific exceptions: for Asr prayer, the sixth is not added because it becomes voluntary after Asr which is disliked; similarly for Fajr, voluntary before and after it is disliked. The passage ends with a note from al-Nahr clarifying that Qadi Khan's exception for Fajr is correct, and the issue of adding in Asr may be interpreted for a qada' prayer.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has already started.
المدرك (al-mudrik): A follower who joins the prayer from the beginning and prays with the imam.
السادسة (al-sadisah): The sixth rak'ah added to make the prayer even after it becomes nafl.
الوصف (al-wasf): Description or attribute; here refers to the extra prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an imam forgets the final tashahhud and stands for a fifth rak'ah, then returns to the sitting before prostrating, and the followers prostrate without knowing, what is the ruling on the followers' prayer?
A) Their prayer is invalid because they prostrated after the imam's return.
B) Their prayer is valid, and they have an extra prostration that does not invalidate.
C) Their prayer is invalid if they prostrated intentionally, but valid if forgetfully.
D) Their prayer is valid only if they did not prostrate.

Key Takeaway
A follower's prayer is not invalidated by an extra prostration performed unknowingly due to the imam's forgetfulness; and when a prayer becomes nafl, a sixth rak'ah is recommended to avoid witr.

Imam Returns Before Sajdah: Followers' Prayer Valid
Ruling on imam returning to qa'dah before sajdah of fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an imam returns before sajdah of an extra rak'ah and explain why the followers' prayer remains valid.

Core Idea
An extra sajdah does not invalidate the followers' prayer if the imam returns before performing it.

In congregational prayer, what happens if the imam mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah but returns to the sitting before prostrating? The followers, unaware, may also prostrate. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the validity of the followers' prayer in such a scenario, based on a narration from al-Muhit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Locate the specific case: imam stands for an extra rak'ah (e.g., fifth in Zuhr), returns to sitting before the sajdah of that extra rak'ah, and the followers prostrate unknowingly.
2
Analyze the effect of the return
The imam's return annuls his bowing (ruku') for the extra rak'ah. Since the followers' bowing is built upon the imam's, it is also annulled. The extra prostration (sajdah) remains but is not tied to a valid bowing.
Key: the extra rak'ah is effectively nullified by the return before sajdah.
3
Apply the principle
A single extra sajdah without a corresponding bowing does not invalidate the prayer. The followers' prayer is valid (sahih), provided they acted forgetfully.
Intentional prostration after return may invalidate, as noted in al-Mujtaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو
قبل أن يقيد الإمام الخامسة بالسجدة ثم قيدها بالسجدة فسدت صلاتهم جميعاً اهـ. وسواء كان المأموم مسبوقاً أو مدركاً كما في الظهيرية. وإذا لم يبطل فرض الإمام بعوده قبل السجود لم يبطل فرض المأموم وإن سجد لما في المحيط : لو صلى إمام ولم يقعد في الرابعة من الظهر وقام إلى الخامسة فركع وتابعه القوم ثم عاد الإمام إلى القعدة ولم يعلم القوم حتى سجد والسجدة لا تفسد صلاتهم لأنهم لما عاد الإمام إلى القعدة ارتفض ركوعه فيرتفض ركوع القوم أيضاً تبعاً له لأنه بناء عليه فبقي لهم زيادة سجدة وذلك لا يفسد الصلاة اهـ. وهذا مما يلغزبه فيقال : مصل ترك القعدة الأخيرة وقيد الخامسة بسجدة ولم تبطل صلاته، أنه ومصل قعد ولم يعتبر قعوده وبطلت بتركه . وقيد بقوله ولم يعلم القوم لما في المجتبي لو عاد الإمام إلى القعود قبل السجود وسجد المقتدي عمداً تفسد وفي السهو خلاف، والأحوط الإعادة .اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : ولا يخفى عدم متابعتهم له فيما إذا قام قبل القعدة وإذا عاد لا يعيد والتشهد.
The Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. Before the Imam ties the fifth (rak'ah) with the prostration, then ties it with the prostration, all their prayers are invalidated. And it is the same whether the follower is one who is preceded (masbuq) or one who catches up (mudrik) as in al-Zahiriyyah. And if the Imam's obligatory prayer is not invalidated by his return before the prostration, then the follower's obligatory prayer is not invalidated even if he prostrated, as in al-Muhit: If an Imam prayed and did not sit for the fourth of Zuhr and stood for the fifth and bowed, and the people followed him, then the Imam returned to the sitting and the people did not know until they prostrated, that prostration does not invalidate their prayer because when the Imam returned to the sitting, his bowing was annulled, so the peoples' bowing is also annulled following him because it is built upon it, so they are left with an extra prostration and that does not invalidate the prayer. And this is something for which a puzzle is made: a person praying left the final sitting and tied the fifth with a prostration and his prayer was not invalidated, and a person praying sat and his sitting was not considered and his prayer was invalidated by leaving it. And he restricted by saying 'and the people did not know' because in al-Mujtaba: if the Imam returned to the sitting before the prostration and the follower prostrated intentionally, it invalidates, and in forgetfulness there is a difference, and the precaution is to repeat. And in Fath al-Qadir: it is not hidden that they do not follow him when he stood before the sitting, and when he returns he does not repeat the tashahhud.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a scenario where the imam inadvertently stands for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah prayer (e.g., Zuhr) but returns to the sitting before performing the sajdah (prostration) of that fifth rak'ah. The imam's return annuls his extra bowing, and since the followers' bowing is built upon his, theirs is also annulled. Thus, any extra prostration they performed does not invalidate their prayer; it is merely an extra sajdah, which is not harmful. The passage also notes that this applies whether the follower is a masbuq (someone who missed part of the prayer) or mudrik (someone who caught up with the imam). The text then presents a puzzle: a person who abandoned the final sitting and performed the fifth rak'ah's sajdah may have his prayer upheld, while a person who sat but whose sitting was not considered (because he stood again) may have his prayer invalidated. The key is that if the imam returns before the sajdah, the followers' prayer remains valid; if they prostrate intentionally after his return, it may invalidate, but if done forgetfully, there is a difference of opinion. The precaution is to repeat. Finally, it cites Fath al-Qadir that followers do not follow the imam when he stands before the sitting, and when he returns he does not repeat the tashahhud.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness or mistakes in prayer.
مأموم (ma'mum): Follower praying behind an imam.
مسبوق (masbuq): Follower who missed one or more rak'ahs and joins the imam late.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam stands for a fifth rak'ah in Zuhr but returns to the sitting before performing sajdah, and the followers (who were unaware) prostrate, what is the status of their prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Their prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Their prayer remains valid despite the extra prostration.
C) Their prayer is valid only if they did not make the extra prostration intentionally.
D) Their prayer becomes nafl (supererogatory).

Key Takeaway
The followers' prayer remains valid because the imam's return annuls the extra bowing, leaving only an extra sajdah which does not invalidate.

Adding a Sixth Rak'ah When Prayer Becomes Nafl
Ruling on adding a sixth rak'ah to an accidental nafl prayer from missing qa'dah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on adding a sixth rak'ah when a four-rak'ah fard prayer becomes nafl accidentally, and distinguish between the views of the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad on this issue.

Core Idea
When a fard prayer accidentally becomes nafl, add a sixth rak'ah to avoid odd-numbered nafl, but it is recommended, not obligatory.

Imagine leading a four-rak'ah prayer and by mistake you stand for a fifth rak'ah without completing the tashahhud. Your fard prayer has now turned into a nafl. What should you do? The Hanafi school has a nuanced ruling: you can salvage the prayer by adding a sixth rak'ah to make it an even-numbered nafl, but scholars differ on whether this addition is obligatory or merely recommended. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Recognize the scenario: an imam leading a four-rak'ah fard prayer mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah without performing the first sitting (qa'dah). The prayer loses its obligatory status and becomes nafl.
This transformation is based on the principle that the essence of the prayer remains, but the description (fard) is lost.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the imam should add a sixth rak'ah to the nafl prayer to make it even (shaf'), because nafl should be performed in pairs, not odd numbers.
The prohibition of odd-numbered nafl is a key point.
3
Analyze the intra-school dispute
Imam Muhammad (in another report) held that the prayer is completely invalid because the fundamental error (increasing the prayer by a rak'ah) cannot be rectified. Thus, no sixth rak'ah is needed; the prayer must be restarted.
This disagreement is based on the principle of 'invalidation of description does not entail invalidation of essence' versus a stricter view.
4
Evaluate the preferred view
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows the Sahibayn. The addition of a sixth rak'ah is considered mandub (recommended), not wajib (obligatory), because the prohibition of odd nafl applies only when intended.
Al-Quduri's wording suggests obligation, but the majority consider it recommended.
5
Apply exceptions
Note that this ruling applies to most prayers except for 'Asr and Fajr. For 'Asr, adding a sixth is disliked because it falls before Maghrib; for Fajr, it is disliked because voluntary prayers before and after Fajr are discouraged.
These exceptions are based on the general dislike of nafl during those times.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فصارت نفلاً فيضم إليها سادسة لما سبق مراراً من أنه لا يلزم من بطلان الوصف بطلان الأصل عندهما خلافاً لمحمد فيضم سادسة لأن التنفل بالوتر غير مشروع ولو لم يضم فلا شيء عليه لأنه ظان وشروعه ليس بملزم وإذا اقتدى به إنسان في الخامسة ثم أفسدها فعلى قول محمد لا يتصور القضاء، وعندهما يقضي ستاً لشروعه في تحريمة الست بخلاف ما إذا عاد الإمام قبل السجدة فإنه يقضي أربعاً. ثم صرح المصنف في الوافي بأن السادسة مندوب وتركه في المختصر للاختلاف. وفي عبارة القدوري تبعاً لرواية الأصل إشارة إلى الوجوب فإنه قال : وكان عليه أن يضم إليها ركعة سادسة ووجهه في فتح القدير بعدم جواز التنفل بالوتر . وفي المبسوط وأحب إلي أن يشفع الخامسة لأن النفل شرع شفعاً لا وتراً. كذا في البدائع والأظهر الندب لأن عدم جواز التنفل بالوتر إنما هو عند القصد، أما عند عدمه فلا ولهذا لا يلزمه شيء لو قطعه . وفي السراج الوهاج : إن ضم السادسة سائر الصلوات إلا في العصر فإنه لا يضم إليها لأنه يكون تطوعاً قبل المغرب وذلك مكروه، وفي قاضيخان إلا الفجر فإنه لا يضيف إليها لأن التنفل قبلها وبعدها مكروه اهـ.
His saying: (so it becomes nafl, so he adds a sixth to it) due to what has preceded repeatedly: that the invalidation of the description does not necessitate the invalidation of the essence according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad (in another version?) so he adds a sixth because performing nafl with an odd number is not legislated. And if he does not add, nothing is upon him because he is a conjecturer (zann) and his commencement is not binding. And if a person follows him in the fifth and then he invalidates it, according to Muhammad's view, making up (the prayer) is not conceivable, and according to the two, he makes up six because of his commencement of the tahrimah of six, unlike if the imam returned before the prostration, then he makes up four. Then the author explicitly stated in al-Wafi that the sixth is mandub (recommended) and he omitted it in al-Mukhtasar due to disagreement. And in the expression of al-Quduri, following the original narration, there is an indication of obligation (wujub) for he said: 'It is upon him to add a sixth rak'ah to it' and its justification in Fath al-Qadir is the impermissibility of performing nafl with an odd number. And in al-Mabsut: 'I prefer that he make the fifth even (i.e., add a sixth) because nafl is legislated as even, not odd.' Similarly in al-Bada'i. And the most apparent is recommendation (nadb) because the impermissibility of performing nafl with an odd number is only when intended, but when not intended, then it is not, and therefore nothing is required of him if he cuts it. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: He adds the sixth for all prayers except for 'Asr, because it would be a voluntary prayer before Maghrib which is disliked, and in Qadikhan except for Fajr, because voluntary prayer before and after it is disliked.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer (like Zuhr) inadvertently becomes nafl (supererogatory) due to the imam performing a fifth rak'ah and not returning. The central issue is whether to add a sixth rak'ah to make the prayer even (as nafl should be performed in pairs). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two), the essence of the prayer is not invalidated when the description (obligatory) is lost; therefore, the prayer becomes nafl and a sixth rak'ah is added to avoid an odd number (witriyyah) which is not legislated for nafl. Muhammad (al-Shaybani) initially disagreed but the relied-upon position of the two is followed. The passage then mentions that al-Quduri's wording suggests wujub (obligation) while other authorities like al-Mabsut consider it mandub (recommended). The preferred view (azhar) is that it is recommended, not obligatory, because the prohibition of odd-numbered nafl applies only when one intends it from the start; here it is accidental. The passage also notes exceptions: for 'Asr, adding a sixth is disliked because it falls in the disliked time for voluntary prayer before Maghrib; for Fajr, according to Qadikhan, it is also excepted because voluntary prayer before and after Fajr is disliked. Thus, the ruling is nuanced with temporal restrictions.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer, here resulting from an intended obligatory prayer that became invalid as fard.
وتر (watr): Odd number; referring to the prohibition of performing nafl as an odd number (without pairing)
مندوب (mandub): Recommended act; not obligatory but rewarding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view (azhar), what is the ruling on adding a sixth rak'ah when a four-rak'ah fard prayer accidentally becomes nafl?
A) It is wajib (obligatory) to add the sixth.
B) It is mandub (recommended) to add the sixth.
C) The prayer should be restarted from the beginning.
D) No action is needed; the prayer is valid as an odd nafl.

Key Takeaway
When a fard prayer accidentally becomes nafl, it is recommended to add a sixth rak'ah to make it even; not adding does not invalidate, but the prohibition of odd nafl applies only when intended.

Imam’s Extra Rak'ah After Final Sitting: Return and Salvage
Ruling on imam who sits at fourth then stands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an imam sits at the fourth rak'ah and then stands, and explain the consequences for followers and the necessity of adding a sixth rak'ah.

Core Idea
An extra rak'ah after the final sitting does not invalidate the fard but requires repair by adding a sixth.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common error in congregational prayer: the imam mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah after already sitting for the final tashahhud. The Hanafi school provides a detailed solution to salvage the prayer without restarting, while also protecting the followers from following an innovation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the error
Recognize that the imam has sat for the final tashahhud of a four-rak'ah prayer (e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr, 'Isha) but then stands, intending a fifth rak'ah.
This is a mistake; the proper final sitting has already occurred.
2
Analyze the first scenario: before prostrating for fifth
If the imam has not yet prostrated for the fifth rak'ah, he must return to the sitting position. He then repeats the tashahhud and completes the prayer with salam.
Salam while standing is invalid; sitting is required.
3
Determine the followers' obligation
If the imam returns, followers return with him. If he continues with the extra rak'ah, followers do not follow because it is a bid'ah (innovation). If the imam returns before completing the fifth with a prostration, followers follow with salam; if he has prostrated, they give salam immediately.
The correct view: no following in bid'ah.
4
Analyze the second scenario: after prostrating for fifth
If the imam has prostrated for the fifth rak'ah, his obligatory prayer is not invalidated but is deficient. He must add a sixth rak'ah to make a pair of two rak'ahs, transforming them into a nafl prayer.
A single rak'ah of nafl is prohibited; pairing is required.
5
Complete the prayer with sujud al-sahw
After adding the sixth rak'ah, the imam performs tashahhud, salam, and then sujud al-sahw. These two rak'ahs do not count as the sunnah of Zuhr; they are separate nafl.
Sujud al-sahw is wajib here because the prayer sequence was altered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وإن قعد في الرابعة ثم قام عاد وسلم لأن التسليم في حالة القيام غير مشروع وأمكنه الإقامة على وجهه بالقعود لأن ما دون الركعة بمحل الرفض، ثم إذا عاد يعيد التشهد وكذا لو نام قاعداً وقال الناطفي : يعيد ثم قيل القوم يتبعونه فإن عاد عادوا معه وإن مضى في النافلة اتبعوه لأن صلاتهم تمت بالقعود والصحيح أنهم لا يتبعونه لأنه لا اتباع في البدعة فإن عاد قبل تقييد الخامسة بالسجدة اتبعوه بالسلام فإن قيد سلموا في الحال . قوله ( وإن سجد للخامسة تم فرضه وضم إليه سادسة أي لم يفسد فرضه بسجوده كما فسد فيما إذا لم يقعد هذا هو المراد بالتمام وإلا فصلاته ناقصة كما سيأتي. وإنما لم يفسد لأن الباقي إصابة لفظ السلام وهي واجبة وإنما يضم إليها أخرى لتصير الركعتان له نقلاً للنهي عن الركعة الواحدة، وإذا ضم فإنه يتشهد ويسلم ثم يسجد للسهو كما سيأتي ثم لا ينوبان عن سنة الظهر وهو الصحيح لأن المواظبة عليهما إنما كانت بتحريمة مبتدأه. أطلق في الضم فشمل ما إذا كان في وقت مكروه كما بعد الفجر والعصر لأن التطوع إنما يكره ...
His saying: (And if he sat in the fourth then stood, he returns and says salam) because giving salam while standing is not legislated, and he can maintain his prayer in a proper manner by sitting, because less than a rak'ah is subject to annulment. Then if he returns, he repeats the tashahhud. Similarly if he sleeps while sitting, and al-Natifi said: he repeats. Then it was said: the people follow him; if he returns, they return with him; and if he continues in the supererogatory prayer, they follow him because their prayer is completed by the sitting. But the correct view is that they do not follow him because there is no following in innovation. If he returns before completing the fifth with a prostration, they follow him with salam; if he completes it, they give salam immediately. His saying: (And if he prostrates for the fifth, his obligatory prayer is completed and he adds a sixth to it) meaning his obligatory prayer is not invalidated by his prostration, unlike the case when he did not sit; that is what is meant by completion, otherwise his prayer is deficient as will come later. It is not invalidated because the remaining is the utterance of salam, which is wajib, and he adds another to it to make the two rak'ahs nafl for him due to the prohibition of a single rak'ah. When he adds, he performs tashahhud and salam then prostrates for forgetfulness as will come, and these two do not serve as the sunnah of Zuhr, and that is the correct view because the regular performance of them was with a new tahrimah. He made the addition general, so it includes when it is in a disliked time like after Fajr and 'Asr because voluntary prayer is disliked...
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage addresses multiple scenarios. First, if the imam sits for the fourth rak'ah (the obligatory sitting at the end of a four-rak'ah prayer) but then stands up (thinking it is not the last), he must return to the sitting and complete the prayer by giving salam, because salam while standing is not valid. He must repeat the tashahhud because his standing disrupted the sitting. Regarding followers: if the imam returns, they return with him; if he continues, they do not follow him in the extra rak'ah because it is an innovation (bid'ah). However, if the imam returns before tying the fifth rak'ah with a prostration, the followers follow him with salam; if he prostrates, they give salam immediately. Second, if the imam prostrates for the fifth rak'ah (after the fourth sitting), the text says his fard (obligatory prayer) is 'completed' (tamma) meaning it is not invalidated, but it is deficient. He must add a sixth rak'ah to make the two extra rak'ahs a nafl pair, because performing a single rak'ah as nafl is prohibited. He then performs tashahhud, salam, and sujud al-sahw. Importantly, these two rak'ahs do not count as the sunnah of Zuhr; they are a separate nafl. The addition of the sixth is general, even in disliked times (e.g., after Fajr or 'Asr), though voluntary prayer at those times is disliked.

Key Terms
قيام (qiyam): Standing in prayer; here, the imam standing for a fifth rak'ah after sitting.
بدعة (bid'ah): Innovation; the extra rak'ah performed after the obligatory sitting is considered a deviation.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness, required here after completing the nafl addition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an imam sits for the fourth rak'ah (final sitting) but then stands up and performs the fifth rak'ah's prostration, what should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) He should immediately stop and restart the prayer.
B) He should add a sixth rak'ah and then perform sujud al-sahw.
C) He should complete the fifth and give salam without adding.
D) He should sit back down and give salam immediately.

Key Takeaway
An imam who adds an extra rak'ah after the final sitting must salvage the prayer by adding a sixth if he prostrates; followers must not follow him in the innovation.
