Complete Rulings on Standing for a Fifth Rak'ah
Rules for standing for a fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios when a person stands for a fifth rak'ah and identify the correct remedy for each scenario, including the follower's case.

Core Idea
If you prostrate for a fifth rak'ah, add a sixth; if not, return and say salam.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the rulings when a worshipper mistakenly or deliberately stands for a fifth rak'ah. The key distinction is whether the fifth rak'ah was tied with a prostration. The correct response preserves the validity of the fard prayer and avoids the prohibition of a single rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main scenarios
Determine whether the person prostrated for the fifth rak'ah or not. This is the turning point that decides the ruling.
Standing alone does not invalidate; only the prostration triggers the need to add a sixth.
2
Analyze the scenario without prostration
If the person stood but has not yet prostrated, he must return to sitting and say salam. The standing is treated as an increase of less than a rak'ah, which is void.
Returning requires repeating the tashahhud. No sujud al-sahw is needed.
3
Analyze the scenario with prostration
If the person prostrated for the fifth, his fard is completed. He must add a sixth rak'ah to make a pair, then say salam and perform sujud al-sahw.
The added two rak'ahs are nafl and do not substitute for the sunnah of the fard.
4
Examine the follower's situation
When a follower joins an imam who is in the fifth rak'ah, there is an intra-Hanafi difference. Abu Yusuf says the follower prays 2 rak'ahs; Muhammad says 6.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Muhammad's view of 6 rak'ahs.
5
Understand the debates
There is also a dispute on whether adding the sixth is wajib or mustahabb. The relied-upon view is that it is permissible (la ba'sa bihi), especially in disliked times.
This flexibility shows the Hanafi concern for removing hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيضم إليها سادسة وإن قعد في الرابعة ثم قام عاد وسلم وإن سجد للخامسة تم فرضه الصحيح أنه لو قعد على رأس الرابعة وقام إلى الخامسة وقيدها بسجدة فإنه يضم سادسة ولو كان في الأوقات المكروهة فينبغي أن لا يكره هنا أيضاً على الصحيح إذ لا فرق بينهما، ولم يذكر المصنف سجود السهود لأن الأصح عدمه لأن النقصان بالفساد لا ينجبر بالسجود. ثم اعلم أنه لا فرق في عدم البطلان عند العود قبل السجود والبطلان إن قيد بالسجود بين العمد والسهو ولذا قال في الخلاصة : فإن قام إلى الخامسة عمداً أيضاً لا تفسد ما لم يقيد الخامسة بالسجدة عندنا . ثم اعلم أيضاً أن البطلان بالتقييد بالسجدة أعم من أن يكون قد قرأ في الركعة الخامسة أو لا كما في الخلاصة، وقد يقال : إن المفسد خلط النفل بالفرض قبل إكماله والركعة بلا قراءة في النفل غير صحيحة فلم يوجد الخلط فكان زيادة ما دون الركعة وهو ليس بمفسد قوله : (وإن قعد في الرابعة ثم قام عاد وسلم لأن التسليم في حالة القيام غير مشروع وأمكنه الإقامة على وجهه بالقعود لأن ما دون الركعة بمحل الرفض، ثم إذا عاد يعيد التشهد وكذا لو نام قاعداً وقال الناطفي : يعيد ثم قيل القوم يتبعونه فإن عاد عادوا معه وإن مضى في النافلة اتبعوه لأن صلاتهم تمت ،بالقعدة والصحيح أنهم لا يتبعونه لأنه لا اتباع في البدعة فإن عاد قبل تقييد الخامسة بالسجدة اتبعوه بالسلام فإن قيد سلموا في الحال . قوله : ( وإن سجد للخامسة تم فرضه وضم إليه سادسة أي لم يفسد فرضه بسجوده كما فسد فيما إذا لم يقعد هذا ا هو المراد بالتمام وإلا فصلاته ناقصة كما سيأتي. وإنما لم يفسد لأن الباقي إصابة لفظ السلام وهي واجبة وإنما يضم إليها أخرى لتصير الركعتان له نقلاً للنهي عن الركعة الواحدة، وإذا ضم فإنه يتشهد ويسلم ثم يسجد للسهو كما سيأتي ثم لا ينوبان عن سنة الظهر وهو الصحيح لأن المواظبة عليهما إنما كانت بتحريمة مبتدأه. أطلق في الضم فشمل ما إذا كان في وقت مكروه كما بعد الفجر والعصر لأن التطوع إنما يكره أو ظهراً بعد العصر فإنه لا يضم كما هو ظاهر، وعليه فيصح التوجيه والله تعالى الموفق ا هـ . أقول : فعلى زيادته الظهر لا يظهر اقتصار السراج على زيادته العصر، والذي يظهر أن استثناء السراج بالنظر إلى المسألة الآتية وهي ما لو قعد على رأس الرابعة ثم قام وإليه يشير تعليله فتدبره. كذا في شرح الشيخ إسماعيل . قلت : هذا غير ظاهر إذ لو كان كذلك لذكرها في محلها مع أنه ذكرها هنا ولكن قد يرتكب ذلك تصحيحاً لكلامه لعلو مقامه هذا. وقال في شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج قلت : وأما المغرب إذا لم يقعد على الثالثة منها وقيد الرابعة بالسجدة يقطع عليها ولا يضم إليها أخرى لنصهم على كراهة التنفل قبلها وعلى كراهته بالوتر مطلقاً اهـ. قوله : (وقد يقال الخ) قال في النهر : ويؤيده أن السجود الخالي عن الركوع لا يعتد به فكذا الخالي عن القراءة إلا أن يفرق بأنه قد عهد إتمام الركعة دون القراءة كما في المقتدي بخلاف الخالية عن الركوع . ما مر من قوله : (لأن التسليم الخ قال في النهر : ومع ذلك لو سلم قائماً صح كما في الخلاصة قوله : فيهما إذا كان عن اختيار أما إذا لم يكن عن اختيار فلا وعليه الاعتماد. وكذا في الخانية وهو الصحيح. كذا في التبيين وعليه الفتوى كذا في المجتبى لكن اختلف في الضم في غير وقت الكراهة قيل بالوجوب وقيل بالاستحباب كما قدمناه وأما في وقت الكراهة فقيل بالكراهة والمعتمد المصحح أنه لا بأس به كما عبروا به بمعنى أن الأولى تركه فظاهره أنه لم يقل أحد بوجوبه ولا باستحبابه وفرق الشارح بين الفجر والعصر فصحح أنه لا يكره في العصر وجزم بالكراهة في الصبح وفيه نظر، إذ لا فرق بين الفجر والعصر فكما صحح عدمها في العصر لزمه تصحيح عدمها في الفجر ولذا سوى بينهما في فتح القدير وقال : والنهي عن التنفل القصدي بعدهما ولذا إذا تطوع من آخر الليل فلما صلى ركعة طلع الفجر الأول أن يتمها ثم يصلي ركعتي الفجر لأنه لم يتنفل بأكثر من ركعتي الفجر قصداً اهـ. وصرح في التجنيس بأن الفتوى على رواية هشام من عدم الفرق بين الصبح والعصر في عدم كراهة الضم وإن لم يتم الركعتين نفلاً فلا شيء عليه كما قدمناه. وفي المحيط : وإن شرع معه رجل في الخامسة يصلي ركعتين عند أبي يوسف وعند محمد ستاً بناءاً على أن إحرام الفرض انقطع بالانتقال إلى النفل عند أبي يوسف لأن من ضرورة الانتقال إلى النفل انقطاع الفرض فلم يصح شارعاً إلا في هذا الشفع، وعند محمد لم ينقطع إحرام الفرض وهو الأصح لأنه صار شارعاً في النفل من غير تكبيرة جديدة، ولو انقطعت التحريمة لاحتاج إلى تكبيرة جديدة لأن الإحرام الجديد لا ينعقد إلا بتكبيرة جديدة، ولما بقيت التحريمة صار شارعاً في الكل. ولو قطع المقتدي هذا النفل قال محمد : لا شيء عليه لأنها غير مضمونة على الإمام فلا تصير مضمونة على المقتدي. وقال أبو يوسف : يلزمه قضاء ركعتين وهو الأصح لأن النفل مضمون في الأصل وإنما لم يصر مضموناً على الإمام هنا لعارض وهو شروعه فيه ساهياً، وقد انعدم هذا العارض في حق المقتدي فبقيت صلاة الإمام مضمونة في حق المقتدي بخلاف اقتداء البالغ بالصبي في النوافل فلا يصح عند عامة المشايخ لأن التطوع إنما لم يصر مضموناً على الصبا بأمر أصلي وهو الصبى فلا يمكن أن يجعل معدوماً في حق المقتدي فبقي بمنزلة اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل اهـ. فالحاصل أن المصحح قول محمد في كونه يصلي ستاً وقول أبي يوسف في لزوم القضاء على المقتدي. والمعتمد المصحح أنه لا بأس به قال في النهر : وعلى هذا فالأولى أن يكون معنى ضم أي جاز له الضم ليعم كل وقت وإلا يخرج عن كلامه بتقدير حمله على الندب والوجوب وقت الكراهة ا هـ . وقد يقال : إن مرادهم الندب لأن الصلاة أقل مراتبها الاستحباب لا الإباحة بدليل ما يأتي من أنه إذا تطوع فصلى ركعة ثم طلع الفجر فالأولى أن يتمها وإنما عبروا هنا بـ لا بأس لأن الوقت المكروه هنا محل توهم أن في الصلاة فيه بأساً فعبروا بـ لا بأس للدلالة على أنه لا يكره التطوع فيه وذلك لا ينافي أن الإتمام أفضل كما هو ظاهر إطلاق قولهم وضم سادسة لشموله الوقت المكروه وتأمل.
He adds a sixth to it. If he sat in the fourth then stood, he returns and says salam. If he prostrated for the fifth, his fard is completed, and he adds a sixth. The correct view is that if he sat at the end of the fourth and stood for the fifth and tied it with a prostration, he adds a sixth. Even in disliked times, it should not be disliked here according to the correct view, as there is no difference. The author did not mention Sujud al-Sahw because the correct view is its absence, since the deficiency due to corruption is not compensated by prostration. Know that there is no difference in the absence of invalidation when returning before prostration and invalidation if tied with prostration between deliberate and forgetful. In al-Khulasa: if he deliberately stands for the fifth, it does not invalidate as long as he does not tie the fifth with prostration according to us. Also, invalidation by tying with prostration is general whether he read in the fifth rak'ah or not. It may be said: the invalidator is mixing nafl with fard before its completion, and a rak'ah without recitation in nafl is invalid, so no mixing occurred, and it is an increase of less than a rak'ah, which is not invalidating. His statement: 'If he sat in the fourth then stood, he returns and says salam' because the salam while standing is not legislated and he can perform it properly by sitting, because less than a rak'ah is subject to rejection. Then if he returns, he repeats the tashahhud, similarly if he slept sitting. Al-Natifi said: he repeats. Then it is said: the people follow him; if he returns, they return with him; if he continues in the nafl, they follow him because their prayer is completed with the sitting. The correct view is that they do not follow him because there is no following in innovation. If he returns before tying the fifth with prostration, they follow him with salam; if he ties it, they say salam immediately. His statement: 'If he prostrates for the fifth, his fard is completed and he adds a sixth' means his fard is not invalidated by his prostration as it would be invalidated if he did not sit. This is the meaning of completion; otherwise his prayer is imperfect as will come. It is not invalidated because the remaining is uttering the word of salam, which is wajib. He only adds another to make the two rak'ahs nafl for him, due to the prohibition of a single rak'ah. When he adds, he recites tashahhud, says salam, then prostrates for forgetfulness as will come. Then these two do not substitute for the sunnah of zuhr – this is the correct view because the continuity of them was only with a new beginning intention. The statement 'he adds' is general, including when in a disliked time like after Fajr and Asr because nafl is disliked. Or zuhr after Asr: he does not add as is apparent. Upon this, the guidance is sound. I say: regarding increasing zuhr, the restriction of al-Siraj to increasing Asr is not apparent. It appears that al-Siraj's exception considers the coming issue of one who sat at the end of the fourth then stood. So reflect. Similarly in the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il. I say: this is not apparent; if it were so, he would have mentioned it in its place, but he mentioned it here. However, this may be done to correct his statement due to his high status. In Sharh al-Munya by Ibn Amir Hajj, I say: As for Maghrib, if he did not sit at the third and tied the fourth with prostration, he stops it and does not add another because of their texts on the dislike of nafl before it and the absolute dislike of witr. His statement: 'It may be said etc.' In al-Nahr: it is supported that prostration without bowing is not considered, so similarly without recitation, except that there is a distinction: completion of a rak'ah without recitation has been experienced in the case of a follower, unlike without bowing. What passed from his statement: 'Because the salam etc.' In al-Nahr: despite that, if he says salam while standing, it is valid as in al-Khulasa. His statement: 'In the two, if it is by choice, then if not by choice, no, and upon it is reliance. Similarly in al-Khaniyya, and it is the correct view. Similarly in al-Tabyin, and upon it is fatwa, similarly in al-Mujtaba. But there is disagreement on adding in non-disliked time: some say obligation, some say recommendation as we presented. As for disliked time, some say dislike, and the relied-upon correct view is that there is no harm (la ba'sa bihi) as they expressed, meaning that leaving it is better. So apparently no one said obligation or recommendation. The commentator distinguished between Fajr and Asr, affirming no dislike in Asr and affirming dislike in Fajr – this is debatable, as there is no difference. So as he affirmed no dislike in Asr, he must affirm no dislike in Fajr. Hence al-Fath al-Qadir equated them, saying: The prohibition is of deliberate nafl after them. Therefore, if one prays nafl at the end of the night and after one rak'ah the true dawn appears, it is better to complete it and then pray the two rak'ahs of Fajr because he did not intend more than two Fajr rak'ahs. Al-Tajnīs states the fatwa is on Hisham's narration of no difference between Fajr and Asr regarding no dislike of adding, and if he does not complete the two rak'ahs as nafl, nothing is upon him as we presented. And in al-Muhit: If a man joins him in the fifth, he prays two rak'ahs according to Abu Yusuf and six according to Muhammad, based on whether the fard ihram is cut off by transitioning to nafl. According to Abu Yusuf, it is cut off because the necessity of transitioning to nafl is the cutoff of fard, so he only starts in this pair. According to Muhammad, the fard ihram is not cut off, which is the correct view, because he started the nafl without a new takbir. If the ihram were cut off, he would need a new takbir, as a new ihram cannot be contracted except with a new takbir. Since the ihram remains, he starts in all. If the follower cuts this nafl, Muhammad says: nothing upon him because it is not guaranteed (ghayr madmun) upon the imam, so it does not become guaranteed upon the follower. Abu Yusuf says: he must make up two rak'ahs, and this is the correct view, because nafl is originally guaranteed; it only became not guaranteed upon the imam here due to a temporary cause (his forgetful starting), and this cause is absent for the follower, so the imam's prayer remains guaranteed for the follower, unlike an adult following a child in nafl – that is invalid according to general scholars because nafl is not guaranteed upon the child due to an original matter (childhood), so it cannot be considered non-existent for the follower, remaining like a muqtadi following a mutanaffil. So the summary: the correct (musahhah) is Muhammad's saying that he prays six, and Abu Yusuf's saying that the follower must make up. The relied-upon correct view is that there is no harm. In al-Nahr: based on this, it is better that the meaning of 'add' is that it is permissible for him to add, to cover all times, otherwise his statement would deviate if taken as recommendation or obligation in disliked times. It may be said: their intent is recommendation because the least rank of prayer is recommendation, not permissibility, as evidenced by what comes: if one prays nafl and after one rak'ah dawn appears, it is better to complete it. They only used 'no harm' here because the disliked time is a place of misconception that there is harm in praying in it, so they used 'no harm' to indicate that nafl is not disliked in it, and that does not contradict completion being better, as is apparent from the generality of their statement 'and adds a sixth' encompassing the disliked time. Reflect.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on what happens when a person in prayer stands for a fifth rak'ah, whether deliberately or forgetfully. The commentary explains two main scenarios. First, if the person stands for a fifth rak'ah after sitting at the end of the fourth but has not yet prostrated for that fifth, he must return to sitting and say the salam. This is because salam is not valid while standing, and it is possible to complete the prayer properly by sitting. Upon returning, he must repeat the tashahhud. Second, if he already prostrates for the fifth, his fard prayer is not invalidated; rather, he completes it by adding a sixth rak'ah to make a pair, avoiding the prohibition of praying a single rak'ah. The added two rak'ahs are nafl and do not substitute for the sunnah of the original fard prayer. The passage also addresses the case when this happens in a disliked time (like after Fajr or Asr). The correct position is that it is not disliked to add the sixth, although leaving it is preferable. There is disagreement on whether adding the sixth is obligatory or recommended, but the relied-upon view is that it is permissible. Finally, the passage discusses the situation where a person joins the imam who is in the fifth rak'ah. According to Abu Yusuf, the follower prays two rak'ahs because the imam's fard ihram is considered broken. According to Muhammad, the follower prays six rak'ahs because the imam's original ihram remains, so the follower joins the same prayer. The relied-upon view is Muhammad's opinion.

Key Terms
ضم سادسة (ḍamm sādīsa): Adding a sixth rak'ah to the prayer when one has mistakenly prayed a fifth.
التقييد بالسجدة (al-taqyīd bi al-sajda): Performing the prostration of the extra rak'ah, which determines whether the prayer is invalidated or requires adding a sixth.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed at the end of the prayer to compensate for errors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person sits at the end of the fourth rak'ah of Zuhr prayer, then forgetfully stands up and prostrates for a fifth rak'ah, what must he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) He should return to sitting and say salam, then repeat the prayer.
B) He should add a sixth rak'ah, then say salam and perform prostration of forgetfulness.
C) He should continue the prayer as five rak'ah and then perform prostration of forgetfulness.
D) He must repeat the entire prayer from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
If you prostrate for a fifth rak'ah, add a sixth; if you haven't prostrated, return and say salam.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Adding a Sixth Rak'ah and the Follower's Prayer When Imam Stands for Fifth
Explains rulings on adding a sixth and follower's prayer in forgetful fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on adding a sixth rak'ah (wajib only for deliberate action) and the number of rak'ahs a follower must pray when joining the imam in the fifth, including the relied-upon tarjih.

Core Idea
When the imam stands for a fifth rak'ah, the prayer becomes voluntary; the follower's rak'ahs depend on whether the consecration remains.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common scenario in congregational prayer: the imam forgetfully stands for a fifth rak'ah after the fourth. It first clarifies when adding a sixth is required and whether it is disliked in certain times. Then it delves into a more complex situation: if a follower joins the imam during that fifth rak'ah, how many rak'ahs does he pray? The Hanafi school has two clear positions on this, and later authorities have resolved which to follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling on adding a sixth
Determine whether the imam's action was deliberate or forgetful. If deliberate, adding a sixth is wajib; if forgetful, it is not required. This is the relied-upon view.
The text states 'if it was by choice' vs 'not by choice'.
2
Analyze the ikhtilaf about dislike in disliked times
Some said adding a sixth is disliked in disliked times (Fajr, Asr), but the correct view (relied upon) is that it is not disliked, though leaving it is better. The fatwa follows Hisham's narration, making no distinction between Fajr and Asr.
The commentator's attempt to distinguish is rejected.
3
Understand the follower's situation when joining in the fifth
When a follower joins the imam during the fifth rak'ah (forgetfully started), there are two opinions: Abu Yusuf says he prays two rak'ahs; Muhammad says six. The difference hinges on whether the original consecration (ihram) for the fard is considered terminated.
Abu Yusuf: transition to voluntary ends fard consecration. Muhammad: no new takbir, so consecration remains.
4
Learn the tarjih (preferred view) for the follower's case
Muhammad's view on the number of rak'ahs (six) is considered more correct (al-asahh). However, if the follower cuts his voluntary prayer, Abu Yusuf's view that he must make up two rak'ahs is the fatwa (ala al-fatwa).
Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj affirms the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view for make-up.
5
Consider the condition of the imam's qa'dah (sitting) for tashahhud
If the imam sat for the amount of tashahhud in the fourth rak'ah and then stood for the fifth, a follower's following is invalid because the imam has entered voluntary prayer before the follower joins. If he did not sit, following is valid because the imam is still in the fard.
This is a separate condition affecting validity of the follower's prayer.

كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو فيهما إذا كان عن اختيار أما إذا لم يكن عن اختيار فلا وعليه الاعتماد. وكذا في الخانية وهو الصحيح. كذا في التبيين وعليه الفتوى كذا في المجتبى لكن اختلف في الضم في غير وقت الكراهة قيل بالوجوب وقيل بالاستحباب كما قدمناه وأما في وقت الكراهة فقيل بالكراهة والمعتمد المصحح أنه لا بأس به كما عبروا به بمعنى أن الأولى تركه فظاهره أنه لم يقل أحد بوجوبه ولا باستحبابه وفرق الشارح بين الفجر والعصر فصحح أنه لا يكره في العصر وجزم بالكراهة في الصبح وفيه نظر، إذ لا فرق بين الفجر والعصر فكما صحح عدمها في العصر لزمه تصحيح عدمها في الفجر ولذا سوى بينهما في فتح القدير وقال : والنهي عن التنفل القصدي بعدهما ولذا إذا تطوع من آخر الليل فلما صلى ركعة طلع الفجر الأول أن يتمها ثم يصلي ركعتي الفجر لأنه لم يتنفل بأكثر من ركعتي الفجر قصداً اهـ. وصرح في التجنيس بأن الفتوى على رواية هشام من عدم الفرق بين الصبح والعصر في عدم كراهة الضم وإن لم يتم الركعتين نفلاً فلا شيء عليه كما قدمناه. وفي المحيط : وإن شرع معه رجل في الخامسة يصلي ركعتين عند أبي يوسف وعند محمد ستاً بناءاً على أن إحرام الفرض انقطع بالانتقال إلى النفل عند أبي يوسف لأن من ضرورة الانتقال إلى النفل انقطاع الفرض فلم يصح شارعاً إلا في هذا الشفع، وعند محمد لم ينقطع إحرام الفرض وهو الأصح لأنه صار شارعاً في النفل من غير تكبيرة جديدة، ولو انقطعت التحريمة لاحتاج إلى تكبيرة جديدة لأن الإحرام الجديد لا ينعقد إلا بتكبيرة جديدة، ولما بقيت التحريمة صار شارعاً في الكل. ولو قطع المقتدي هذا النفل قال محمد : لا شيء عليه لأنها غير مضمونة على الإمام فلا تصير مضمونة على المقتدي. وقال أبو يوسف : يلزمه قضاء ركعتين وهو الأصح لأن النفل مضمون في الأصل وإنما لم يصر مضموناً على الإمام هنا لعارض وهو شروعه فيه ساهياً، وقد انعدم هذا العارض في حق المقتدي فبقيت صلاة الإمام مضمونة في حق المقتدي بخلاف اقتداء البالغ بالصبي في النوافل فلا يصح عند عامة المشايخ لأن التطوع إنما لم يصر مضموناً على الصبا بأمر أصلي وهو الصبى فلا يمكن أن يجعل معدوماً في حق المقتدي فبقي بمنزلة اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل اهـ. فالحاصل أن المصحح قول محمد في كونه يصلي ستاً وقول أبي يوسف في لزوم ركعتين لو أفسدها. وفي السراج الوهاج وعليه الفتوى وقد قدمنا أنه إذا اقتدى به في الخامسة ولم يكن قعد الإمام قدر التشهد ولم يعد فإنه يلزمه الست والفرق بين المسألتين أن المسألة الأولى التزم صلاة الإمام وهي ست ركعات نفلاً والشروع في النفل لا يوجب أكثر من ركعتين إلا بالاقتداء، وههنا الإمام لم يكن متنفلاً إلا بركعتين فلزم المأموم ركعتان. وفي السراج الوهاج : إذا قعد في الرابعة قدر التشهد وقام إلى الخامسة ساهياً واقتدى به رجل لا يصح اقتداؤه ولو عاد إلى القعدة لأنه لما قام إلى الخامسة فقد شرع في النفل فكان اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل ولو لم يقعد مقدار التشهد صح الاقتداء لأنه لم يخرج من الفرض قبل أن يقيدها بسجدة اهـ .
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. In both [cases] if it was by choice, but if it was not by choice then no [need to add] and on it is reliance. Likewise in al-Khaniyah and it is correct. Likewise in al-Tabyin and on it is the fatwa, likewise in al-Mujtaba. But there is disagreement regarding adding [a sixth] outside the disliked time: some said obligatory, some said recommended as we mentioned earlier. And regarding the disliked time, some said it is disliked, and the relied-upon correct [view] is that there is no harm in it, as they expressed, meaning that leaving it is better. Its apparent meaning is that no one said it is obligatory nor recommended. The commentator distinguished between Fajr and Asr, deeming it not disliked in Asr and stating definitely that it is disliked in Fajr, but there is consideration [of this], for there is no difference between Fajr and Asr: just as he deemed the absence [of dislike] in Asr correct, he must deem its absence in Fajr correct. Hence he made them equal in Fath al-Qadir and said: The prohibition is regarding deliberate supererogatory prayer after them, hence if one prays voluntarily at the end of the night and after one rak‘ah the first dawn appears, he should complete it then pray the two rak‘ahs of Fajr, because he did not voluntarily pray more than two rak‘ahs of Fajr deliberately. End. And he stated explicitly in al-Tajnis that the fatwa is according to the narration of Hisham, of no difference between Fajr and Asr in the absence of dislike of adding, and if he does not complete the two rak‘ahs voluntarily, there is nothing upon him as we mentioned. And in al-Muhit: If a man joins him in the fifth [rak‘ah], he prays two rak‘ahs according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad six, based on the fact that the consecration of the obligatory [prayer] is terminated by the transition to voluntary [prayer] according to Abu Yusuf, because from the necessity of transitioning to voluntary is the termination of the obligatory, so he only became a participant in this pair [of rak‘ahs]. According to Muhammad, the consecration of the obligatory is not terminated, and this is more correct, because he becomes a participant in the voluntary without a new takbir. If the consecration were terminated, he would need a new takbir because a new consecration is only established by a new takbir. Since the consecration remains, he becomes a participant in all [prayers]. And if the follower cuts this voluntary [prayer], Muhammad said: nothing is upon him because it is not guaranteed upon the imam, so it does not become guaranteed upon the follower. Abu Yusuf said: he must make up two rak‘ahs, and this is more correct, because voluntary [prayer] is originally guaranteed, and it only did not become guaranteed upon the imam here due to a hindrance, namely his entering into it forgetfully, and this hindrance is absent with respect to the follower, so the imam‘s prayer remains guaranteed with respect to the follower. Unlike the following of an adult by a minor in supererogatory prayers, for it is not valid according to most shaykhs, because supererogatory [prayer] only did not become guaranteed upon the minor due to an original matter, namely minority, so it cannot be considered non-existent with respect to the follower, so it remains like the following of one who prays obligatory by one who prays voluntary. End. The summary is that the correct view is Muhammad‘s opinion that he prays six, and Abu Yusuf‘s opinion regarding the obligation of two rak‘ahs if he spoils them. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and upon it is the fatwa, and we have presented that if he followed him in the fifth and the imam had not sat for the amount of tashahhud and did not return, then six are obligatory upon him. The difference between the two issues is that in the first issue, the imam‘s prayer is six rak‘ahs voluntarily, and entering into voluntary does not obligate more than two rak‘ahs except by following. Here, the imam was only praying voluntarily two rak‘ahs, so two rak‘ahs are obligatory upon the follower. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he sat in the fourth for the amount of tashahhud and stood for the fifth forgetfully, and a man followed him, his following is not valid, even if he returns to the sitting, because when he stood for the fifth, he entered into voluntary, so it is following of one who prays obligatory by one who prays voluntary. If he did not sit for the amount of tashahhud, the following is valid, because he did not exit the obligatory before he tied it with a prostration. End.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the chapter on prostrations of forgetfulness. It begins by stating the ruling on adding a sixth rak‘ah when the imam mistakenly stands for a fifth: if the imam‘s action was deliberate, he must add a sixth and prostrate for forgetfulness; if it was forgetful, he does not need to add, and this is the relied-upon view. The text then discusses whether adding a sixth is obligatory or recommended outside the disliked times, and whether it is disliked within them. The correct view is that it is not disliked, though leaving it is better; no one held it obligatory or recommended. The commentator tried to distinguish between Fajr and Asr, but this is criticized because the same principle applies to both. The fatwa follows the narration of Hisham, making no distinction between the two prayers. The passage then shifts to a case where a follower joins the imam during the fifth rak‘ah. According to Abu Yusuf, the follower prays only two rak‘ahs because the imam‘s obligatory prayer ended when he stood for the fifth, so only the voluntary pair remains. According to Muhammad, the follower prays six rak‘ahs because the original consecration for the fard is still intact, and the follower joins in the entire prayer as voluntary. The tarjih (preference) is that Muhammad‘s view is correct regarding the number of rak‘ahs, but Abu Yusuf‘s view is correct regarding the follower‘s obligation to make up two rak‘ahs if he cuts the voluntary prayer. The text ends with another case from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if the imam sits for tashahhud in the fourth and then stands forgetfully, a follower who joins at that point does not have a valid following, because the imam has entered voluntary prayer. If the imam did not sit for tashahhud, the follower‘s following is valid because the imam is still in the fard. This passage covers multiple intra-Hanafi disputes and establishes the operative rulings for the school.

Key Terms
ضم (damm): Adding an extra rak'ah to make the total even (e.g., adding a sixth when the imam mistakenly stands for a fifth).
سجود السهو (sujood al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness (sahw) in prayer.
إحرام (ihram): The consecration (takbirat al-ihram) that marks the beginning of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an imam forgetfully stands for a fifth rak'ah, what is the Hanafi ruling regarding adding a sixth?
A) It is wajib to add a sixth.
B) It is mustahabb to add a sixth.
C) It is not required to add a sixth; the imam should return to sitting.
D) The prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
When the imam forgetfully stands for a fifth rak'ah, no sixth is added; if a follower joins, he prays six rak'ahs (Muhammad's view), and cutting requires making up two (Abu Yusuf's view).

Building Additional Rak'ahs After Sujūd al-Sahw
Ruling on building additional rak'ahs after sujūd al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on building additional rak'ahs after sujūd al-sahw and explain the Hanafi reasoning including the traveler exception.

Core Idea
Building after sujūd al-sahw is valid but disliked; the sujūd must be repeated, except for the traveler.

In this passage from al-Baḥr al-Rā'iq, Ibn Nujaym clarifies a nuanced ruling: after performing the prostration of forgetfulness (sujūd al-sahw) in a prayer, is it permissible to add further rak'ahs? The text explains that while the building is valid (the prayer remains intact), it is disliked (makruh) because the sujūd was performed out of its proper place. A key exception is made for the traveler who intends to settle, where building is permitted to avoid a greater loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: building additional rak'ahs upon a prayer after performing sujūd al-sahw. The base text says 'one does not build', but the commentary clarifies that the building is valid though disliked.
The prohibition is not about validity but about optimal practice.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to the case of a traveler who prostrates for forgetfulness and then intends settlement. In that case, he cannot build upon his two rak'ahs; he must complete four and repeat the sujūd.
This shows that building after sujūd al-sahw is generally not allowed because the sujūd occurred in the middle of the prayer.
3
Understand the traveler exception
If a traveler prostrates for forgetfulness and then intends to settle (i.e., becomes a resident), he is permitted to build additional rak'ahs to complete the full four, even though this violates a wājib, because not doing so would void his entire prayer.
The principle: violating a lesser wājib is tolerated to avoid a greater loss.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a disagreement about whether the sujūd al-sahw must be repeated after building. The chosen view (mukhtār) is that it must be repeated because the original sujūd was performed in the middle of the prayer and is not considered valid.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the validity of the prayer but affects whether compensation is needed.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that building after sujūd al-sahw is not allowed for obligatory prayers (farḍ) and is disliked for supererogatory (nafl). The traveler exception remains. The sujūd al-sahw should be repeated if building occurs.
This is based on the later Hanafi authorities like Ibn Nujaym.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو محمد عن يبني نفلاً عليه وإبطاله لا يجوز لا إذا استلزم تصحيحه نقض ما هو فوقه .اهـ. وإنما قال «لم يبن» ولم يقل «لم يصح البناء لأن البناء صحيح وإن كان مكروهاً لبقاء التحريمة واختلفوا في إعادة سجود السهو والمختار إعادته لأن ما أتى به من السجود وقع في وسط الصلاة فلا يعتد به كالمسافر إذا نوى الإقامة بعدما سجد للسهو ويلزم الأربع ويعيد السجود قيد بشفع التطوع لأنه لو كان مسافراً فسجد للسهو وثم ثوى الإقامة فله ذلك لأنه لو لم يبن وقد لزم الإتمام بنية الإقامة بطلت صلاته، وفي البناء نقض الواجب ونقض الواجب أدنى فيتحمل دفعاً للأعلى لكن يرد على التقييد بشفع التطوع أنه لو صلى فرضاً تاماً وسجد للسهو وثم أراد أن ليس له ذلك لما تقدم، فلو قال فلو سجد في صلاة لم يبن صلاة عليها إلا في المسافر لكان أولى ولذا لم يقيد في الخلاصة بالتطوع وإنما قال : : وإذا صلى ركعتين وسها فيها فسجد لسهوه بعد السلام ثم أراد أن يبني عليها ركعتين لم يكن له ذلك بخلاف المسافر إلا أن يقال : إن الحكم في الفرض يكون بالأولى لأنه يكره البناء على تحريمته، سواء كان سجد للسهو أو لا بخلاف شفع التطوع
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. Muhammad narrated: He builds upon it as supererogatory, and nullifying it is not permissible, except if its correction necessitates overturning what is above it. End. And he said 'he does not build' and did not say 'the building is not valid' because the building is valid though disliked due to the preservation of the consecration (taḥrīma). And they differed regarding repeating the prostration of forgetfulness, and the chosen view is to repeat it because the prostration he performed occurred in the middle of the prayer, so it is not considered, like a traveler who intends to settle after prostrating for forgetfulness: he must perform four rak'ahs and repeat the prostration. He restricted it to an even number of supererogatory (shaf' al-taṭawwu') because if a traveler prostrates for forgetfulness and then intends settlement, he has that permission; because if he did not build and completion became obligatory by the intention of settlement, his prayer would be void. And in building there is a violation of an obligatory act, and violating an obligatory act is lesser, so it is tolerated to repel the greater. But there is an objection to the restriction to even supererogatory: if one prays a complete obligatory prayer and prostrates for forgetfulness and then wants to do otherwise, he does not have that due to what preceded. So if he said: 'If he prostrates in a prayer, he does not build a prayer upon it except in the case of a traveler,' it would be more appropriate, and thus it was not restricted in al-Khulāṣa to supererogatory. Rather he said: 'When one prays two rak'ahs and forgets in them, and prostrates for his forgetfulness after the salām, then wants to build two rak'ahs upon them, he does not have that, unlike the traveler.' Except it is said that the ruling in the obligatory is a fortiori because building upon its consecration is disliked, whether he prostrated for forgetfulness or not, unlike an even supererogatory.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rā'iq discusses the ruling on building additional rak'ahs upon a prayer after having performed the prostration of forgetfulness (sujūd al-sahw). The base text (matn) states that one does not build upon a prayer after sujūd al-sahw, but the commentary clarifies that this does not mean the building is invalid; rather it is valid but makruh (disliked) because the consecration (taḥrīma) remains. The commentator explains the reasoning: the prostration of forgetfulness performed in the middle of the prayer is not considered valid for counting, so it must be repeated. An analogy is made to a traveler who, after prostrating for forgetfulness, intends to settle (i.e., becomes a resident). In that case, he cannot build upon the two rak'ahs of the traveler's prayer; instead he must complete four rak'ahs and repeat the prostration. The restriction to supererogatory prayers (shaf' al-taṭawwu') is critiqued because the same ruling applies to obligatory prayers as well, except that building is disliked in obligatory prayers regardless of sujūd al-sahw. The preferred view (mukhtār) is to repeat the prostration of forgetfulness because it was performed outside its proper place.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
البناء (al-binā'): Adding additional rak'ahs to a prayer after having performed its original parts, considered building upon the original.
شفع التطوع (shaf' al-taṭawwu'): An even number of supererogatory rak'ahs, such as two or four.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing sujūd al-sahw in the middle of a supererogatory prayer and then building additional rak'ahs?
A) It is completely invalid and the prayer is void.
B) It is valid but disliked, and the sujūd must be repeated.
C) It is recommended and encouraged.
D) It is only allowed for obligatory prayers.

Key Takeaway
Building additional rak'ahs after sujūd al-sahw is valid but disliked, and the sujūd must be repeated, except for the traveler where building is tolerated to avoid a greater loss.

Salah — Prayer

Following an Imam Who Says Salam Before Prostration of Forgetfulness
Ruling on validity of following an imam who says salām before sujūd al-sahw, and branches of the dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether salām before sujūd al-sahw exits the prayer, identify the thamarah al-khilaf in three branches, and evaluate the correct application of detail according to the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Salām before sujūd al-sahw: Abu Hanifa says it does not exit; the Sahibayn say it exits tentatively – but the detail applies only to following the imam.

In congregational prayer, what happens if the imam forgets and says salām before performing the prostration of forgetfulness? The Hanafi school has a well-known internal dispute. Understanding this dispute is essential for determining the validity of following such an imam, as well as related rulings on loud laughter and the traveler's intention of settlement. This lesson unpacks the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and clarifies which branches of the dispute carry a detailed ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two Hanafi positions
The core question: does the salām of a forgetful imam exit him from the prayer? State Abu Hanifa's view (no exit) and the Sahibayn's view (tentative exit, tawaqquf).
The difference turns on whether sujūd al-sahw is a wajib performed within the prayer's consecration (Abu Hanifa) or an independent compensatory act (Sahibayn).
2
Trace the three branches (furū')
List the three practical cases affected by the dispute: (1) a follower joining the imam after his salām, (2) loud laughter (qahqaha) during the interval, (3) a traveler intending settlement during that interval.
Each branch yields different rulings depending on which position is adopted.
3
Apply the detail: which branches get the detailed ruling?
According to the author, the Sahibayn's detail (returning to prostration vs. not) applies only to the first branch (following the imam). For branches 2 and 3, the Sahibayn have absolute rulings without detail.
This is the critical refinement: many incorrectly extend the detail to all branches.
4
Resolve the apparent contradiction in later texts
The author refutes the claim in Ghāyat al-Bayān that the Sahibayn detail all three branches. He defends the standard Hidāyah position, showing that the majority of Hanafi works agree on the limited scope of detail.
The author's resolution preserves the integrity of the madhhab's transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المحيط وشرح الطحاوي، وظاهره أيضاً أنه لو نوى الإقامة فالأمر موقوف عندهما إن سجد لزمه الإتمام وإلا فلا، وعند محمد مطلقا وقد صرح به في غاية البيان وهو غلط أيضاً فإن الحكم فيه إذا نوى الإقامة قبل يتم قد في العناية. وحاصله أن معنى التوقف كونه في حرمتها من وجه دون وجه المقابل لما اختاره مما استدل عليه بالفروع من أنه الخروج من كل وجه . وفي الفتح : هذا غير لازم من القول بالتوقف للمتأمل إذ حقيقته توقف الحكم بأنه خرج عن حرمة الصلاة أولاً، فالثابت في نفس الأمر أحدهما عيناً والسجود وعدمه معرف كما يفيده ما هو مصرح به في البدائع من التجوزين، وهذا قط لا يوجب الحكم بكونه بعد السلام في الصلاة من وجه دون وجه بل الوقوف عن الحكم بأنه خرج من كل وجه أو لم يخرج من وجه أصلاً فتأمل قوله : (كما صرح به في غاية البيان وهو غلط الخ) أقول : صرح بمثل ما في غاية البيان في هذا وفي الذي بعده أيضاً في الدرر ومتن الملتقي ومتن التنوير . قال الباقاني في شرح الملتقي : وتبع الماتن صاحب الوقاية ونسب أبو المكارم صاحب الوقاية إلى الغفلة حيث قال في شرح المختصر : وإن قهقه انتقض الوضوء عنده خلافاً لهما وصلاته تامة إجماعاً وسقط عنه سجود السهو وإن نوى الإقامة انقلب فرضه أربعاً عنده ويسجد في آخر الصلاة، وعندهما لا ينقلب أربعاً ويسقط عنه سجود السهو إذ يجابه يوجب إبطاله . كذا في الكافي والهداية وشروحها وفتاوی قاضیخان وعدة من الكتب المشهورة وما ذكر صاحب الوقاية من أنه يبطل وضوءه بالقهقهة ويصير فرضه أربعاً بنية الإقامة إن سجد بعد وإلا فلا، فهو مخالف لما في عامة الكتب، ولما ذكر هو في شرحه للهداية أنه من بعد ما قهقه يتعذر سجود السهو لبطلان التحريمة الموقوفة بالقهقهة فلعل ذلك هفوة منه ا هـ . هذا ما في الباقاني ملخصاً، وهذا يفيد أن ظاهر كلام الهداية وغيرها ليس كما ادعاه المؤلف لكن في القهستاني اقتصر على تفريع المسألة الأولى فقط على الاختلاف المذكور، وذكر أن الفرعين الأخيرين ليسا من فروعه في شيء وقال : وفي الوقاية هنا سهو مشهور ا هـ . قلت وبالله تعالى أستعين : لا يخفى على من له أدنى بصيرة أن الفروع الثلاثة حكمها مختلف على كل من القولين، فالتفريع صحيح لأن الخلاف إنما هو في الخروج باتاً أو موقوفاً لكن لما أمكن التفصيل عندهما بين العود إلى السجود وعدمه في الفرع الأول ذكروه فيه ولما لم يمكن في الأخيرين كما علمت حكموا بعدم انتقاض الطهارة وعدم تغير الفرض عندهما ولم يفصلوا بين ما إذا عاد أولاً كما فصلوا في الأول فظهر أنه ليس ظاهر كلامهم ما ذكره المؤلف وأن التفريع الذي أطبق عليه عامة الكتب صحيح لا كما قال القهستاني من عدم صحته في الأخريين إذ لم يذكروا التفصيل فيهما أيضاً.
His statement: (If the forgetful person says salām and someone else follows him, then if he prostrates, it is valid; otherwise not). And he said: whether the imam prostrates or not, because according to him (Abu Hanifa) the salām of the one upon whom forgetfulness is obligatory does not exit him from the prayer; it remains fundamentally valid because it (prostration) became obligatory to compensate for deficiency, so it must be within the consecration of prayer. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it exits him on a tentative basis because it (salām) is a permissible act in itself, but it is not operative due to his need to perform the prostration; so the need is not manifest without it, and there is no need considering non-return. And the difference appears in the validity of following, and in nullification... He prostrates in the even supererogatory built upon obligatory except that one distinguishes between supererogatory built upon obligatory intentionally and built unintentionally because it is one prayer. His statement: (And he only said 'he does not build' etc.) Al-Ramli said: In al-Nihāya there is something implying two narrations. I say: The validity of building must be restricted to when he does not say salām to terminate; if he says salām to terminate the prayer, building is prevented because his salām is from one upon whom there is no prostration of forgetfulness and it exits from the prayer. So how can building upon the obligatory be possible? Like building upon supererogatory in that he repeats sujūd al-sahw, and it contradicts what we mentioned from al-Qunyah earlier. Perhaps this is the secret of the author's restriction to supererogatory. Consider: His statement: 'then he prostrates for his forgetfulness after the salām' – restricting it to after salām does not mean that if he prostrated before it he would have it without dislike, as al-Ramli imagined; rather the restriction is because that is its place according to us. Consider his statement: 'so it (the need) does not appear without it' – the need does not appear without the prostration; meaning when he prostrates for forgetfulness, the need is realized, so the meaning of dissolution (taḥlīl) by salām falls due to need; so the need is not realized if he does not return to sujūd al-sahw. His statement: (And the difference appears etc.) He said in al-Nihāyah after discussing these branches: I say: By this it is known that according to them (the two), the one who says salām for forgetfulness exits from the sanctity of prayer completely, not that the meaning of suspension (tawaqquf) is that he exits in one respect and not another; then by prostration he enters the sanctity of prayer. Because if he were in the sanctity of prayer in one respect, the rulings would be the opposite according to them as well, as is the madhhab of Muhammad: the nullification of purity by loud laughter, the obligation of performance by following, and the obligation of four upon intention of settlement, acting on precaution. End. And he followed him. Purity by loud laughter and change of the obligatory by intention of settlement in this case. So in al-Hidāyah and others. And its apparent meaning is that purity is nullified according to him (Abu Hanifa) by loud laughter absolutely, and according to them (the Sahibayn) if he returns to prostration it is nullified, otherwise not, as stated in Ghāyat al-Bayān – and this is a mistake, because there is no detail in it between prostration and non-prostration according to them, because loud laughter necessitates dropping sujūd al-sahw according to all due to loss of the sanctity of prayer because it is speech. Rather the ruling is nullification according to him and non-nullification according to them, as stated in al-Muḥīṭ and Sharh al-Ṭaḥāwī. And its apparent meaning is also that if he intends settlement, the matter is suspended according to them: if he prostrates, completion becomes necessary; otherwise not. And according to Muhammad it is absolute, and this has been stated in Ghāyat al-Bayān – and this is also a mistake, because the ruling in it if he intends settlement before... As in al-ʿInāyah. The summary is that the meaning of suspension is that he is in its sanctity in one respect and not in another, opposite to what he chose, which he evidenced by the branches: that it is complete exit. And in al-Fatḥ: This is not necessary from the statement of suspension for the contemplative. Its reality is the suspension of the ruling whether he exited from the sanctity of prayer or not. So what is established in reality is one of them definitely, and the prostration or its absence is known, as is clarified in al-Badā'iʿ from the two possibilities. And this never necessitates the ruling that after salām he is in prayer in one respect and not another; rather it is a pause in ruling whether he exited completely or did not exit at all. So consider. His statement: (As stated in Ghāyat al-Bayān and it is a mistake etc.) I say: The like of what is in Ghāyat al-Bayān is stated in this and in what follows in al-Durar, Matn al-Multaqā, and Matn al-Tanwīr. Al-Bāqānī said in Sharh al-Multaqā: The author of al-Wiqāyah followed, and Abu al-Makārim, the author of al-Wiqāyah, was attributed with negligence where he said in Sharh al-Mukhtaṣar: If he laughs loudly, wuḍū' is nullified according to him contrary to them, and his prayer is complete by consensus, and sujūd al-sahw is dropped; and if he intends settlement, his obligatory becomes four according to him and he prostrates at the end, and according to them it does not become four and sujūd al-sahw is dropped because it necessitates its nullification. So in al-Kāfī, al-Hidāyah and its commentaries, Fatāwā Qāḍīkhān, and several well-known books. And what the author of al-Wiqāyah mentioned – that he nullifies his wuḍū' by loud laughter and his obligatory becomes four by intention of settlement if he prostrates afterwards, otherwise not – contradicts what is in most books, and what he himself mentioned in his commentary on al-Hidāyah: that after he laughs loudly, sujūd al-sahw becomes impossible due to the invalidity of the consecration suspended by loud laughter; so perhaps that is a slip from him. End. This is what is in al-Bāqānī summarized. And this indicates that the apparent meaning of al-Hidāyah and others is not as the author claimed. But in al-Qahustānī he confined himself to deriving only the first branch from the mentioned difference, and he said that the last two branches are not derived from it at all. And he said: In al-Wiqāyah here there is a well-known oversight. End. I say, and by Allah the Exalted I seek help: It is not hidden from anyone with the slightest insight that the three branches differ in ruling according to each of the two statements. So the derivation is correct because the difference is only regarding exit definitively or suspended; but when detail was possible according to them between returning to prostration and not returning in the first branch, they mentioned it; and when it was not possible in the last two as you know, they ruled with non-nullification of purity and non-change of the obligatory according to them, and they did not detail between whether he returns or not as they detailed in the first. Thus it appears that the apparent meaning of their statements is not what the author mentioned, and the derivation that most books agree upon is correct, not as al-Qahustānī said regarding its incorrectness in the last two, since they did not mention detail in them either.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding a forgetful imam who says salām before performing sujūd al-sahw, and its effects on followers, purity, and the traveler's prayer. The core issue: does the salām of a forgetful person exit him from the prayer? According to Abu Hanifa, the salām does not exit him because sujūd al-sahw is still obligatory and the prayer remains in a state of consecration. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the salām exits him on a tentative basis (tawaqquf) – meaning the exit is conditional upon whether he returns to sujūd al-sahw. This difference impacts three branches: (1) the validity of following such an imam, (2) the nullification of wudu by loud laughter (qahqaha) during the prayer, and (3) the travel (qasr) prayer becoming complete upon intending settlement. The author then critiques an error in some texts (e.g., Ghāyat al-Bayān) that claim the Sahibayn make detail based on returning to sujūd al-sahw in all branches. The author argues that such detail applies only to the first branch (following the imam), not the other two, and defends the standard Hanafi position. The discussion confirms that the standard textbooks (Hidāyah, etc.) are correct, contrary to some allegations of oversight.

Key Terms
الساهي (al-sāhī): The person who forgets in prayer and is required to perform sujūd al-sahw.
الاقتداء (al-iqtidā'): The act of following the imam in congregational prayer.
القهقهة (al-qahqaha): Loud laughter that breaks both prayer and wudu in the Hanafi school.
نيَة الإقامة (niyyat al-iqāma): The intention of a traveler to settle in a place, which changes the ruling from qasr to complete prayer.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Suspension of the ruling; the salām is considered to exit the prayer only provisionally, pending the performance of sujūd al-sahw.
الفرع (al-far'): A branch; a specific legal case derived from a general principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Baḥr al-Rā'iq, which of the following three branches (furū') does the Sahibayn's detail (between returning to sujūd al-sahw or not) apply to?
A) All three branches equally.
B) Only the first branch, regarding following the imam.
C) Only the second branch, regarding loud laughter.
D) Only the third branch, regarding the traveler's intention of settlement.

Key Takeaway
The effect of salām before sujūd al-sahw in Hanafi fiqh is disputed internally; the Sahibayn's position of tentative exit applies detail only to the branch of following the imam.

The Ruling on Laughter (Qahqaha) in Prayer: Ablution Dispute
Dispute resolution on laughter's effect on ablution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding invalidation of ablution by laughter during prayer, and identify the mistake in Ghayat al-Bayan.

Core Idea
Laughter drops sujud al-sahw; Sahibayn say ablution is not invalidated, contrary to a misattributed conditional view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether laughter (qahqaha) during prayer invalidates ablution. While Abu Hanifa holds it invalidates absolutely, the two companions (Sahibayn) maintain it does not, and the author corrects a confusion in Ghayat al-Bayan that attributed a conditional view to them. Understanding this dispute is crucial for knowing the validity of a person's prayer and purification after laughter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ground
All agree that laughter drops the prostration of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw) because it is considered speech and violates the sanctity of prayer.
This is a key premise for the dispute.
2
State the two positions on invalidation of ablution
Abu Hanifa holds ablution is invalidated absolutely by laughter. The Sahibayn hold it is not invalidated at all.
The text explicitly rejects any conditional detail for Sahibayn.
3
Analyze the mistaken attribution in Ghayat al-Bayan
Ghayat al-Bayan incorrectly claimed that according to Sahibayn, invalidation depends on returning to prostration. The author refutes this, citing al-Muhit and Sharh al-Tahawi as correct sources.
This error is important to avoid confusion.
4
Conclude the correct Sahibayn position
The Sahibayn's position is that laughter does not invalidate ablution under any circumstances because it causes exit from the prayer's sanctity.
This is the relied-upon view in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو
انتقاض الطهارة بالقهقهة وتغيير الفرض بنية الإقامة في هذه الحالة. كذا في الهداية وغيرها. وظاهره أن الطهارة تنتقض عنده بالقهقهة مطلقاً، وعندهما إن عاد إلى السجود انتقضت وإلا فلا كما صرح به في غاية البيان وهو غلط، فإنه لا تفصيل فيه بين السجود وعدمه عندهما لأن القهقهة أوجبت سقوط سجود السهو عند الكل لفوات حرمة الصلاة لأنها كلام، وإنما الحكم هو النقض عنده وعدمه عندهما كما صرح به في المحيط وشرح الطحاوي، وظاهره أيضاً أنه لو نوى الإقامة فالأمر موقوف عندهما إن سجد لزمه الإتمام وإلا فلا، وعند محمد مطلقا وقد صرح به في غاية البيان وهو غلط أيضاً فإن الحكم فيه إذا نوى الإقامة قبل السجود أنه لا يتغير فرضه عندهما ويسقط سجود السهو لأنه لو سجد فقد عاد إلى حرمة الصلاة فيتغير فرضه أربعاً فيقع سجوده في خلال الصلاة فلا يعتد به فلا فائدة في الاشتغال به، وعنده يتمها أربعاً ويسجد في آخر صلاته. كذا في المحيط. وذكر في معراج الدراية أن عندهما لا يتغير فرضه، سواء سجد للسهو أو لا، لأنه لو تغير قبل السجود لصحت النية قبل السجود ولو صحت لوقعت السجدة في وسط الصلاة فصار كأنه لم يسجد أصلاً، فلو لصحت بلا سجود ولا وجه له عندهما لأنه يحصل بعد الخروج فلا يتغير فرضه. وقيدنا بكونه نوى الإقامة قبل السجود لأنه لو نواها بعدما سجد سجدة أو سجدتين تغير فرضه اتفاقاً ويسجد في آخرها للسهو لأن النية صادفت حرمة الصلاة فصار مقيماً. كذا في المحيط. وما في غاية البيان من أن ثمرة الاختلاف تظهر في مسألة رابعة وهي ما إذا اقتدى به إنسان في هذه الحالة ثم وجد منه ما ينافي الصلاة قصداً هل يقضي أم لا، فعند محمد يقضي سجد الإمام أو لم يسجد لصحة الاقتداء، وعندهما لا يقضي لعدم صحة الاقتداء، فليست مسألة رابعة بل متفرعة على مسألة المتن وهي صحة الاقتداء فإنه إن صح الاقتداء أو أفسدها لزمه القضاء وإلا فلا. وجعل في الخلاصة ثمرة الاختلاف تظهر أيضاً في الصلاة على رسول الله والأدعية، فعند محمد يأتي بهما في القعدة الأخيرة وهي قعدة سجود السهو لأنها قعدة الختم عنده وعندهما يأتي بهما في قعدة الصلاة لأنه لما عاد إلى السجود تبين أنه يكن خارجاً فكان الأولى قعدة الختم.
The chapter of prayer, section on prostration of forgetfulness. The invalidation of purification by laughing out loud and the change of the obligatory prayer by the intention of residency in this situation. Thus in al-Hidayah and others. Its apparent meaning is that purification is invalidated according to him (Abu Hanifa) by laughter absolutely, while according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is invalidated if he returns to prostration, otherwise not, as stated in Ghayat al-Bayan, and that is a mistake. For there is no detail about returning to prostration or not according to them, because laughter necessitates the dropping of the prostration of forgetfulness according to all due to the loss of the sanctity of prayer because it is speech. The ruling is only invalidation according to him and non-invalidation according to them, as stated in al-Muhit and Sharh al-Tahawi. And its apparent meaning also is that if he intended residency, the matter is suspended according to them: if he prostrated, he must complete it, otherwise not; and according to Muhammad absolutely, and that is also a mistake. For the ruling regarding it is that if he intended residency before prostration, his obligatory prayer does not change according to them, and the prostration of forgetfulness is dropped, because if he prostrated, he would have returned to the sanctity of prayer, then his obligatory prayer would change to four, and his prostration would occur in the middle of the prayer, so it would not be considered, so there is no benefit in engaging in it. And according to him (Muhammad?), he completes it as four and prostrates at the end of his prayer. Thus in al-Muhit. And it is mentioned in Mi'raj al-Dirayah that according to them his obligatory prayer does not change, whether he prostrates for forgetfulness or not, because if it changed before prostration, the intention would be valid before prostration, and if it were valid, the prostration would occur in the middle of the prayer, so it would be as if he did not prostrate at all, so if it were valid without prostration, there is no way for it according to them because it occurs after exiting, so his obligatory prayer does not change. And we restricted it to his intending residency before prostration, because if he intended it after he had prostrated once or twice, his obligatory prayer changes by agreement, and he prostrates at the end of it for forgetfulness, because the intention encountered the sanctity of prayer, so he became a resident. Thus in al-Muhit. And what is in Ghayat al-Bayan that the fruit of the difference appears in a fourth issue, which is if a person follows him in this state and then does something that contradicts prayer deliberately, does he make up (the prayer) or not? According to Muhammad, he makes up whether the imam prostrated or not, due to the validity of following; according to them, he does not make up due to the invalidity of following. This is not a fourth issue but rather a branch of the issue in the text, which is the validity of following; for if following is valid or he invalidated it, he must make up, otherwise not. And in al-Khulasa, the fruit of the difference is also shown regarding the prayer upon the Messenger of Allah and supplications: according to Muhammad, he performs them in the last sitting, which is the sitting for the prostration of forgetfulness, because it is the sitting of completion according to him; according to them, he performs them in the sitting of the prayer, because when he returned to prostration, it becomes clear that he was not outside, so the first is the sitting of completion.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effects of laughter (قهقهة) during prayer and the intention to change from traveler to resident (نية الإقامة). The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq is commenting on the text of Kanz al-Daqaiq and refuting a mistake in Ghayat al-Bayan. The dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa (عنده) and the two companions Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (عندهما). The issue: When a person laughs out loud during prayer, according to Abu Hanifa, his ablution (طهارة) is invalidated absolutely, and the prayer becomes void? Actually, the text discusses invalidation of purification (طهارة) and change of the obligatory prayer (فرض) from two to four when intending to become resident. The author clarifies that laughter does not affect the prostration of forgetfulness; all agree it drops because laughter is speech and violates prayer's sanctity. The dispute is about whether the purification is invalidated: Abu Hanifa says yes, the two say no unless the person returns to prostration. Similarly, for intention of residency: Abu Hanifa says the prayer becomes four regardless; the two say it remains two unless the person returns to prostration, then it becomes four. The author corrects the claim that the two companions differentiate based on returning to prostration; he says they do not differentiate—they hold that the prayer does not change at all, because the intention to change occurs after exiting the prayer (due to laughter), so it cannot affect the prayer. The practical consequences (ثمرة الخلاف) include: if someone follows such an imam, according to Muhammad the following is valid (so if the follower does something invalidating, he must make up), while according to the two the following is invalid (so no makeup). Also in the final sitting for supplications, according to Muhammad they are said in the sitting after prostration of forgetfulness (because it's the completion sitting), while according to the two they are said in the last sitting of the original prayer (since the person never truly exited). The passage emphasizes that the correct position is what is in al-Muhit and other reliable books, not the mistaken elaboration in Ghayat al-Bayan.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Laughing out loud during prayer, which breaks the prayer's sanctity and drops the prostration of forgetfulness.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness to compensate for omissions or errors in prayer. In this context, it drops if laughter occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view of the Sahibayn, does laughter during prayer invalidate ablution?
A) Yes, absolutely.
B) Yes, unless he returns to prostration.
C) No, never.
D) No, unless he laughs multiple times.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn hold that laughter does not invalidate ablution because it causes exit from prayer; the mistaken detail in Ghayat al-Bayan is refuted.

The Effect of Intention to Residency After Laughter: Prayer Length and Following
Dispute on intention to residency after laughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a traveler's prayer length after intending residency following laughter, and determine the validity of following such an imam.

Core Idea
Intention to become resident after laughter does not change prayer length according to Sahibayn; it does according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage continues the intra-Hanafi dispute, focusing on what happens when a traveler who has laughed during prayer intends to become a resident. The Sahibayn hold that the prayer remains two rak'ahs, while Abu Hanifa holds it becomes four. The author also clarifies the practical consequences for followers and for supplications during the final sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A traveler laughs during prayer, then intends to become a resident (niyyat al-iqama) before prostrating for forgetfulness.
The timing of intention relative to prostration is crucial.
2
State the dispute on prayer length
Abu Hanifa: the prayer changes to four rak'ahs. Sahibayn: the prayer remains two rak'ahs because the intention occurs after exiting the prayer.
The author refutes the mistaken view that Sahibayn make it conditional on returning to prostration.
3
Examine the thamarat al-khilaf
Two practical consequences: (a) If a follower joins such an imam, according to Muhammad the following is valid and the follower must make up if he does something invalidating; according to Sahibayn the following is invalid so no makeup. (b) The sitting for supplications: Muhammad says they are said in the sitting after sujud al-sahw (because it's the completion sitting), Sahibayn say in the original last sitting.
These consequences flow from the core difference on validity of the prayer.
4
Understand the exception
If the intention to residency is made after prostrating once or twice, all agree the prayer changes to four and sujud al-sahw is performed at the end.
This is because the intention encounters the prayer's sanctity after returning to it.

كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو
انتقاض الطهارة بالقهقهة وتغيير الفرض بنية الإقامة في هذه الحالة. كذا في الهداية وغيرها. وظاهره أن الطهارة تنتقض عنده بالقهقهة مطلقاً، وعندهما إن عاد إلى السجود انتقضت وإلا فلا كما صرح به في غاية البيان وهو غلط، فإنه لا تفصيل فيه بين السجود وعدمه عندهما لأن القهقهة أوجبت سقوط سجود السهو عند الكل لفوات حرمة الصلاة لأنها كلام، وإنما الحكم هو النقض عنده وعدمه عندهما كما صرح به في المحيط وشرح الطحاوي، وظاهره أيضاً أنه لو نوى الإقامة فالأمر موقوف عندهما إن سجد لزمه الإتمام وإلا فلا، وعند محمد مطلقا وقد صرح به في غاية البيان وهو غلط أيضاً فإن الحكم فيه إذا نوى الإقامة قبل السجود أنه لا يتغير فرضه عندهما ويسقط سجود السهو لأنه لو سجد فقد عاد إلى حرمة الصلاة فيتغير فرضه أربعاً فيقع سجوده في خلال الصلاة فلا يعتد به فلا فائدة في الاشتغال به، وعنده يتمها أربعاً ويسجد في آخر صلاته. كذا في المحيط. وذكر في معراج الدراية أن عندهما لا يتغير فرضه، سواء سجد للسهو أو لا، لأنه لو تغير قبل السجود لصحت النية قبل السجود ولو صحت لوقعت السجدة في وسط الصلاة فصار كأنه لم يسجد أصلاً، فلو لصحت بلا سجود ولا وجه له عندهما لأنه يحصل بعد الخروج فلا يتغير فرضه. وقيدنا بكونه نوى الإقامة قبل السجود لأنه لو نواها بعدما سجد سجدة أو سجدتين تغير فرضه اتفاقاً ويسجد في آخرها للسهو لأن النية صادفت حرمة الصلاة فصار مقيماً. كذا في المحيط. وما في غاية البيان من أن ثمرة الاختلاف تظهر في مسألة رابعة وهي ما إذا اقتدى به إنسان في هذه الحالة ثم وجد منه ما ينافي الصلاة قصداً هل يقضي أم لا، فعند محمد يقضي سجد الإمام أو لم يسجد لصحة الاقتداء، وعندهما لا يقضي لعدم صحة الاقتداء، فليست مسألة رابعة بل متفرعة على مسألة المتن وهي صحة الاقتداء فإنه إن صح الاقتداء أو أفسدها لزمه القضاء وإلا فلا. وجعل في الخلاصة ثمرة الاختلاف تظهر أيضاً في الصلاة على رسول الله والأدعية، فعند محمد يأتي بهما في القعدة الأخيرة وهي قعدة سجود السهو لأنها قعدة الختم عنده وعندهما يأتي بهما في قعدة الصلاة لأنه لما عاد إلى السجود تبين أنه يكن خارجاً فكان الأولى قعدة الختم.
The chapter of prayer, section on prostration of forgetfulness. The invalidation of purification by laughing out loud and the change of the obligatory prayer by the intention of residency in this situation. Thus in al-Hidayah and others. Its apparent meaning is that purification is invalidated according to him (Abu Hanifa) by laughter absolutely, while according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is invalidated if he returns to prostration, otherwise not, as stated in Ghayat al-Bayan, and that is a mistake. For there is no detail about returning to prostration or not according to them, because laughter necessitates the dropping of the prostration of forgetfulness according to all due to the loss of the sanctity of prayer because it is speech. The ruling is only invalidation according to him and non-invalidation according to them, as stated in al-Muhit and Sharh al-Tahawi. And its apparent meaning also is that if he intended residency, the matter is suspended according to them: if he prostrated, he must complete it, otherwise not; and according to Muhammad absolutely, and that is also a mistake. For the ruling regarding it is that if he intended residency before prostration, his obligatory prayer does not change according to them, and the prostration of forgetfulness is dropped, because if he prostrated, he would have returned to the sanctity of prayer, then his obligatory prayer would change to four, and his prostration would occur in the middle of the prayer, so it would not be considered, so there is no benefit in engaging in it. And according to him (Muhammad?), he completes it as four and prostrates at the end of his prayer. Thus in al-Muhit. And it is mentioned in Mi'raj al-Dirayah that according to them his obligatory prayer does not change, whether he prostrates for forgetfulness or not, because if it changed before prostration, the intention would be valid before prostration, and if it were valid, the prostration would occur in the middle of the prayer, so it would be as if he did not prostrate at all, so if it were valid without prostration, there is no way for it according to them because it occurs after exiting, so his obligatory prayer does not change. And we restricted it to his intending residency before prostration, because if he intended it after he had prostrated once or twice, his obligatory prayer changes by agreement, and he prostrates at the end of it for forgetfulness, because the intention encountered the sanctity of prayer, so he became a resident. Thus in al-Muhit. And what is in Ghayat al-Bayan that the fruit of the difference appears in a fourth issue, which is if a person follows him in this state and then does something that contradicts prayer deliberately, does he make up (the prayer) or not? According to Muhammad, he makes up whether the imam prostrated or not, due to the validity of following; according to them, he does not make up due to the invalidity of following. This is not a fourth issue but rather a branch of the issue in the text, which is the validity of following; for if following is valid or he invalidated it, he must make up, otherwise not. And in al-Khulasa, the fruit of the difference is also shown regarding the prayer upon the Messenger of Allah and supplications: according to Muhammad, he performs them in the last sitting, which is the sitting for the prostration of forgetfulness, because it is the sitting of completion according to him; according to them, he performs them in the sitting of the prayer, because when he returned to prostration, it becomes clear that he was not outside, so the first is the sitting of completion.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effects of laughter (قهقهة) during prayer and the intention to change from traveler to resident (نية الإقامة). The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq is commenting on the text of Kanz al-Daqaiq and refuting a mistake in Ghayat al-Bayan. The dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa (عنده) and the two companions Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (عندهما). The issue: When a person laughs out loud during prayer, according to Abu Hanifa, his ablution (طهارة) is invalidated absolutely, and the prayer becomes void? Actually, the text discusses invalidation of purification (طهارة) and change of the obligatory prayer (فرض) from two to four when intending to become resident. The author clarifies that laughter does not affect the prostration of forgetfulness; all agree it drops because laughter is speech and violates prayer's sanctity. The dispute is about whether the purification is invalidated: Abu Hanifa says yes, the two say no unless the person returns to prostration. Similarly, for intention of residency: Abu Hanifa says the prayer becomes four regardless; the two say it remains two unless the person returns to prostration, then it becomes four. The author corrects the claim that the two companions differentiate based on returning to prostration; he says they do not differentiate—they hold that the prayer does not change at all, because the intention to change occurs after exiting the prayer (due to laughter), so it cannot affect the prayer. The practical consequences (ثمرة الخلاف) include: if someone follows such an imam, according to Muhammad the following is valid (so if the follower does something invalidating, he must make up), while according to the two the following is invalid (so no makeup). Also in the final sitting for supplications, according to Muhammad they are said in the sitting after prostration of forgetfulness (because it's the completion sitting), while according to the two they are said in the last sitting of the original prayer (since the person never truly exited). The passage emphasizes that the correct position is what is in al-Muhit and other reliable books, not the mistaken elaboration in Ghayat al-Bayan.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqama): Intention to change from traveler to resident status during prayer, affecting the number of rak'ahs.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness; in this context, it drops if laughter occurs, but if one returns to it, it may affect the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Four, because intention changes it.
B) Two, because intention occurs after exit.
C) Four, only if he returns to prostration.
D) The prayer is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn hold that intention to residency after laughter does not change the prayer length; the prayer remains two rak'ahs.

Intention of Iqama and Sujud al-Sahw: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on traveler's intention of residency before sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a traveler's intention of residency before Sujud al-Sahw and apply the relied-upon ruling.

Core Idea
When a traveler intends residency before Sujud al-Sahw, Abu Hanifa says his prayer becomes 4 rak'ahs, but the Sahibayn say it remains 2.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: if a traveler (musafir) who still needs to perform Sujud al-Sahw intends to become a resident (niyyat al-iqama) before performing the prostration, does his obligation change from 2 to 4 rak'ahs? The disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), reveals important principles about the inviolability of prayer (hurmat al-salah) and the nature of compensatory acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine what is being disputed: the traveler intends residency before performing Sujud al-Sahw, and the question is whether his fard changes from 2 to 4 rak'ahs.
The intention of iqama is made when the traveler is still in prayer and has an outstanding Sujud al-Sahw.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the fard changes to 4; the traveler must complete 4 rak'ahs and then perform Sujud al-Sahw at the end.
His reasoning is that the intention of residency makes him a resident, so his obligation changes, and Sujud al-Sahw can still be performed within the prayer.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the fard remains 2, and Sujud al-Sahw is not performed; the prayer is considered complete upon intention.
They argue that if the fard changed, it would create a vicious circle (dawr) because the traveler would need to return to prayer's inviolability to perform the prostration, which is impossible without completing the prayer.
4
Understand the cyclic argument
The Sahibayn reason that if the fard changed, the intention would occur before the prostration, making the prostration mid-prayer and invalid. To avoid this, they deem the prayer complete at the moment of intention, so no change occurs.
The cycle: to return to prayer's inviolability, one needs to complete prayer, but completion requires the intention to be valid, which it cannot be if it changes the fard. Cutting the cycle means the prayer is finished.
5
Identify the practical consequences
The difference affects whether a follower of such an imam must make up the prayer and the order of supplications. According to the Sahibayn, if the imam's fard does not change, following him is invalid, so the follower must repeat the prayer.
The thamarah al-khilaf also appears in the order of blessings and supplications during the last sitting.
