Missing Sajdah from Unknown Prayer: Taharrī and Precaution
Ruling on forgetting a prostration when unsure from which prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who remembers a missed sajdah but cannot recall from which prayer, and explain the roles of taharrī and ihtiyat in such doubt.

Core Idea
When certainty is impossible, taharrī guides; if unresolved, precaution recommends repeating both prayers, but does not obligate it.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario of doubt during prayer: a person is praying 'Asr and suddenly recalls that he omitted a prostration (sajdah) at some point, but cannot remember whether it occurred in the preceding Zuhr prayer or in the current 'Asr. The Hanafi school provides a step‑by‑step procedure involving estimation (taharrī) and then precautionary action (ihtiyat), while also clarifying that the precaution is recommended rather than mandatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the source passage carefully: a person is in the middle of 'Asr prayer and remembers that he missed a sajdah (prostration) at some earlier time, but he cannot tell whether it was from the previous Zuhr prayer or from the current 'Asr prayer.
This is a case of doubt about a past prayer, not about the present prayer exclusively.
2
Apply Taharrī
The person must first make a judgement (taharrī) to try to determine the most likely prayer where the sajdah was omitted. If his estimation yields a clear result, he acts accordingly. The passage focuses on the case where taharrī does not yield a conclusion.
Taharrī means using personal estimation to resolve doubt when certainty is impossible.
3
If Taharrī Fails: Complete Current Prayer with Compensation
If no clear judgement is reached, the person completes his current 'Asr prayer and performs one extra sajdah (a compensation sajdah) to cover the possibility that the omission was from 'Asr.
This sajdah is not the sajdah of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) but a separate act to compensate for the possible missed obligation.
4
Precautionary Repetition of Both Prayers
After completing 'Asr, out of precaution (ihtiyat), the person should repeat both the Zuhr and 'Asr prayers. This ensures that the obligatory sajdah is fulfilled in one of them, removing the doubt entirely.
The repetition is recommended (mandub) but not obligatory, as the next step shows.
5
Understand the Non‑Obligatory Nature of Repetition
The passage explicitly says that if he does not repeat the prayers, there is nothing upon him (i.e., no sin or further obligation). This indicates that the repetition is a precaution, not a mandatory requirement.
Hanafi fiqh gives leeway in deep doubt: precaution is encouraged but not forced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تذكر مصلي العصر أنه ترك سجدة ولا يدري أنه تركها من صلاة الظهر أو من صلاة العصر الذي هو فيها فإنه يتحرى فإن لم يقع تحريه على شيء يتم العصر ويسجد سجدة واحدة لاحتمال أنه تركها من العصر ثم يعيد الظهر احتياطاً ثم يعيد العصر، فإن لم يعد فلا شيء عليه.
If a person praying 'Asr remembers that he left a sajdah and does not know whether he left it from Zuhr or from 'Asr which he is in, then he makes a judgement (taharrī). If his judgement does not settle on anything, he completes 'Asr and performs one sajdah because of the possibility that he left it from 'Asr, then repeats Zuhr out of precaution, then repeats 'Asr. If he does not repeat, there is nothing upon him.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: a person is praying 'Asr and suddenly remembers that he omitted a prostration (sajdah) at some point, but he cannot recall whether it occurred during the preceding Zuhr prayer or during the current 'Asr prayer. The ruling is that he should first attempt to determine the most likely case (taharrī). If no clear judgement emerges, he must complete the current 'Asr prayer and perform an extra sajdah (sajdat al-tilawah? Actually here it is a sajdah of compensation) to cover the possibility that the omission was from 'Asr. Then, out of precaution, he must repeat both Zuhr and 'Asr. However, if he chooses not to repeat, he incurs no sin or further obligation. This reflects the Hanafi principle that precaution (ihtiyat) is encouraged but not always compulsory where doubt is deep. The repetition of both prayers ensures that the obligatory sajdah is fulfilled in one of them. Note that this is a case of doubt about a previous prayer's validity, which is rarer; normally, doubt during the current prayer takes precedence.

Key Terms
تحری (taharrī): A process of judgement or estimation to determine the most likely correct action when certainty is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only repeat Zuhr.
B) Complete 'Asr, perform one sajdah, then repeat both prayers precautionarily.
C) Continue 'Asr and ignore the memory.
D) Repeat 'Asr only.

Key Takeaway
When taharrī fails, complete the current prayer with a compensating sajdah, then repeat both prayers precautionarily, but the repetition is not obligatory.

Interpreting 'First Time' in Doubt: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'first time' when doubt occurs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi interpretations of 'awwal marrah' (first time) for forgetfulness in prayer and apply each to determine whether a worshipper must act on a subsequent doubt.

Core Idea
The definition of 'first time' determines when doubt is ignored or acted upon — three Hanafi views.

In Hanafi fiqh, repeated doubt during worship is generally disregarded, but the first occurrence requires action. However, scholars differed on what constitutes 'first time' — is it the very first time in life, the first time in a prayer, or the first time it becomes a habit? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents three intra-Hanafi interpretations and their practical impact on how a worshipper should handle forgetfulness in prayer, wudu, and other acts.

Guided Path
1
Recall the rule for recurrent doubt
The general Hanafi principle: if a doubt (e.g., about the number of rak'ahs or occurrence of an act) persists or recurs often, it is ignored. Only the first occurrence requires the worshipper to act (e.g., repeat the act or perform sujud al-sahw). The definition of 'first time' is therefore critical.
2
Enumerate the three interpretations
Identify the three views from the passage: (1) Majority: first occurrence in one's entire life after puberty. (2) Imam al-Sarakhsi: the first time forgetfulness is not yet a habit. (3) Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi: the first occurrence in the current prayer session.
Each view uses a different benchmark: lifespan, habit, or single prayer.
3
Understand the thamarah (practical consequence)
Work through the example: a person forgets once, then after years forgets again. According to the majority, the second doubt is ignored (it's not the first in life). According to Sarakhsi, it is still a first time because it hasn't become a habit. According to Fakhr al-Islam, it is a first time in this new prayer, so action is required. The passage also notes that the majority view leads to taharrī (making a judgment) in some cases.
4
Apply to wudu and takbir examples
The passage extends the principle to wudu: if one doubts a part of wudu for the first time (according to the chosen interpretation), he washes that part; if recurrent, he ignores. Similarly for doubt about the opening takbir, hadath, najasa, or wiping the head. Practice applying each interpretation to these scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفوا في معنى قولهم أول مرة فأكثر مشايخنا كما في الخلاصة والخانية والظهيرية على أن معناه أول ما وقع له في عمره يعني لم يكن سها في صلاة قط بعد بلوغه كما ذكره الشارح . وذهب الإمام السرخسي إلى أن معناه أن السهو ليس بعادة له لا أنه لم يسه قط. وقال فخر الإسلام أي في هذه الصلاة واختاره ابن الفضل كما في الظهيرية وكلاهما قريب. كذا في غاية البيان وفائدة الخلاف بين العبارات أنه إذا سها في صلاته أول مرة واستقبله ثم وقف سنين ثم سها على قول شمس الأئمة يستأنف لأنه لم يكن من عادته وإنما حصل له مرة واحدة والعادة إنما هي من المعاودة، وعلى العبارتين الأخريين يجتهد في ذلك. كذا في السراج الوهاج وفيه نظر، بل يستأنف على عبارة السرخسي وفخر الإسلام، ويتحرى على قول الأكثر فقط لأنه أول سهو وقع له في تلك الصلاة فيستأنف على قول فخر الإسلام كما لا يخفى. وهذا الاختلاف يفسر قولهم وإن كثر تحرى . فعلى قول الأكثر المراد بالكثرة مرتان بعد بلوغه، وعلى قول فخر الإسلام مرتان في صلاة واحدة وفي المجتبى وقيل مرتين في سنته، ولعله على قول السرخسي. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو شك في بعض وضوئه وهو أول ما عرض له غسل ذلك الموضع وإن كان يعرض له كثيراً لا يلتفت إليه كذا في معراج الدراية. وفي المجتبى والمبتغى : ومن شك أنه كبر للافتتاح أولا، أو هل أحدث أو لا، أو هل أصابت النجاسة ثوبه أو لا، أو مسح رأسه أم لا، استقبل إن كان أول مرة وإلا فلا اهـ.
They differed on the meaning of their statement 'first time'. Most of our scholars, as in al-Khulasa, al-Khaniyya, and al-Zahiriyya, hold that its meaning is the first thing that occurred to him in his life, meaning he had never forgotten in any prayer after puberty, as the commentator mentioned. Imam al-Sarakhsi went to the view that its meaning is that forgetfulness is not a habit of his, not that he never forgot at all. Fakhr al-Islam said: i.e., in this prayer, and Ibn al-Fadl chose it, as in al-Zahiriyya; both are close. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. The benefit of the disagreement between the expressions is that if he forgets in his prayer for the first time and then stops (for years) then forgets again, according to Shams al-A'imma he starts afresh because it was not his habit; it only occurred once, and habit is from repetition. According to the other two expressions, he makes an effort (ijtihad) in that. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and there is a consideration: rather, he starts afresh according to the expression of al-Sarakhsi and Fakhr al-Islam, and he makes a judgement (taharrī) according to the majority only, because it is the first forgetfulness that occurred to him in that prayer, so he starts afresh according to Fakhr al-Islam, as is not hidden. This difference interprets their statement 'even if it is many'. According to the majority, 'many' means twice after puberty; according to Fakhr al-Islam, twice in one prayer; and in al-Mujtaba it is said twice in his year, and perhaps according to al-Sarakhsi. The author indicated that if he doubts about some part of his wudu and it is the first time it occurred to him, he washes that part, even if it occurs to him frequently he does not pay attention. Similarly in al-Mujtaba and al-Mubtagha: If he doubts whether he said the opening takbir or not, or whether he had an event (hadath) or not, or whether najasa touched his garment or not, or whether he wiped his head or not, he starts afresh if it is the first time, otherwise no.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal term 'first time' (awwal marrah) as it applies to doubt in prayer. The term appears in the rule: if a doubt occurs for the first time, the worshipper must act upon it (e.g., repeat or compensate), but if it is recurrent, he ignores it. The majority of Hanafi scholars (as recorded in al-Khulasa, al-Khaniyya, al-Zahiriyya) interpret 'first time' literally as the very first occurrence in the worshipper's entire life after puberty. Thus, only if he has never experienced this type of doubt before does he act; if he has, he disregards it. Imam al-Sarakhsi defines it differently: 'first time' means that forgetfulness is not a habitual occurrence; even if he forgot once years ago, that alone does not make it habitual. Fakhr al-Islam (al-Bazdawi) restricts it to the current prayer: if it is the first doubt in this particular prayer, he acts; otherwise not. The practical consequence (thamarah) is illustrated: if a person forgets in prayer once, then goes years without any doubt, then forgets again, according to the majority he should ignore the new doubt because it is not the absolute first in life; according to Sarakhsi, he starts afresh because it is not yet a habit; according to Fakhr al-Islam, he starts afresh because it is the first in this new prayer. The passage then applies this principle to wudu and takbir: if a person has doubt about wudu validity for the first time (ever, or in that session depending on the view), he must repeat the doubtful part; otherwise he ignores. Similarly for doubt about saying the opening takbir, or hadath, or najasa, or wiping the head. This shows how the definition of 'first time' affects practice.

Key Terms
أول مرة (awwal marrah): The first occurrence of a specific type of doubt; its exact scope (life, prayer, or habit) is disputed.
السهو (al-sahw): Forgetfulness in prayer leading to possible need for sujud al-sahw or repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars in this passage, what is meant by 'first time' (awwal marrah) for forgetfulness in prayer?
A) The first time in a particular prayer session.
B) The first time in one's entire life after puberty.
C) The first time in a given year.
D) The first time forgetfulness becomes a habit.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'first time' in forgetfulness is a term of art with three valid interpretations that affect when a worshipper must act on doubt.

Salah — Prayer

Definitions of Shakk, Zann, Wahm and Building on the Lesser Number in Prayer
Definitions of doubt terms and al-bina' 'ala al-aqall rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the three states of doubt in Hanafi fiqh (shakk, zann, wahm) and apply the rule of building on the lesser number (al-bina' 'ala al-aqall) when doubt in rak'ahs persists after taharrī.

Core Idea
In prayer doubt, when neither side preponderates, build on the lesser number to avoid missing obligatory sittings.

This lesson clarifies how a Hanafi worshipper should handle doubt during prayer. We begin by defining three mental states: shakk (equal doubt), zann (preponderance of correctness), and wahm (preponderance of error). The passage then explains that after seeking the strongest opinion (taharrī), if no preponderance emerges, the rule is to build on the lesser number of rak'ahs. This precautionary method ensures that all obligatory and wajib sittings are performed, and any error is compensated by sujud al-sahw.

Guided Path
1
Define the Three Terms
Identify the Hanafi definitions: shakk is equal probability between two possibilities; zann is preponderance of the side of correctness; wahm is preponderance of the side of error.
These definitions are foundational for the subsequent rulings.
2
Understand Taharrī and Its Limit
Taharrī is the effort to reach a predominant opinion. If after taharrī one side is clearly preponderant, act on it. If still equal, move to building on the lesser number.
Taharrī does not create certainty; it helps identify the stronger side if present.
3
Apply Building on the Lesser Number
When doubt persists between two rak'ahs, treat the current rak'ah as the smaller number. For example, doubt between 2nd and 3rd: treat as 2nd; sit for tashahhud, then continue.
The rule is wajib; deviation without valid reason invalidates the precaution.
4
Sit in Every Doubtful Position
While building on the lesser, one must sit in every place where a sitting might be obligatory or wajib. This avoids missing an essential sitting.
The text gives an example: for a four-rak'ah prayer, four sittings occur (two fard, two wajib).
5
Recognize the Exception for Doubt About Stood Rak'ah
If doubt is about the rak'ah one has stood from (e.g., after standing, doubt if previous was 2nd or 3rd), the correct view (al-Ramli) is not to sit back down. The rule of not returning except in Maghrib and Witr applies.
This is a specific exception to the general sitting rule.

Source Text

في كل موضع يتوهم قعود فرضاً كان القعود أو واجباً كيلا يصير تاركاً فرض القعدة أو واجبها، فإن وقع في رباعي أنها الأولى أو الثانية يجعلها الأولى ثم يقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى ويقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة يوهم أنه لا فرق بينهما لكنه قدم في التيمم عن أصول اللامشي أن أحد الطرفين إذا قوي وترجح على الآخر ولم يأخذ القلب ما ترجح به ولم يطرح الآخر فهو الظن، وإذا عقد القلب على أحدهما وترك الآخر فهو أكبر الظن وغالب الرأي ا هـ. ذكر العلامة ابن أمير حاج في أوائل شرحه على التحرير أن هذا الفرق غريب بل المعروف أن الظن هو الحكم المذكور ) . أخذ القلب به وطرح المرجوح أو لم يأخذ ولم يطرح الآخر ، وأن غلبة الظن زيادة أخرى
Contrary to if he doubts whether this takbir is the opening takbir or the qunut takbir, then he does not become a starter (of prayer) because the start is not established for him after he made it for qunut and he does not know he intended it to be for the opening. The meaning of 'istiqbal' (starting anew) is exiting the prayer by an act that contradicts it and entering another prayer. Starting anew with the salam while sitting is better because it is a known dissolver (of prayer) unlike speech, and mere intention is meaningless; he does not exit the prayer with it, thus they said. Its apparent meaning is that an act is necessary; if he does not perform a contradictory act and completes it based on his predominant opinion, it does not become invalid, except that it becomes supererogatory and it becomes incumbent upon him to perform the obligatory prayer if the prayer he doubted was obligatory. If it was supererogatory, it would be necessary for him to make it up even if he completed it because of the obligation of restarting. I have not seen this branch mentioned except that the commentator's statement that istiqbal is not conceivable except by exiting and that an act contradicting prayer is preferable indicates that it is not invalidated by mere doubt, as is not hidden. Taharrī is seeking the best opinion, which is what his predominant view indicates. They expressed it sometimes as zann (opinion) and sometimes as ghalib al-zann (predominant opinion). They mentioned that shakk (doubt) is equality of two matters, zann is preponderance of the side of correctness, and wahm (misgiving) is preponderance of the side of error. If nothing preponderates after seeking, he builds on the lesser: he makes it one if he doubts it is second, two if he doubts it is third, three if he doubts it is fourth. When building on the lesser, he sits in every place where he imagines sitting, whether the sitting is obligatory or wajib, so that he does not become a neglecter of the obligatory sitting or its wajib. If in a four-rak'ah prayer he thinks it is the first or second, he makes it the first, then sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah, then sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah, then sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah; thus he performs four sittings: two obligatory (third and fourth) and two wajib. However, al-Hidaya restricted its statement to 'he sits in every...' but then the passage discusses the distinction between zann and ghalib al-zann and the ruling on doubt whether a rak'ah is second or third. The commentator al-Ramli said: i.e., he doubts the rak'ah he stood up to whether it is second or third etc. If he doubts the rak'ah he stood up from whether it is second or third, he does not sit, and this is the correct view, because if it is third it is apparent, and if it is second, it was previously stated that when he stands up from the first sitting he does not return except in Maghrib and Witr due to the possibility that it is third and sitting is obligatory in them; so he performs tashahhud and stands and prays another rak'ah.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This dense passage concludes the discussion on doubt in prayer by defining key terms and outlining the method of building on the lesser number (al-bina' 'ala al-aqall). First, it distinguishes the case where a person doubts whether a takbir was for opening or for qunut: such doubt prevents him from having entered prayer validly because the intention is uncertain. The concept of 'istiqbal' (starting anew) requires exiting the current prayer by a contradictory action (e.g., salam) and then beginning again; mere intention is insufficient. If one completes the prayer based on predominant opinion (ghalib al-zann) without exiting, the prayer converts to nafl if the original was fard, and the fard must still be performed. The passage then defines three mental states: shakk (equivalent probability), zann (preponderance of correctness), and wahm (preponderance of error). Taharrī is the effort to arrive at the strongest opinion. If after taharrī no preponderance emerges, the rule is to build on the lesser number: e.g., if one doubts whether it is the second or third rak'ah, treat it as one (i.e., sit as if it is the second? Actually the text says 'he makes it one if he doubts it is second' meaning when in doubt between 1 and 2, treat as 1; between 2 and 3, treat as 2; between 3 and 4, treat as 3). While building on the lesser, one must sit in every position where sitting might be required, to avoid missing an obligatory or wajib sitting. The example given for a four-rak'ah prayer: if one thinks it may be the first or second, treat as first, then sit, stand, and continue, resulting in four sittings total. The passage also notes a dispute between al-Hidaya and others about whether to sit in all doubtful places. Finally, it addresses the difference between zann and ghalib al-zann: according to some, zann is when one side is stronger but the heart does not fully commit, while ghalib al-zann is when the heart commits to one side and discards the other. This distinction affects when one may rely on his opinion versus when he must build on the lesser. The section ends with a specific ruling from al-Ramli: if one doubts whether the rak'ah he has stood up from is the second or third, he should not sit (for tashahhud) because if it was third, he has already passed the sitting, and if it was second, the rule is not to return except in Maghrib and Witr.

Key Terms
الشك (al-shakk): Equal probability between two possibilities, requiring action on a lesser number or taharrī.
الظن (al-zann): Preponderance of one side over the other, but without complete commitment; still requires caution.
الوهم (al-wahm): Preponderance of the side of error; treated as unreliable.
البناء على الأقل (al-bina' 'ala al-aqall): Building on the smaller number of rak'ahs when doubt cannot be resolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is praying 'Asr (4 rak'ahs) and after the second rak'ah he doubts whether he is in the second or third, and after taharrī he has no preponderance, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He should assume it is the third and not sit until the end.
B) He should build on the lesser, treat it as the second, sit, and then continue with additional rak'ahs and sittings.
C) He should repeat the prayer from the beginning.
D) He should perform two extra rak'ahs of caution (ihiyat) without sitting.

Key Takeaway
When doubt in prayer rak'ahs remains unresolved after taharrī, build on the lesser number and sit in every potentially required position, then perform sujud al-sahw.

Rulings on Doubt (Shakk) in the Number of Rak'at During Prayer
Detailed cases of doubt in rak'at and their required actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedures when doubt arises about rak'at during prayer and apply them to common scenarios such as Fajr and four-rak'at prayers.

Core Idea
When in doubt about rak'at, rely on your preponderant opinion (taharri); if none, build on the minimum and perform sujud al-sahw.

Doubt about the number of rak'at completed is a frequent occurrence in prayer. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: if you have a preponderant opinion, act on it; otherwise, assume the smaller number and complete the prayer with sujud al-sahw. This lesson explores the detailed scenarios described in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, including the exact steps for doubt while standing, prostrating, or sitting, and the differences between two- and four-rak'at prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of prayer and moment of doubt
First, note whether the prayer is Fajr (2 rak'at) or a four-rak'at prayer (Zuhr, Asr, Isha). Also identify when the doubt occurs: while standing, prostrating, or sitting. This determines the required action.
Different rules apply for two-rak'at vs four-rak'at prayers.
2
Determine if there is a preponderant opinion (taharri)
If the worshipper has a strong inclination about the correct number of rak'at, he should act upon that opinion. If not, he must assume the smaller number and proceed accordingly.
If the doubt persists without any inclination, the prayer may become invalid in some cases.
3
Apply the specific ruling for the scenario
Using the rules from the passage, derive the exact steps. For example, if doubt occurs while standing in Fajr, sit immediately, then pray two rak'at and perform sujud al-sahw. If doubt occurs while prostrating, the ruling differs based on whether it is the first or second sajdah.
The text provides detailed sub-cases for each prostration scenario.
4
Understand the role of sujud al-sahw
In all cases where doubt leads to building on the minimum or acting on taharri, sujud al-sahw is wajib before the closing salam to compensate for the uncertainty.
If the doubt is resolved during the prayer, the need for sujud al-sahw may change.

A place where one imagines that he delayed his prayer so as not to become abandoning the obligation of sitting. So Al-Fath Al-Qadir attributed it to deficiency, and his excuse is that his sitting in a place where he imagines it is the place of obligatory sitting is not agreed upon, rather there is difference among the mashayikh as transmitted in Al-Mujtaba. If he is sitting and the case is the same, he tries to form an inclination: if his inclination falls upon that it is second, he continues on his prayer; if his inclination falls upon that it is third, he forms inclination in the sittings: if his inclination falls upon that he did not sit at the end of two rak'at, his prayer is invalid; if his inclination does not fall upon anything, his prayer is also invalid. His statement: 'that sajdah is elevated' etc. Al-Fath said: This also indicates contrary to what is in Al-Hidayah by what we presented in the recollection of a substantive (rukun) that repeating the rukn in which recollection occurs is mustahabb, and if we branch upon it, it should be invalid here due to the absence of elevation of the mentioned sajdah. His statement: 'it is invalid because of the possibility that he bound the third with the second sajdah and mixed the obligatory prayer with the supererogatory before completing the obligatory prayer, so his prayer becomes invalid' meaning the obligatory prayer. Thus in Al-Tatarkhaniyyah and in Al-Fath, and the analogy of this is that it becomes invalid if the doubt occurs after he raises from the first sajdah, whether he does the second sajdah first or not. His statement: 'then he prays another rak'a and recites tashahhud' to consider what is the reason for this tashahhud, for this rak'a is either the third or fifth and there is no tashahhud in them, unlike the previous one which he returned to being the second or fourth.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of doubt (shakk) during prayer regarding the number of rak'at performed, specifically within the chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. The author begins by discussing a subtle point: if a person sits in a place where he mistakenly imagines it to be the end of his prayer, this sitting is considered obligatory (fard) based on the apparent meaning of earlier texts. He then proceeds to detail various scenarios of doubt in prayer. For example, in Fajr prayer, if one doubts while standing whether it is the first or third rak'a, he must sit immediately for tashahhud, then stand and complete two rak'at and perform sujud al-sahw. If the doubt occurs during prostration, different rules apply depending on whether it is the first or second sajdah. The text also discusses the ruling when one's inclination (taharri) does not resolve the doubt, leading to invalidation of the prayer. In prayers of four rak'at, similar rules apply. The commentator then addresses a point from al-Halabi's commentary, clarifying that if one remembers a missed rukn during the sajdah, that sajdah is considered elevated, though there is disagreement with al-Hidayah. The passage emphasizes the importance of sujud al-sahw in all cases of doubt, whether one acts on inclination or builds on the minimum.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt about the number of rak'at performed, requiring specific actions.
التحري (al-taharri): The effort to form a preponderant opinion about the number of rak'at when in doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Fajr prayer, if a person doubts while prostrating that he has prayed two or three rak'at, and the doubt occurs in the second sajdah, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be restarted.
B) The prayer is valid and he should perform sujud al-sahw.
C) He should sit immediately and then pray one rak'a.
D) He should complete the sajdah and then perform sujud al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Doubt in prayer requires either acting on one's preponderant opinion (taharri) or building on the minimum, followed by sujud al-sahw.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Mistakenly Completing Prayer and Saying Salam
Ruling on forgetful salam and completion with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person mistakenly says salam before completing prayer, and apply the conditions that distinguish valid from invalid salam.

Core Idea
Forgetful salam does not nullify prayer; complete the missed rak'at and perform sujud al-sahw.

Imagine you are praying Zuhr and after two rak'at you suddenly say 'Assalamu alaykum', thinking you are done. Then you realize your mistake. What should you do? The Hanafi school provides a clear answer based on the Prophet's example. In this lesson, we will examine the ruling, its proof, and the important distinction between forgetful and deliberate salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
Read the opening sentence: if a person praying Zuhr imagines he has completed and says salam, then knows he only prayed two rak'at, he must complete the remaining two and perform sujud al-sahw.
The ruling applies when the salam is said forgetfully, not deliberately.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn (the man who told the Prophet he had prayed only two rak'at), where the Prophet stood up, completed the prayer, and performed sujud al-sahw.
This is a Sunnah ahad proof, considered zanni in thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action shows that a forgetful salam does not nullify the prayer; it is treated as a mistake that can be compensated by completing the prayer and doing sujud al-sahw.
The salam is considered a supplication in some respect, so it does not break the prayer.
4
Distinguish deliberate salam
The text states that if the salam is said deliberately (e.g., thinking one is a traveler or knowing a rukn is missing), the prayer becomes invalid. This is because the action is intentional.
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether deliberate salam invalidates unless intended to address a human.
5
Consider extensions
The passage also covers cases where a substantive sajdah is missed after salam, or where a follower joins after such a salam. The rulings depend on whether the person remains in the masjid, walks away, or has a sutrah.
These details are for advanced study; the core ruling is the first scenario.

And if a person praying Zuhr imagines that he has completed it and says salam, then knows that he prayed two rak'at, he completes it and performs sujud al-sahw. And if a person praying Witr doubts while standing whether it is his second or third, he completes that rak'a and performs qunut in it and sits, then stands and prays another rak'a and also performs qunut in it. That is the chosen view. Up to here is the expression of al-Khulasah. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention sujud al-sahw in the cases of doubt, following what is in al-Hidayah, which is something that should not be omitted, because sujud is obligatory in doubt in all forms, whether one acts on inclination or builds on the minimum. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And the investigator omitted a necessary condition which should not be omitted, which is that the doubt occupies him to the extent of performing a rukn, and he does not engage during the state of doubt in recitation or tasbih as we mentioned at the beginning of the chapter. But it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that in the chapter of building on the minimum, he performs sujud al-sahw, and in the chapter of building on predominant opinion, if his thought occupies him to the extent of performing a rukn, then sujud is obligatory, otherwise not. And it is as if in the chapter of building on the minimum, the deficiency occurs absolutely due to the possibility of increase, so a compensator is necessary, and in the second chapter, the deficiency is due to prolonged thinking, not absolute thinking. His statement: (And if a person praying Zuhr imagines that he completed it and says salam, then knows that he prayed two rak'at, he completes it and performs sujud al-sahw) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did so in the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, and because salam said forgetfully does not invalidate the prayer, as it is a supplication in some respect. He restricted it because if he says salam thinking he is a traveler, or thinking it is Friday, or he is new to Islam and thinks that the Zuhr obligation is two rak'at, or he is in the Isha prayer and thinks it is Tarawih and says salam, or he says salam while knowing that there is a rukn upon him, then his prayer is invalid because he is deliberate. And in al-Mujtaba: If a praying person deliberately says salam before completion, it is said to be invalid, and it is said it is not invalid until he intends thereby to address a human. Thus it should not be invalid in these cases according to the second saying. And his intention from his statement 'then he knows that he prayed two rak'at' is knowledge of the lack of completion, to include the case where he knows that he left a substantive sajdah or a tilawah sajdah after salam. And its ruling is that if he is in the masjid and has not spoken, he must perform it, even if he turned away from the qiblah, because his salam did not take him out of the prayer, so much so that if a person follows him as an imam after this salam, he enters. If he prostrates, he prostrates with him; if he does not prostrate, his prayer becomes invalid if the omission is a substantive one, and the prayer of the follower becomes invalid due to its invalidity after the correctness of the following, and the follower must make up the prayer. Even if he enters into a four-rak'at obligatory prayer, for example, he must make up four if the imam is a resident, and two if he is a traveler. And if he is in the desert and departs, if he passes beyond the rows behind him or to the right or left, it becomes invalid in the substantive omission, and the deficiency is established without compensation in the tilawah. And if his imam walks, it is not mentioned in the apparent narration. Its ruling is that if he has a sutrah, he builds as long as he does not pass it; if he does not have a sutrah, it is said that if he walks the distance of the rows behind him or more, it is prevented, and this is narrated from Abu Yusuf, considering one side like the other. And it is said: if he passes beyond his place of prostration according to the more correct view, because that amount is in the ruling of his leaving the masjid, so it prevents following. Thus in Fath. He returns and it is, unlike after it because it is fourth or sixth, so it should be checked. Then I saw in Fath he said in the issue: And if he doubts whether it is the fourth or fifth, or whether it is the third or fifth, then he mentioned the ruling as this, and it is apparent in the first only. His statement: (So it should not be invalid...) Al-Shaykh Isma'il said: It is apparent, and the first is the definitive view in many reliable books.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq continues the discussion on Sujud al-Sahw, focusing on the case where a person mistakenly thinks he has completed his Zuhr prayer and says salam, then realizes he only prayed two rak'at. The ruling is that he must complete the remaining rak'at and perform sujud al-sahw. The proof is the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) did exactly that. The reason is that a forgetful salam does not nullify the prayer because it is akin to a supplication. However, if the salam is deliberate or due to a wrong assumption (e.g., thinking he is a traveler), the prayer becomes invalid. The text then discusses nuances: if the omission is a missed sajdah (whether from the prayer itself or tilawah), and the person remains in the masjid without speaking, he should perform it even if he turned from the qiblah. If he walks out of the masjid or beyond his place, the ruling depends on whether he crossed the rows or had a sutrah. The passage also touches on the duty of the follower (muqtadi) if he joins after such a salam. Additionally, the text emphasizes that sujud al-sahw is obligatory in all cases of doubt, contrary to what might be inferred from al-Hidayah. The investigator adds a condition: the doubt must occupy him to the extent of performing a rukn, and he should not be reciting or performing tasbih during the doubt.

Key Terms
السلام (al-salam): The final salutation of prayer, saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'.
ساهياً (sahiyan): Forgetfully, without deliberate intent.
المتروك صلبية (al-matruk salbiyyah): A missed substantive part (rukn) of the prayer, such as a sajdah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, if a person praying Zuhr mistakenly thinks he has completed and says salam, then realizes he only prayed two rak'at, what should he do?
A) He must restart the prayer completely.
B) He should complete the remaining two rak'at and perform sujud al-sahw.
C) He should perform sujud al-sahw only and not complete the prayer.
D) His prayer is invalid and he must make it up later.

Key Takeaway
A forgetful salam does not nullify prayer; the remedy is to complete the missing rak'at and perform sujud al-sahw.

Salah — Prayer

Sujud al-Sahw: Forgetful Salam, Doubt, and Intentional Salam
Commentary on sujud al-sahw rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for forgetful salam citing the hadith of Dhu al-Yadain, distinguish between forgetful and intentional salam, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on intentional salam.

Core Idea
Forgetful salam does not invalidate; intentional salam's effect depends on intent.

Sujud al-sahw compensates for mistakes in prayer. The author opens with a common scenario: a person says salam thinking he completed his prayer, then realizes he only prayed two rak'ahs. He must complete and perform sujud al-sahw. This ruling is rooted in the Prophet's action. The passage also addresses doubt, intentional salam, and missed prostrations, revealing the school's nuanced approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic case and its proof
Read the opening scenario: person praying Zuhr mistakenly thinks he finished, says salam, then knows he only did two rak'ahs. Ruling: complete the prayer and perform sujud al-sahw. The proof is the Prophet's action in the hadith of Dhu al-Yadain.
The hadith is ahad, so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
2
Understand sujud al-sahw in cases of doubt
The author criticizes the omission of sujud al-sahw in doubt from the matn. He states that sujud is obligatory in all forms of doubt, whether one builds on the minimum or acts on predominant conjecture, provided the doubt occupies the mind for the duration of a pillar and the person is not engaged in recitation.
The condition of being occupied by doubt for a rukn's measure is essential.
3
Distinguish forgetful from intentional salam
The text restricts the initial ruling: if the salam is based on false assumptions (e.g., thinking one is a traveler) or done knowingly while a pillar is missing, the prayer is invalid. Intentional salam is different from forgetful.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on intentional salam
From al-Mujtaba: two opinions. One says intentional salam invalidates prayer; the other says it does not unless intended to address a human. The author prefers the second. Understand the reasoning: salam is like dhikr unless it becomes communication.
Practical difference: if intentional salam without addressing human, prayer is valid with sujud al-sahw; otherwise repeat.
5
Review rulings on missed prostrations after salam
If a person remembers a missed bodily or recital prostration after salam, the ruling depends on location and actions. In the mosque, without speech, he must perform it. If he leaves or speaks, the prayer may be invalid, especially for bodily prostration. Detailed cases from al-Tajnis illustrate complexity.
These cases show the depth of Hanafi fiqh in sujud al-sahw.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو

توهم مصلي الظهر أنه أتمها فسلم ثم علم أنه صلى ركعتين أتمها وسجد للسهو . ولو شك الوتر وهو قائم أنها ثانيته أم ثالثته يتم تلك الركعة ويقنت فيها ويقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعة أخرى ويقنت فيها أيضاً هو المختار إلى هنا عبارة الخلاصة. ولم يذكر المصنف رحمه الله سجود السهو في مسائل الشك تبعاً لما في الهداية وهو مما لا ينبغي إغفاله فإنه يجب السجود في الشك، جميع صور سواء عمل بالتحري أو بنى على الأقل. كذا في فتح القدير. وترك المحقق قيداً لا بد منه مما لا ينبغي إغفاله وهو أن يشغله الشك قدر أداء ركن ولم يشتغل حالة الشك بقراءة ولا تسبيح كما قدمناه أول الباب لكن ذكر في السراج الوهاج أن في فصل البناء على الأقل يسجد للسهو، وفي فصل البناء على غلبة الظن إن شغله تفكره مقدار أداء الركن وجب السهو وإلا فلا .اهـ. وكأنه في فصل البناء على الأقل حصل النقص مطلقاً باحتمال الزيادة فلا بد من جابر، وفي الفصل الثاني النقصان بطول التفكر لا بمطلقه قوله (وإن توهم مصلى الظهر أنه أتمها فسلم ثم علم أنه صلى ركعتين أتمها وسجد للسهو) لأنه عليه السلام فعل كذلك في حديث ذي اليدين ولأن السلام ساهياً لا يبطل الصلاة لكونه دعاء من وجه قيد به لأنه لو سلم على ظن أنه مسافر أو على ظن أنها الجمعة أو كان قريب العهد بالإسلام فظن أن فرض الظهر ركعتان أو كان في صلاة العشاء فظن أنها التراويح فسلم أو سلم ذاكراً أن عليه ركناً فإن صلاته تبطل لأنه عامداً. وفي المجتبي : ولو سلم المصلي عمداً قبل التمام قيل تفسد وقيل لا تفسد حتى يقصد به خطاب آدمي .اهـ. فينبغي أن لا تفسد في هذه المسائل على القول الثاني. ومراده من قوله «ثم علم أنه صلى ركعتين العلم بعدم تمامها ليدخل فيه ما إذا علم أنه ترك سجدة صلبية أو تلاوية بعد السلام وحكمه أنه إن كان في المسجد ولم يتكلم وجب أن يأتي به وإن انصرف عن القبلة لأن سلامه لم يخرجه عن الصلاة حتى لو اقتدى به إنسان بعد هذا السلام صار داخلاً فإن سجد سجد معه وإن لم يسجد فسدت صلاته إذا كان المتروك صلبية وفسدت صلاة الداخل بفسادها بعد صحة الاقتداء ووجب القضاء على الداخل حتى لو دخل في فرض رباعي مثلاً يلزمه قضاء الأربع إن كان الإمام مقيماً، وركعتين إن كان مسافراً وإن كان في الصحراء فانصرف إن جاوز الصفوف خلفه أو يمنة أو يسرة فسدت في الصلبية وتقرر النقص وعدم الجبر في التلاوة، وإن مشى إمامه لم يذكر في ظاهر الرواية، وحكمه إن كان له سترة بني مالم يجاوزها، وإن لم يكن له سترة فقيل إن مشى قدر الصفوف خلفه عاد أو أكثر امتنع وهو مروي أبي يوسف اعتباراً لأحد الجانبين بالآخر . وقيل : إن جاوز موضع سجوده عن الأصح لأن ذلك القدر في حكم خروجه من المسجد فكان مانعاً من الاقتداء. كذا في فتح القدير. وذكر في التجنيس : إذا سلم الرجل في صلاة الفجر وعليه سجود السهو فسجد ثم تكلم ثم تذكر أنه ترك سجدة صلبية إن تركها من الركعة الأولى فسدت صلاته لأنها صارت ديناً في ذمته فصارت قضاء وانعدمت نية القضاء، وإن تركها من الركعة الثانية لا تفسد إلا رواية عن أبي يوسف لأنها لم تصر ديناً في ذمته فنابت سجدتا السهو عن الصلبية ولو كانت المسألة بحالها إلا أنه لما سلم للفجر تذكر أن عليه سجدة التلاوة فسجد لها ثم تذكر أن عليه سجدة صلبية فصلاته فاسدة في الوجهين لأن سجدة التلاوة دين عليه فانصرف نيته إلى قضاء الدين فلا تنصرف السجدة إلى غير القضاء اهـ. وفي الظهيرية وإذا سلم ساهياً وعليه سجدة فإن كان سجدة تلاوة يأتي بها وفي ارتفاض القعدة روايتان والأصح رواية الارتفاض، وإن كانت صلبية يأتي بها وترتفض القعدة اهـ. وفي التجنيس : إذا صلى رجل من المغرب ركعتين وقعد قدر التشهد فزعم أنه أتمها فسلم ثم قام فكبر ينوي الدخول في سنة المغرب ثم تذكر أنه لم يصل المغرب وقد سجد للسنة أولاً فصلاة المغرب فاسدة لأنه كبر ونوى الشروع في صلاة أخرى فيكون ناقلاً من الفرض إلى النفل قبل إتمامها، وأما إذا سلم ثم تذكر أنه لم يتم فحسب أن صلاته قد فسدت وقام وكبر للمغرب ثانياً وصلى ثلاثاً إن صلى ركعة وقعد قدر التشهد أجزأه المغرب الأول لأن نية المغرب ثانياً لا تصح ، بقي مجرد التكبير وذا لا يخرجه عن الصلاة .اهـ ومسائل السجدات معلومة في كتب الفتاوى وغيرها فلا نطيل بذكرها والله سبحانة وتعالى أعلم بالصواب .
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. A person praying Zuhr thought he completed it, so he said salam, then knew he prayed two rak'ahs, so he completes it and prostrates for forgetfulness. And if a person in Witr is standing and doubts whether it is the second or third, he completes that rak'ah, performs qunut in it, sits, then stands and prays another rak'ah and performs qunut in it as well — that is the selected opinion, thus far is the wording of al-Khulasa. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention sujud al-sahw in the issues of doubt, following al-Hidaya, and this is something that should not be overlooked, for sujud is obligatory in doubt in all forms, whether he acts on investigation or builds on the lesser. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And the researcher omitted an indispensable condition that should not be overlooked, which is that the doubt occupies him for the duration of performing a pillar, and he was not engaged in recitation or glorification during the state of doubt as we presented at the beginning of the chapter. However, it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that in the section of building on the lesser, he prostrates for forgetfulness, and in the section of building on predominant conjecture, if his thinking occupies him for the measure of performing a pillar, sujud is obligatory, otherwise not. End. And it is as if in the section of building on the lesser, deficiency occurs absolutely due to the possibility of increase, so a compensator is necessary, and in the second section, deficiency is due to lengthy thinking, not its absolute. His statement: (And if a person praying Zuhr thought he completed it and said salam, then knew he prayed two rak'ahs, he completes it and prostrates for forgetfulness) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did likewise in the hadith of Dhu al-Yadain, and because salam forgetfully does not invalidate the prayer, as it is a form of supplication from one aspect. He restricted it because if he said salam assuming he was a traveler, or assuming it was Friday, or he was new to Islam and thought the Zuhr obligation is two rak'ahs, or he was in the 'Isha prayer and thought it was Tarawih and said salam, or he said salam while knowing that he has a pillar remaining, then his prayer is invalidated because it was intentional. And in al-Mujtaba: If the praying person says salam intentionally before completion, it is said it invalidates, and it is said it does not invalidate until he intends to address a human. End. So the appropriate view is that it should not invalidate in these issues according to the second opinion. And his intent by his statement 'then he knew he prayed two rak'ahs' is knowledge of incompleteness, to include the case where he knows he omitted a bodily prostration or a recital prostration after salam. Its ruling: if he is in the mosque and has not spoken, he must perform it, even if he turned away from the qibla, because his salam did not remove him from the prayer, to the extent that if a person follows him after this salam, he enters. If he prostrates, he prostrates with him; if he does not prostrate, his prayer is invalid if the omitted is bodily, and the follower's prayer is invalidated by its corruption after valid following, and the follower must make up. So if he entered into a four-rak'ah obligation, he must make up four if the imam was resident, and two if he was a traveler. And if he was in the desert and departed, if he passed the rows behind him, or to the right or left, it is invalidated in the bodily prostration, and the deficiency is established and not compensated in recital. And if his imam walked, it is not mentioned in the apparent transmission. Its ruling: if he has a screen, he builds as long as he does not pass it; if he does not have a screen, it is said if he walked the distance of the rows behind him, he returns, or more, it is prevented, and it is narrated by Abu Yusuf, considering one side like the other. And it is said: if he passes the place of his prostration, the correct view is that because that amount is in the ruling of leaving the mosque, it prevents following. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it is mentioned in al-Tajnis: If a man says salam in Fajr prayer while he owes sujud al-sahw, then he prostrates, then speaks, then remembers that he omitted a bodily prostration — if he omitted it from the first rak'ah, his prayer is invalid because it became a debt in his dhimmah, so it became qada', and the intention of qada' is absent. If he omitted it from the second rak'ah, it does not invalidate except in a narration from Abu Yusuf, because it did not become a debt in his dhimmah, so the two prostrations of forgetfulness suffice for the bodily prostration. And if the case were the same except that when he said salam for Fajr, he remembered that he owes a recital prostration, so he prostrated for it, then remembered that he owes a bodily prostration, his prayer is invalid in both ways because the recital prostration is a debt upon him, so his intention turned to paying the debt, so the prostration does not turn to other than qada'. End. In al-Zahira: If he says salam forgetfully while he owes a prostration, if it is a recital prostration, he performs it, and regarding the raising of the sitting, there are two narrations, and the correct is the narration of raising. If it is bodily, he performs it and the sitting is raised. End. In al-Tajnis: If a man prays two rak'ahs of Maghrib and sits for the measure of tashahhud, then claims he completed it and said salam, then stood and said takbir intending to enter into the sunna of Maghrib, then remembers that he did not pray Maghrib, and he had prostrated for the sunna first — his Maghrib prayer is invalid because he said takbir and intended to begin another prayer, thus he transfers from obligation to supererogation before completion. As for if he said salam then remembered he did not complete, and he supposed his prayer was invalid, so he stood and said takbir for Maghrib a second time and prayed three — if he prayed one rak'ah and sat for the measure of tashahhud, his first Maghrib suffices because the intention for a second Maghrib is invalid, only the mere takbir remains, and that does not remove him from the prayer. End. And the issues of prostrations are known in the books of fatawa and others, so we will not lengthen by mentioning them. And Allah, glorified and exalted, knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the chapter of Sujud al-Sahw from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author opens by stating the ruling for a person praying Zuhr who mistakenly thinks he completed his prayer, says salam, then realizes he only performed two rak'ahs. He must complete the prayer and perform sujud al-sahw. Similarly, for doubt in Witr, the relied-upon opinion is to act on the assumption that the doubt is about the second or third rak'ah and complete accordingly with qunut. The author then notes that the original text (Kanz) omitted sujud al-sahw in cases of doubt, following al-Hidaya, but this is a serious omission because sujud becomes obligatory in all forms of doubt, whether one relies on investigation (taharrī) or builds on the minimum (binā' 'alā al-aqall). He quotes Fath al-Qadir to emphasize that the doubt must occupy the mind for the duration of performing a pillar, and the person should not be engaged in recitation or tasbīḥ during that doubt. The author then explains the specific case from the matn: the Prophet's action in the hadith of Dhu al-Yadain establishes that salam forgetfully does not invalidate the prayer because it is like a supplication (du'ā'). However, if the salam is intentional or based on a false assumption about the nature of the prayer (e.g., thinking one is a traveler or that the prayer is Friday), it invalidates because it is deliberate. An intra-Hanafi dispute is cited from al-Mujtabā: some say intentional salam before completion invalidates, while others say it does not unless the person intends to address a human. The author favors the second opinion. The passage then discusses the implications of forgetting a bodily prostration (sajdah ṣalbiyyah) or a recital prostration (sajdah tilāwah) after salam. If the person is still in the mosque and has not spoken, he must perform the missed prostration and his prayer remains valid. But if he leaves the mosque or speaks, the prayer may be invalidated, depending on the type of prostration and other factors. Detailed rulings are given about following an imam in such cases, the effect of walking away, and the status of the follower's prayer. The passage concludes with several case studies from al-Tajnis and al-Ẓāhiriyyah, including scenarios involving Fajr and Maghrib prayers, emphasizing the complexity of sujud al-sahw rules and referring to fatwa collections for further details.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness or mistakes occurring in the prayer, such as omissions, additions, or doubts.
بناء على الأقل (binā' 'alā al-aqall): A method in cases of doubt where one assumes the lesser number (e.g., if unsure between two and three rak'ahs, one builds on the lesser, i.e., two).
التحري (al-taḥarrī): Acting on the basis of one's best judgment or predominant conjecture after reflection, used in cases of doubt.
سجدة صلبية (sajdah ṣalbiyyah): A bodily prostration that is an integral part of the prayer (i.e., a regular sajdah from the prayer itself, as opposed to a tilāwah prostration).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person deliberately says salam before completing his prayer without intending to address a human?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and no sujud al-sahw is required.
C) The prayer is valid but sujud al-sahw is wajib.
D) The prayer is invalid but sujud al-sahw is not required.

Key Takeaway
Forgetful salam does not invalidate prayer; sujud al-sahw compensates, but intentional salam based on false assumptions or with human address invalidates.

Ruling on Prayer of the Sick: Standing and Sitting
متن كنز الدقائق في باب صلاة المريض

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a sick person may pray sitting or by gesture (ima'), and apply the Hanafi ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Genuine inability to stand or fear of worsening illness permits sitting; only when even sitting movements are impossible does ima' become permissible.

Prayer remains obligatory for the sick, but Allah has provided concessions based on ability. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the primary ruling: if standing is impossible (ta'adhur) or would harmfully increase illness, the sick person prays sitting. If even sitting with bowing and prostration is impossible, he prays by gesture (ima'). This lesson unpacks the meaning of ta'adhur and the proper sequence of concessions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
The act is salah, which is wajib on every Muslim including the sick. The ruling concerns the manner of performing it.
2
Identify the condition for sitting
Ta'adhur: either genuine inability to stand (ta'adhur haqiqi) or fear that standing will worsen the illness (ta'adhur hukmi). This is the key condition.
3
Distinguish between sitting and ima'
Sitting: perform ruku' and sujud normally. Ima': only if even sitting with movements is impossible, then gesture with slight bow for ruku' and deeper for sujud.
4
Note the order of options
Stand if able; if not, sit; if even sit with movements is impossible, then ima'. This sequence is essential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعذر عليه القيام أو خاف زيادة المرض صلى قاعداً يركع ويسجد ومومياً إن تعذر القدير.
Standing becomes impossible for him, or he fears increase of illness; he prays sitting, bowing and prostrating, and (if even that is impossible) by gesture if the [؟] is impossible.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This is the opening matn of the chapter on the prayer of the sick from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The ruling statement gives the primary rule: if a person is unable to stand due to genuine inability (ta'adhur haqiqi) or fears that standing will worsen his illness (ta'adhur hukmi), then he is permitted to pray sitting. In the sitting position, he must still perform ruku' and sujud normally. Only if even sitting and performing bowing and prostration are impossible may he resort to prayer by gesture (ima') by slightly bowing for ruku' and lowering more for sujud. The text uses القدير which is unclear; in context it likely refers to the ability to perform ruku' and sujud. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تعذر (ta'adhur): In this context, the absolute inability to perform an action (like standing) without severe hardship.
قاعداً (qa'idan): Sitting position, typically cross-legged or on the knees, from which ruku' and sujud are performed.
مومياً (mu'iman): Praying by gesture, i.e., slight bowing for ruku' and lowering further for sujud when even sitting with movement is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a sick person pray sitting according to the Hanafi school?
A) Whenever they feel tired.
B) Only when standing is absolutely impossible or would worsen the illness.
C) Whenever they are over 70 years old.
D) Only if they are in the hospital.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits sitting prayer only when standing is impossible or would cause harmful worsening; ima' is an even further concession when sitting movements are impossible.

When Does a Missed Sajdah Invalidate the Prayer? The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
تفصيل أحكام السجدة المتروكة مع سجود السهو والتلاوة

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a missed sajdah from the first and second rak'ah, and state the ruling on prayer validity with the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding compensation by sajdah al-sahw.

Core Idea
A missed pillar sajdah becomes a debt only if a complete rak'ah intervenes; from the first rak'ah it invalidates, from the second it may not.

What happens when you finish your prayer, say salam, and then remember you missed a sajdah? The answer depends on which rak'ah the sajdah was missed from and whether you had already performed sajdah al-sahw. This lesson unpacks a series of cases from al-Tajnis, revealing a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a missed sajdah becomes a 'debt' on your liability that requires a specific intention of make-up (qada').

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the missed sajdah's rak'ah
Read the first case: the person performed Fajr, said salam while obligated for sajdah al-sahw, performed it, spoke, then recalled missing a pillar sajdah. Determine whether the missed sajdah was from the first or second rak'ah.
The ruling differs critically based on this distinction.
2
Apply the principle of 'debt in liability' (dayn fi dhimma)
If the missed sajdah is from the first rak'ah, a complete rak'ah intervened, making it a debt requiring an explicit intention of qada'. The sajdah al-sahw performed earlier was not intended as qada', so the prayer is invalid. If from the second rak'ah, no complete rak'ah intervened, so it does not become a debt and sajdah al-sahw can substitute.
This is the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
3
Compare Abu Yusuf's narration
Note that a narration from Abu Yusuf holds that even a missed sajdah from the second rak'ah invalidates the prayer. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical consequence is whether the worshipper must repeat the prayer or can rely on sajdah al-sahw.
The text presents this as an exception: 'except in a narration from Abu Yusuf'.
4
Apply to the tilawah and Maghrib cases
Examine the subsequent cases: if a tilawah sajdah is remembered first and performed, then a pillar sajdah is recalled, the prayer is invalid because the intention for tilawah does not cover the pillar debt. Also, in the Maghrib case, starting another prayer (sunnah) after mistakenly thinking the fard is complete transfers the intention, invalidating the fard.
These cases illustrate that intention and the nature of the debt are decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في التجنيس : إذا سلم الرجل في صلاة الفجر وعليه سجود السهو فسجد ثم تكلم ثم تذكر أنه ترك سجدة صلبية إن تركها من الركعة الأولى فسدت صلاته لأنها صارت ديناً في ذمته فصارت قضاء وانعدمت نية القضاء، وإن تركها من الركعة الثانية لا تفسد إلا رواية عن أبي يوسف لأنها لم تصر ديناً في ذمته فنابت سجدتا السهو عن الصلبية ولو كانت المسألة بحالها إلا أنه لما سلم للفجر تذكر أن عليه سجدة التلاوة فسجد لها ثم تذكر أن عليه سجدة صلبية فصلاته فاسدة في الوجهين لأن سجدة التلاوة دين عليه فانصرف نيته إلى قضاء الدين فلا تنصرف السجدة إلى غير القضاء اهـ. وفي الظهيرية وإذا سلم ساهياً وعليه سجدة فإن كان سجدة تلاوة يأتي بها وفي ارتفاض القعدة روايتان والأصح رواية الارتفاض، وإن كانت صلبية يأتي بها وترتفض القعدة اهـ. وفي التجنيس : إذا صلى رجل من المغرب ركعتين وقعد قدر التشهد فزعم أنه أتمها فسلم ثم قام فكبر ينوي الدخول في سنة المغرب ثم تذكر أنه لم يصل المغرب وقد سجد للسنة أولاً فصلاة المغرب فاسدة لأنه كبر ونوى الشروع في صلاة أخرى فيكون ناقلاً من الفرض إلى النفل قبل إتمامها، وأما إذا سلم ثم تذكر أنه لم يتم فحسب أن صلاته قد فسدت وقام وكبر للمغرب ثانياً وصلى ثلاثاً إن صلى ركعة وقعد قدر التشهد أجزأه المغرب الأول لأن نية المغرب ثانياً لا تصح ، بقي مجرد التكبير وذا لا يخرجه عن الصلاة .اهـ ومسائل السجدات معلومة في كتب الفتاوى وغيرها فلا نطيل بذكرها والله سبحانة وتعالى أعلم بالصواب .
And it is mentioned in al-Tajnis: If a man says salam in the Fajr prayer while he owes sajdah al-sahw, and he prostrates [for it], then speaks, then remembers that he left a pillar prostration: if he left it from the first rak'ah, his prayer is invalid because it became a debt in his liability (dhimma) and thus became a make-up (qada'), and the intention of make-up is absent; if he left it from the second rak'ah, it is not invalid except in a narration from Abu Yusuf, because it did not become a debt in his liability, so the two prostrations of sajdah al-sahw sufficed for the pillar prostration. If the case remained as it was except that when he said salam for Fajr, he remembered that he owes a tilawah prostration, so he prostrated for it, then remembered that he owes a pillar prostration, his prayer is invalid in both cases because the tilawah prostration is a debt on him; his intention turned to paying the debt, so the prostration does not turn to other than the make-up. In al-Zahiriyyah: If he says salam forgetfully and he owes a prostration, then if it is a tilawah prostration, he performs it, and there are two narrations regarding the rising from the sitting (irtifad al-qa'dah), the more correct is the narration of rising; if it is a pillar prostration, he performs it and the sitting is elevated. In al-Tajnis: If a man prays two rak'ahs of Maghrib and sits for the amount of tashahhud, then claims he completed it, says salam, then stands and says takbir intending to enter the sunnah of Maghrib, then remembers he did not pray Maghrib and he had prostrated for the sunnah first, then the Maghrib prayer is invalid because he said takbir and intended to start another prayer, thus transferring from fard to nafl before completing it. However, if he said salam then remembered he did not complete, so he thought his prayer had become invalid and stood and said takbir for Maghrib a second time and prayed three [rak'ahs] – if he prayed one rak'ah and sat for the amount of tashahhud, the first Maghrib suffices him because the intention for a second Maghrib is not valid; only the takbir remains and that does not take him out of the prayer. The issues of prostrations are known in the books of fatawa and others, so we do not lengthen by mentioning them. And Allah, glorified and exalted, knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a collection of case rulings from the work al-Tajnis, dealing with situations where a person forgets a pillar prostration (sajdah salbiyah) or a tilawah prostration after having performed sajdah al-sahw or after salam. The first case: A person performs Fajr, ends with salam while obligated to perform sajdah al-sahw, then prostrates for it, speaks, then recalls that he had missed a sajdah from the first rak'ah. The ruling: his prayer is invalid because the missed sajdah became a debt on his dhimma and required a specific intention of qada', but his intention during the sajdah al-sahw was not for that. If the missed sajdah was from the second rak'ah, it does not invalidate except in a narration from Abu Yusuf, because the sajdah al-sahw can substitute for it. The second case: He remembers a tilawah prostration first, performs it, then remembers a pillar prostration. The prayer is invalid because the tilawah prostration also becomes a debt and his intention was diverted. The third case (from al-Zahiriyyah): If he says salam forgetfully and owes a prostration, he can still perform it; if it is a tilawah prostration, there is a difference whether his sitting position is nullified; the correct view is that it is nullified (irtifad al-qa'dah). The fourth case: Someone mistakenly thinks he finished Maghrib, says salam, then starts sunnah, then realizes he missed Maghrib. His Maghrib is invalid if he intended to start another prayer. But if he simply re-enters Maghrib by takbir without valid intention, the first Maghrib may be valid if he performed one rak'ah and sat. The common misunderstanding is that any sajdah can substitute for another; the Hanafi school carefully distinguishes based on whether the missed sajdah has become a 'debt' (dhan) and the state of intention.

Key Terms
سجدة صلبية (sajdah salbiyyah): A prostration that is a pillar (rukn) of the prayer, i.e., one of the two sajdahs in each rak'ah.
ديناً في ذمته (daynan fi dhimmatihi): A legal obligation (debt) that becomes due on the person's liability, requiring specific fulfillment.
ارتفاض القعدة (irtifad al-qa'dah): The act of raising or nullifying the sitting position after salam, meaning the sitting is no longer valid and the prayer is considered ended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Tajnis, when does a missed pillar sajdah become a debt (dayn) on the worshipper's liability?
A) When the sajdah is missed from any rak'ah and the prayer is completed.
B) When a complete rak'ah intervenes between the missed sajdah and the end of the prayer.
C) Only when sajdah al-sahw has not been performed.
D) When the worshipper speaks after salam.

Key Takeaway
A missed pillar sajdah only becomes a debt requiring intentional qada' if a complete rak'ah passes after its omission; otherwise, sajdah al-sahw can substitute per the majority view.

Principles Behind the Sajdah Rulings
Extraction of four usul from al-Tajnis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi principles governing sajdah al-sahw and apply them to determine when qada' intention is needed for a missed sujud.

Core Idea
Hanafi principles: no order required, missed sujud attaches, salam doesn't break hurmah, qada' needed only after a full rak'ah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq extracts four foundational principles (usul) that underpin the detailed rulings on missing sujud in prayer. These principles are not direct rulings but legal maxims that guide the application of sajdah al-sahw. Understanding them is essential for correctly handling forgetfulness in salah according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
First Principle: Order of the Two Prostrations
Identify that the Hanafi school does not require the two sujuds of sajdah al-sahw to be performed in a specific order. This is a principle of leniency.
This differs from other schools that may consider order obligatory.
2
Second Principle: Attachment of the Missed Sujud
Understand that when a missed sujud is made up (qada'), it is considered as if it was performed in its original place, retroactively curing the deficiency.
3
Third Principle: Effect of Forgetful Salam
Recognize that salam given out of forgetfulness does not fully end the prayer; the sanctity (hurmah) remains, allowing corrective actions like sajdah al-sahw.
This is a key Hanafi position.
4
Fourth Principle: Threshold for Qada' Intention
Determine that a missed sujud only becomes a 'debt' requiring explicit qada' intention if a complete rak'ah has intervened. Less than a full rak'ah keeps it within its place (mahall), so no qada' intention is needed.
The concept of 'mahall al-rafd' (place of rescinding) is critical here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وذكر في التجنيس . . .) هذا مبني على أصول : أحدها أن الترتيب في أداء السجدتين ليس بشرط ثانيها أن المتروكة إذا قضيت التحقت بمحلها وصارت كالمؤداة في محلها . ثالثها أن سلام الساهي لا يخرجه عن حرمة الصلاة رابعها أن السجدة إذا فاتت عن محلها لا تجوز إلا بنية القضاء ومتى لم تفت عن محلها تجوز بدون نية القضاء، وإنما تفوت عن محلها بتخلل ركعة كاملة وبما دون الكاملة لا تفوت عن محلها لأنه محل الرفض وتمامه في التاترخانية وغيرها .
His saying: (And it is mentioned in al-Tajnis...) This is based on principles: First, that order in performing the two prostrations is not a condition. Second, that when the missed (prostration) is made up, it attaches to its place and becomes like one performed in its place. Third, that the salam of the forgetful person does not take him out of the sanctity of the prayer. Fourth, that the prostration, when it misses its place, is not valid except with the intention of make-up (qada'), and when it does not miss its place, it is valid without the intention of make-up. It misses its place by the interposition of a complete rak'ah; what is less than a complete rak'ah does not cause it to miss its place, because that is the place of rescinding (rafd). The completion of this is in al-Tatarkhaniyyah and others.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage extracts four foundational principles (usul) that underlie the detailed rulings on missing sujud and sajdah al-sahw. The commentator is explaining the legal reasoning behind the earlier cases. Principle 1: There is no requirement to perform the two prostrations of sajdah al-sahw in a specific order relative to each other. Principle 2: When a missed sujud is made up (qada'), it is considered as if it was performed in its original place, thus curing the deficiency. Principle 3: Salam given out of forgetfulness does not fully exit the prayer; the sanctity (hurmah) of the prayer remains, allowing corrective actions. Principle 4: A missed sujud only becomes a 'debt' requiring specific qada' intention if a complete rak'ah intervenes after its missed place. If less than a complete rak'ah intervenes (e.g., forgetting in the same rak'ah before moving on), the sujud can be performed without qada' intention because it is still considered within its place (mahall). The term 'rafd' (rescinding) refers to the option to abandon the current position and return to the missed act. These principles are crucial for understanding the Hanafi methodology in fiqh of prayer.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): Order between the two sajdahs of sajdah al-sahw; it is not a condition in the Hanafi school.
محل الرفض (mahall al-rafd): The place (in the prayer) where the missed act can be rescued without it becoming a debt; i.e., before a complete rak'ah intervenes.
حرمة الصلاة (hurmah al-salah): The sanctity or inviolability of the prayer that remains even after forgetful salam, allowing corrective actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principles mentioned, when does a missed sujud require the intention of qada'?
A) Always, whenever it is missed.
B) Only if a complete rak'ah has intervened after its missed place.
C) Only if it is a tilawah prostration.
D) Never, it can be made up without intention.

Key Takeaway
The four Hanafi principles provide a systematic framework for handling missed sajdahs in prayer, emphasizing leniency and structured correction.
