Defining Ta'adhur in the Prayer of the Sick
بيان المراد بالتعذر في المتن

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi concept of ta'adhur (inability) as distinct from ta'assur (hardship) and apply the correct threshold for permitting sitting in prayer.

Core Idea
Ta'adhur is genuine inability or harm; mere difficulty (ta'assur) does not excuse standing.

The text from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a critical distinction in the prayer of the sick: when does inability (ta'adhur) genuinely excuse standing? The Hanafi school distinguishes between real impossibility or harm and mere hardship, and this lesson unpacks the precise threshold based on Quran, Sunnah, and intra-madhhab discussions. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rulings on praying while sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term under debate
Identify the word 'ta'adhur' in the matn and note that the commentary is devoted to clarifying its meaning.
The commentator discusses whether ta'adhur means real impossibility, harm, or mere hardship.
2
Distinguish ta'adhur from ta'assur
Understand that ta'adhur (inability) is different from ta'assur (hardship). Inability makes an act impossible or harmful; hardship is possible with difficulty.
The text explicitly rejects equating ta'adhur with ta'assur.
3
Examine the proofs
Review the Quranic verse (Al 'Imran 3:191) and the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn, which provide the basis for the ruling.
The Companions interpreted the verse as permitting sitting when unable to stand.
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Note the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the ability to stand with support (qudrah bi al-ghayr).
This affects whether leaning on a person is sufficient to require standing.
5
Determine the mufta bihi threshold
Conclude that the relied-upon view is that ta'adhur requires either real impossibility (falling) or proven harm (darar) from standing.
Mere discomfort or difficulty does not excuse sitting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (إذا كان التعذر أعم الخ قال في النهر أقول : حيث أراد به الحقيقي لزم أن يكون الصلاة . شك أن فهم المراد من لفظ المرض أجلى من فهمه من قولنا معنى يزول بحلوله في بدن الحي اعتدال الطبائع الأربع، بل ذلك يجري مجرى التعريف بالأخفى وعرفه في كشف الأسرار بأنه حالة للبدن خارجة عن المجرى الطبيعي، والإضافة فيه من باب إضافة الفعل إلى فاعله كقيام زيد أو إلى محله كتحريك الخشب قوله : (تعذر عليه القيام أو خاف زيادة المرض صلى قاعداً يركع ويسجد) لقوله تعالى الذين يذكرون الله قياماً وقعوداً وعلى جنوبهم [آل عمران: ۱۹۱] قال ابن مسعود وجابر وابن عمر الآية نزلت في الصلاة أي قياماً إن قدروا، وقعوداً إن عجزوا عنه، وعلى جنوبهم إن عجزوا عن القعود ولحديث عمران بن حصين أخرجه الجماعة إلا مسلماً قال : كانت بي بواسير فسألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن فقال : صل قائماً فإن لم تستطع فقاعداً فإن لم تستطع فعلى جنبك. زاد النسائي : فإن لم تستطع فمستلقياً لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا وسعها. ثم المصنف رحمه الله أراد بالتعذر التعذر الحقيقي بحيث لو قام سقط بدليل أنه عطف عليه التعذر الحكمي وهو خوف زيادة المرض. واختلفوا في التعذر فقيل ما يبيح الإفطار وقيل التيمم، وقيل بحيث لو قام سقط، وقيل ما يعجزه عن القيام بحوائجه، والأصح أن يلحقه ضرر بالقيام. كذا في النهاية والمجتبي وغيرهما. وإذا كان التعذر أعم من الحقيقي والحكمي فلا حاجة إلى جعل التعذر بمعنى التعسر وأنهم لا يريدون به عدم الإمكان كما في الذخيرة وفي المجتبى : حد المرض المسقط للقيام والجمعة والمبيح للإفطار والتيمم زيادة العلة أو امتداد المرض أو اشتداده أو يجد به وجعاً اهـ هـ. قيد بتعذر القيام أي جميعه لأنه لو قدر عليه متكئاً أو متعمداً على عصاً أو حائظ لا يجزئه إلا كذلك خصوصاً على قولهما فإنهما يجعلان قدرة الغير قدره له . قال الهندواني : إذا قدر على بعض القيام يقوم ذلك ولو قدر آية أو تكبيرة ثم يقعد وإن لم يفعل ذلك خفت أن تفسد صلاته هذا هو المذهب ولا يروى عن أصحابنا خلافه وكذا إذا عجز عن القعود وقدر على الاتكاء والاستناد إلى إنسان أو إلى حائط أو إلى وسادة لا يجزئه إلا كذلك، ولو بمعنى التعسر لما قد علمت ا هـ . قلت : ولا يخفى ما فيه والذي يظهر أنه إن أريد به حقيقته وهو ما ذكره أنه مراد المصنف ونقله في الشرنبلالية عن الكافي أي بحيث لو قام سقط لا يكون المراد منه التعسر لأن المراد منه ما يمكن بمشقة وعلى ذلك المعنى المراد ما لا يمكن أصلاً فهو غيره، وإن أريد به غير ما أراده المصنف أعني الأعم من الحقيقي والحكمي فلا حاجة إلى جعله بمعنى التعسر كما ذكر المؤلف، وإن أريد منه ماهو الأصح أي بأن يلحقه ضرر بالقيام لزم أن يكون بمعنى التعسر تأمل قوله : (متكئاً) أي على خادم له كما في الخلاصة . قلت : ويشكل هذا على أصل أبي حنيفة رحمه الله من عدم اعتبار القدرة بالغير، وقد ذكر المؤلف في مسألة ما لو وجد من يوضئه ولو زوجته أو غيرها لا يجزئه التيمم في ظاهر المذهب، فنقل عن التجنيس هناك أن الفرق بين هذه وبين ما لو وجد قوماً
His saying: (If ta'adhur is general ...) He said in al-Nahr: I say: When he intended by it the real (ta'adhur), it necessarily follows that ... Doubt that understanding the intended meaning of the word 'illness' is clearer than understanding it from our saying 'a meaning that, by its settling in the body of a living being, removes the equilibrium of the four humors'; rather, that is but a definition by what is more obscure. And it is defined in Kashf al-Asrar as: a state of the body departing from the natural course. The genitive construction here is either of the action to its doer like 'standing of Zayd' or to its locus like 'movement of wood'. His saying: (Standing becomes impossible for him or he fears increase of illness; he prays sitting, bowing and prostrating) due to the saying of Allah, the Exalted: 'Those who remember Allah standing and sitting and on their sides' [Al 'Imran: 191]. Ibn Mas'ud, Jabir, and Ibn 'Umar said: The verse was revealed about prayer, i.e., standing if able, sitting if incapable, and on their sides if incapable of sitting. And due to the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn – recorded by all except Muslim – he said: I had hemorrhoids, so I asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about prayer. He said: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side.' Al-Nasa'i added: 'If you cannot, then lying on your back. Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' Then the author (may Allah have mercy on him) intended by ta'adhur the real inability such that if he stood he would fall, as evidenced by his connecting to it the legal inability, which is fear of increase of illness. They differed regarding ta'adhur: some said it is what permits breaking the fast; some said tayammum; some said such that if he stood he would fall; some said what incapacitates him from standing for his needs. The most correct is that harm befalls him by standing. This is in al-Nihayah and al-Mujtaba and others. If ta'adhur is general including both real and legal, then there is no need to make ta'adhur mean hardship (ta'assur) and that they do not intend by it impossibility, as is in al-Dhakhirah. And in al-Mujtaba: The definition of illness that drops standing and Jumu'ah and permits breaking the fast and tayammum is increase of the cause, or prolongation of illness, or its intensity, or that he finds pain from it. He restricted it to the impossibility of standing, i.e., all of it, because if he is able to stand leaning or supported by a stick or a wall, it is not valid except that way, especially according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), for they consider the ability of another as his ability. Al-Hindawani said: If he is able to do part of the standing, he should stand for that part, even if only for one verse or one takbir, then sit; if he does not do that, I fear his prayer would be invalid. This is the madhhab, and no contrary is narrated from our companions. Similarly, if he is unable to sit but is able to lean or support himself on a person, a wall, or a pillow, it is not valid except that way. And if (ta'adhur) meant hardship (ta'assur), as you have known. I say: It is not hidden what is in it; the apparent is that if what is intended is its real meaning – which he mentioned as the author's intention and as transmitted in al-Shurnublaliyyah from al-Kafi, i.e., such that if he stood he would fall – then it is not hardship, because hardship means what is possible with difficulty, while this meaning is what is absolutely impossible; so it is different. And if what is intended by it is other than what the author intended, i.e., the general (including real and legal), then there is no need to make it hardship as the author mentioned. And if what is intended is the most correct, i.e., that harm befalls him by standing, then it follows that it is hardship. Ponder his saying: 'leaning' i.e., on his servant, as in al-Khulasah. I say: This is problematic according to the principle of Abu Hanifah (may Allah have mercy on him) of not considering ability through another. And the author mentioned in the issue of one who finds someone to perform wudu for him, even his wife or others, that tayammum is not valid in the apparent madhhab. It is transmitted from al-Tajnis that the difference between this and the case where he finds people... (text breaks off)
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the word 'تفاعل' (ta'adhur) in the matn. It begins by discussing various definitions of illness (marad) and the legal meaning of inability. The commentator notes that the verse from Surah Al 'Imran and the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn provide the primary proofs for the ruling. The author of al-Hidayah (the sharh) clarifies that the matn author (al-Marghinani) intended by ta'adhur the real, physical inability (such that standing would cause falling), not mere hardship (ta'assur). He then reviews different scholarly opinions on the threshold for ta'adhur: some equate it with the excuse for breaking fast or tayammum, others require actual falling. The most correct (asahh) is that harm (darar) results from standing. The passage then addresses the issue of partial ability: if one can stand for part of the prayer, he must do so; leaning on a support is required if possible. A subtle point: Abu Hanifa's doctrine does not consider ability through another person (e.g., being supported by someone), but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do consider it. The commentator notes a potential inconsistency with Abu Hanifa's principle. The passage ends abruptly, likely continuing in the next page.

Key Terms
التعذر (al-ta'adhur): Real or legal inability to perform standing in prayer; either absolute impossibility or severe harm.
التعسر (al-ta'assur): Hardship or difficulty in performing an action, but still possible.
القدرة بالغير (al-qudrah bi al-ghayr): Ability through another person (e.g., being supported or assisted).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires genuine inability or proven harm (darar) to excuse standing; mere hardship does not suffice.

Sick Person's Prayer: When Standing is Impossible
Commentary on ruling, evidence, and definition of inability to stand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sick person who cannot stand, cite the evidence, and distinguish between impossibility (ta'addhur) and difficulty (ta'asur).

Core Idea
When standing causes harm or is impossible, the sick pray sitting — the obligation is tailored to capacity.

A sick person's ability to perform the pillars of prayer may be compromised. This lesson explains the key ruling from the Hanafi school: when standing becomes impossible—either absolutely or due to fear of harm—the person may pray sitting, bowing and prostrating normally. We will examine the Quranic and Prophetic evidence, then clarify the precise threshold of 'inability' that triggers this concession, distinguishing it from mere difficulty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة المريض الصلاة شك أن فهم المراد من لفظ المرض أجلى من فهمه من قولنا معنى يزول بحلوله في بدن الحي اعتدال الطبائع الأربع، بل ذلك يجري مجرى التعريف بالأخفى وعرفه في كشف الأسرار بأنه حالة للبدن خارجة عن المجرى الطبيعي، والإضافة فيه من باب إضافة الفعل إلى فاعله كقيام زيد أو إلى محله كتحريك الخشب قوله : (تعذر عليه القيام أو خاف زيادة المرض صلى قاعداً يركع ويسجد لقوله تعالى الذين يذكرون الله قياماً وقعوداً وعلى جنوبهم [آل عمران: ۱۹۱] قال ابن مسعود وجابر وابن عمر الآية نزلت في الصلاة أي قياماً إن قدروا، وقعوداً إن عجزوا عنه، وعلى جنوبهم إن عجزوا عن القعود ولحديث عمران بن حصين أخرجه الجماعة إلا مسلماً قال : كانت بي بواسير فسألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن فقال : صل قائماً فإن لم تستطع فقاعداً فإن لم تستطع فعلى جنبك. زاد النسائي : فإن لم تستطع فمستلقياً لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا وسعها. ثم المصنف رحمه الله أراد بالتعذر التعذر الحقيقي بحيث لو قام سقط بدليل أنه عطف عليه التعذر الحكمي وهو خوف زيادة المرض. واختلفوا في التعذر فقيل ما يبيح الإفطار وقيل التيمم، وقيل بحيث لو قام سقط، وقيل ما يعجزه عن القيام بحوائجه، والأصح أن يلحقه ضرر بالقيام. كذا في النهاية والمجتبي وغيرهما. وإذا كان التعذر أعم من الحقيقي والحكمي فلا حاجة إلى جعل التعذر بمعنى التعسر وأنهم لا يريدون به عدم الإمكان كما في الذخيرة وفي المجتبى : حد المرض المسقط للقيام والجمعة والمبيح للإفطار والتيمم زيادة العلة أو امتداد المرض أو اشتداده أو يجد به وجعاً اهـ هـ. قيد بتعذر القيام أي جميعه لأنه لو قدر عليه متكئاً أو متعمداً على عصاً أو حائظ لا يجزئه إلا كذلك خصوصاً على قولهما فإنهما يجعلان قدرة الغير قدره له . قال الهندواني : إذا قدر على بعض القيام يقوم ذلك ولو قدر آية أو تكبيرة ثم يقعد وإن لم يفعل ذلك خفت أن تفسد صلاته هذا هو المذهب ولا يروى عن أصحابنا خلافه وكذا إذا عجز عن القعود وقدر على الاتكاء والاستناد إلى إنسان أو إلى حائط أو إلى وسادة لا يجزئه إلا كذلك، ولو بمعنى التعسر لما قد علمت ا هـ . قلت : ولا يخفى ما فيه والذي يظهر أنه إن أريد به حقيقته وهو ما ذكره أنه مراد المصنف ونقله في الشرنبلالية عن الكافي أي بحيث لو قام سقط لا يكون المراد منه التعسر لأن المراد منه ما يمكن بمشقة وعلى ذلك المعنى المراد ما لا يمكن أصلاً فهو غيره، وإن أريد به غير ما أراده المصنف أعني الأعم من الحقيقي والحكمي فلا حاجة إلى جعله بمعنى التعسر كما ذكر المؤلف، وإن أريد منه ماهو الأصح أي بأن يلحقه ضرر بالقيام لزم أن يكون بمعنى التعسر تأمل قوله : (متكئاً) أي على خادم له كما في الخلاصة . قلت : ويشكل هذا على أصل أبي حنيفة رحمه الله من عدم اعتبار القدرة بالغير، وقد ذكر المؤلف في مسألة ما لو وجد من يوضئه ولو زوجته أو غيرها لا يجزئه التيمم في ظاهر المذهب، فنقل عن التجنيس هناك أن الفرق بين هذه وبين ما لو وجد قوماً قائماً استلقى لا يجزئه ودخل تحت العجز الحكمي ما لو صام رمضان صلى قاعداً وإن أفطر صلى يصوم ويصلي قاعداً، وما لو عجز عن السجود وقدر على القيام فإنه لا يجب عليه القيام. وما لو صلى قائماً سلس بوله ولو صلى قاعداً لا فإنه يصلي قاعداً بخلاف ما لو كان لو قام أو قعد سال بوله ولو استلقى لا فإنه يصلي قاعداً ولا يستلقي لأنها مستلقياً لا تجوز عند الاختيار بحال كما لا تجوز مع الحدث فاستويا وتمامه في المحيط : وما لو كان في بطنها ولد فأخرجت إحدى يديه وتخاف خروج الوقت تصلي بحيث لا يلحق الولد ضرر لأن الجمع بين حق الله وحق الولد ممكن كما في التجنيس، وما لو خاف من العد وإن صلى قائماً أو كان في خباء لا يستطيع أن يقيم صلبه فيه وإن خرج لم يستطع أن يصلي من الطين والمطر أنه قاعداً ومن به أدنى علة وهو في طريق فخاف إن نزل عن المحمل للصلاة بقي في الطريق فإنه يجوز أن يصلي الفرائض على محمله وكذا المريض الراكب إذا لم يقدر على النزول ولا على من ينزله بخلاف ما لو قدر على من ينزله واختلف المشايخ فيما إذا كان يستطيع القيام لو صلى في بيته ولو خرج إلى الجماعة يعجز عن القيام والأصح أنه يخرج إلى الجماعة قاعداً. كذا في الولوالجية وقدمنا في باب صفة الصلاة أن الفتوى على خلافه .
Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Sick Person's Prayer. Know that understanding the intended meaning of the word 'illness' is clearer than understanding from our saying 'a meaning that departs with its entry into the living body from the balance of the four humors'. Rather, that is like a definition by something more obscure. It is defined in Kashf al-Asrar as a state of the body outside the natural course. The addition (of 'prayer' to 'sick') is like adding a verb to its doer, e.g., Zaid's standing, or to its place, e.g., movement of wood. His saying: (Standing is impossible for him or he fears increase of illness, he prays sitting, bowing and prostrating) due to Allah's saying: 'Those who remember Allah standing, sitting, and on their sides' [Al 'Imran:191]. Ibn Mas'ud, Jabir, and Ibn 'Umar said: the verse was revealed about prayer, i.e., standing if able, sitting if unable for it, and on their sides if unable to sit. And due to the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn, recorded by all except Muslim, who said: I had hemorrhoids, so I asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about prayer. He said: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side.' Al-Nasa'i added: 'If you cannot, then lying on your back. Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' Then the author (may Allah have mercy on him) meant by 'impossibility' (ta'addhur) the real impossibility such that if he stands he would fall, as shown by the fact that he joined to it the ruling-based impossibility, which is fear of increase of illness. And they differed regarding impossibility: some said what permits breaking the fast; some said tayammum; some said such that if he stands he would fall; some said what incapacitates him from standing for his needs. The most correct is that harm would befall him from standing. Thus in al-Nihayah, al-Mujtaba, and others. And if impossibility is more general than real and ruling-based, then there is no need to make impossibility mean difficulty, and they do not mean by it lack of capability, as in al-Dhakhirah. In al-Mujtaba: The definition of illness that drops standing, Friday, and permits breaking fast and tayammum is: increase of the illness, or prolongation of illness, or its severity, or he feels pain. End. He restricted it to impossibility of standing, i.e., all of it, because if he can do it leaning or supported on a stick or a wall, it does not suffice him except like that, especially according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), for they consider the ability of another as his ability. Al-Hinduwani said: If he can do some standing, he should stand that much, even if just one verse or takbir, then sit; and if he does not do that, I fear his prayer would be invalid. This is the madhhab, and no opposition is narrated from our companions. Similarly, if he cannot sit but can lean on a person, wall, or pillow, it does not suffice except like that. And if (impossibility) were meant as difficulty, as you know. End. I say: What is in it is not hidden. It appears that if it is meant in its true sense, which he mentioned as the author's intent and he narrated from al-Kafi, i.e., such that if he stands he falls, then it is not meant as difficulty, because difficulty means possible with hardship, and that meaning is what is absolutely impossible, so it is different. If it is meant as other than what the author intended, i.e., the general including real and ruling-based, then there is no need to make it mean difficulty as the author said. If it is meant as the most correct, i.e., harm befalls him from standing, it would necessarily mean difficulty. Ponder. His saying: (leaning) i.e., on a servant of his, as in al-Khulasa. I say: This is problematic on Abu Hanifa's principle of not considering ability through others. The author mentioned in the issue of one who finds someone to perform wudu for him, even his wife or others, it does not permit tayammum in the apparent madhhab, and he narrated from al-Tajnis the difference between this and if he finds people standing... He lay on his back does not suffice him. And included under ruling-based inability is: one who fasts Ramadan prays sitting, and if he breaks the fast, he fasts and prays sitting; one who cannot prostrate but can stand, standing is not obligatory on him; one who if he prays standing has urine incontinence, but if he prays sitting he does not, then he prays sitting; unlike if both standing and sitting cause incontinence but lying does not, then he prays sitting and does not lie down, because lying down is not permissible when choice is possible, just as it is not permissible with impurity, so they are equal. And its completion is in al-Muhit: If a woman has a child in her belly and has put out one hand and fears that time will exit, she prays in a way that does not harm the child, because combining Allah's right and the child's right is possible, as in al-Tajnis. If one fears contamination even if praying standing, or is in a tent where he cannot straighten his spine, and if he goes out he cannot pray due to mud and rain, he prays sitting. One with a slight ailment on a road who fears that if he descends from the litter for prayer he will be left on the road, it is permissible for him to pray obligatory prayers on his litter. Likewise the sick rider who cannot descend and has no one to help him down, unlike if he can find someone to help him down. The shaykhs differed regarding one who could stand if he prayed at home, but if he goes out to the congregation he cannot stand; the correct view is that he goes out to the congregation sitting. Thus in al-Walwaljiyya. And we already mentioned in the chapter on prayer description that the fatwa is contrary to that.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling of a sick person's prayer. The author begins by defining illness not by the usual humoral theory but as any state of the body outside the natural course. The core ruling: if standing is impossible or harmful, the sick person prays sitting, performing bowing (ruku') and prostration (sajdah) normally. The evidence is the Quranic verse (Al 'Imran 3:191) which was interpreted by the Companions to refer to prayer positions, and the well-known hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn which explicitly commands: 'Pray standing; if you cannot, then sitting; if you cannot, then on your side; if you cannot, then lying on your back.' The author clarifies that 'impossibility' (ta'addhur) in the matn means absolute inability (e.g., if standing would cause falling) or the ruling-based impossibility of fearing increased illness. Various definitions are cited: some say it's the level that permits breaking the fast or tayammum, others say it's when standing causes harm. The relied-upon (asahh) view is that harm must befall him from standing. Then the text discusses nuances: if one can stand partially (even one verse), he must do so; if he can lean on a staff or wall, he must; if he can lean on a person, he must—but this is problematic with Abu Hanifa's principle of not counting ability through others except in certain cases. Numerous examples follow: the person with urinary incontinence, the pregnant woman, the traveler in mud, the sick rider, and the one who can stand at home but not in congregation. The fatwa on the latter is noted to be contrary to the preferred view mentioned earlier, meaning it is allowed to go to congregation sitting. Each example illustrates the principle that the obligation is tailored to capability, based on the Qur'anic principle 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.'

Key Terms
تعذر (ta'addhur): Inability; in this text, either absolute impossibility (like falling if stands) or ruling-based impossibility (fear of increased illness).
مرض (marad): Illness; defined as a state of the body outside its natural course.
تعسر (ta'asur): Difficulty; something possible but with hardship, contrasted with impossibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum level of inability (تعذر) that allows a sick person to pray sitting according to the relied-upon view?
A) Inability to stand even with support
B) That standing would cause harm or increase illness
C) That the person cannot attend the congregational prayer
D) That the person cannot find water for wudu

Key Takeaway
A sick person prays sitting only when standing is impossible or harmful; mere hardship does not lift the obligation.

The Ruling on Gesturing (إيماء) for the Sick in Prayer
Ruling on إيماء and its minimum requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gesturing (إيماء) for a sick person who cannot bow or prostrate, and identify the minimum gesture required.

Core Idea
Slight bending of the head suffices for ruku' and sajdah when physical pillars are impossible.

This lesson explores the ruling of performing prayer with gestures (إيماء) when a person is unable to bow or prostrate due to illness. The source passage clarifies the minimal requirement and the principle that obedience is according to capacity. Understanding this ruling is essential for knowing how a sick person may fulfill the obligation of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
The sick person cannot perform actual ruku' and sajdah due to illness or injury. The prayer obligation remains, but the manner of performance is modified.
Inability must be genuine; if able to bow even slightly, one must do so.
2
State the ruling
The person prays sitting and gestures (إيماء) by lowering the head: slightly for ruku', more for sajdah. This replaces the actual movements.
Gesturing is valid as a substitute; the prayer is valid and fulfills the obligation.
3
Analyze the minimum gesture
The text clarifies that a slight lowering of the head suffices. If the person can place cushions and affix the forehead, that is also allowed, but pure gesture is sufficient. If the forehead or nose is excused, only gesture is needed.
The key is that some bending is required; mere intention without movement is insufficient.
4
Recognize the legal principle
The ruling is based on the principle 'obedience is according to capacity' (الطاعة بحسب الطاقة), derived from Quran and hadith.
This principle governs the relaxation of pillars in cases of hardship.
5
Note the scope
The ruling applies when ruku' and sajdah are impossible. If one can perform them partially, that must be done before resorting to gesture.
The passage also mentions that placing the forehead on a cushion is a form of gesture, not full prostration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومومياً إن تعذر) أي يصلي مومياً وهو قاعد إن تعذر الركوع والسجود لما قدمناه، ولأن الطاعة بحسب الطاقة. وفي المجتبى : وقد كان كيفية الإيماء بالركوع والسجود مشتبهاً على أنه يكفيه بعض الانحناء أم أقصى ما يمكنه إلى أن ظفرت بحمد الله على الرواية ما وهو ذکره شمس الأئمة الحلواني أن المومي إذا خفض رأسه للركوع شيئاً ثم للسجود جاز، ولو وضع بين يديه وسائد وألصق جبهته عليها ووجد أدنى الانحناء جاز عن الإيماء وإلا فلا. ومثله في تحفة الفقهاء وذكر أبو بكر إذا كان بجبهته وأنفه عذر يصلي بالإيماء ولا يلزمه تقريب الجبهة إلى الأرض بأقصى ما يمكنه وهذا نص في بابه ا هـ . ثم إذا صلى المريض قاعداً بركوع وسجود أو بإيماء كيف يقعد، أما في حال التشهد فإنه يجلس كما يجلس للتشهد بالإجماع، وأما في حالة القراءة وحال الركوع روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجلس كيف شاء من غير كراهة إن شاء محتبياً وإن شاء متربعاً وإن شاء على ركبتيه كما في التشهد. وقال زفر : يفترش رجله اليسرى في جميع صلاته والصحيح ما روي عن أبي حنيفة لأن عذر المرض أسقط عنه الأركان فلأن يسقط عن الهيئات أولى كذا في البدائع وفي الخلاصة والتجنيس والولوالجية : الفتوى على قول زفر لأن ذلك أيسر على المريض ولا يخفى ما فيه، بل الأيسر الخلاصة يستعين بهم في الإقامة والثبات جاز له الصلاة قاعد أنه يخاف على المريض زيادة الوجع في قيامه ولا يلحقه زيادة الوجع في الوضوء إلا أن يراد بالغير غير الخادم كما يشعر به ما نقلناه. تأمل. وتقدم في باب التيمم ما يوضحه فراجعه . عن
His saying: (and gesturing if impossible) meaning he prays gesturing (mu'miyan) while sitting if bowing and prostration are impossible, as we have presented, and because obedience is according to capacity. In al-Mujtaba: The modality of gesturing for bowing and prostration was ambiguous as to whether a slight bending suffices or the utmost possible, until by Allah's praise I came across the narration that Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani mentioned: that the gesturer if he lowers his head for bowing slightly, then for prostration, it is permissible. And if he places cushions before him and affixes his forehead on them and finds the slightest bending, it is permissible as a substitute for gesturing; otherwise no. Similar in Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'. And Abu Bakr mentioned: if he has an excuse on his forehead and nose, he prays with gestures and is not required to bring his forehead close to the ground as much as possible. This is a definitive text in its chapter, end. Then if the sick person prays sitting with bowing and prostration or with gestures, how does he sit? As for during tashahhud, he sits as one sits for tashahhud by consensus. As for during recitation and during bowing (ruku'), it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he sits however he likes without dislike: if he wishes, sitting with knees drawn up (muhtabiyan); if he wishes, sitting cross-legged (mutarabb'ran); if he wishes, on his knees as in tashahhud. Zufar said: He spreads (yaftarish) his left foot in all of his prayer. The correct (sahih) is what is narrated from Abu Hanifa because the excuse of illness has removed the pillars, so it is more appropriate that it removes the postures (hay'at). Thus in al-Bada'i'. In al-Khulasa, al-Tajnis, and al-Walwaljiyya: The fatwa is according to Zufar's statement because that is easier for the patient. And what is in it is not hidden; rather, the easier is... al-Khulasa: 'He seeks help from them in standing and stability, it is permissible for him to pray sitting because it is feared for the patient increase of pain in his standing, and he does not suffer increase of pain in wudu unless the 'other' intends other than the servant, as is indicated by what we narrated. Ponder. And we previously mentioned in the chapter on tayammum what clarifies it, so refer to it. 'An'
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: the rule of gesturing (إيماء) when a sick person cannot bow or prostrate, and the debate on the correct sitting posture. The ruling on إيماء: if a sick person cannot perform ruku' or sajdah, he sits and gestures by bowing his head slightly for ruku' and more for sajdah. The text clarifies that a slight bow suffices; he does not need to bring his forehead to the ground if he can place it on something. If he has an excuse on his forehead or nose, he simply gestures. This is based on the principle 'obedience is according to capacity.' The second part discusses how a sick person sits during prayer if he prays sitting. By consensus, the tashahhud sitting is normal (iftirash). For the rest of the prayer (qiyam and ruku'), there are two views: Abu Hanifa says any sitting position is allowed without dislike (cross-legged, on knees, etc.) because the excuse of illness removes the major obligations (arkan), so it more readily removes minor postures (hay'at). Zufar says the sick person should sit in iftirash (sitting on the left foot) throughout the entire prayer. The text notes that in many later works (al-Khulasa, al-Tajnis, al-Walwaljiyya), the fatwa is on Zufar's view because it is easier for the patient. The author comments that this is not necessarily easier, but indicates that the easier method for the patient is to sit with iftirash, and that one should refer to the chapter on tayammum for more clarification. The passage ends with a note about seeking help in standing and stability.

Key Terms
إيماء (ima'): Gesturing by lowering the head slightly for bowing and more for prostration, used when unable to perform actual ruku' and sajdah.
مومي (mu'mi): One who performs إيماء in prayer.
افتراش (iftirash): Sitting on the left foot with the right foot upright, the normal posture in tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum gesture required for a sick person who cannot bow or prostrate?
A) He must bend his entire upper body as much as possible.
B) He must lower his head slightly for ruku' and more for sajdah.
C) He must place his forehead on the ground even if painful.
D) He must gesture with his hands as well as his head.

Key Takeaway
A slight lowering of the head for ruku' and sajdah is sufficient for a sick person to validly pray with gestures.

The Sitting Posture for a Sick Person: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting posture for the sick.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sitting posture for a sick person who prays sitting, and state the mufta bihi position according to later authorities.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa allows any sitting posture; Zufar requires iftirash; fatwa follows Zufar for ease.

This lesson examines the debated ruling on how a sick person should sit during prayer when unable to stand. While there is consensus on the tashahhud sitting, there is a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his student Zufar on the posture during recitation and bowing. The passage presents both views and notes that later authorities give fatwa on Zufar's opinion, citing ease for the patient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between sitting during tashahhud (consensus: normal iftirash) and sitting during recitation and ruku' (dispute).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa permits any comfortable sitting posture (cross-legged, on knees, knees drawn up) without dislike. His dalil: illness removes the pillars (arkan), so it is more appropriate that it removes the postures (hay'at).
This is the 'sahih' (sound) view attributed to Abu Hanifa in al-Bada'i'.
3
State Zufar's position
Zufar requires iftirash (sitting on the left foot) throughout the entire prayer. He considers it necessary to maintain the normal prayer posture as much as possible.
4
Analyze the tarjih
Later sources (al-Khulasa, al-Tajnis, al-Walwaljiyya) give fatwa on Zufar's view because it is easier for the patient. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq notes this but questions whether it is actually easier.
The text adds a note about seeking help from others for standing, which is a separate ruling.
5
Determine the current mufta bihi
The operative fatwa is on Zufar's view: the sick person should sit in iftirash during the entire prayer, including recitation and ruku'.
This is the position used in most Hanafi fatwa manuals today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومومياً إن تعذر) أي يصلي مومياً وهو قاعد إن تعذر الركوع والسجود لما قدمناه، ولأن الطاعة بحسب الطاقة. وفي المجتبى : وقد كان كيفية الإيماء بالركوع والسجود مشتبهاً على أنه يكفيه بعض الانحناء أم أقصى ما يمكنه إلى أن ظفرت بحمد الله على الرواية ما وهو ذکره شمس الأئمة الحلواني أن المومي إذا خفض رأسه للركوع شيئاً ثم للسجود جاز، ولو وضع بين يديه وسائد وألصق جبهته عليها ووجد أدنى الانحناء جاز عن الإيماء وإلا فلا. ومثله في تحفة الفقهاء وذكر أبو بكر إذا كان بجبهته وأنفه عذر يصلي بالإيماء ولا يلزمه تقريب الجبهة إلى الأرض بأقصى ما يمكنه وهذا نص في بابه ا هـ . ثم إذا صلى المريض قاعداً بركوع وسجود أو بإيماء كيف يقعد، أما في حال التشهد فإنه يجلس كما يجلس للتشهد بالإجماع، وأما في حالة القراءة وحال الركوع روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجلس كيف شاء من غير كراهة إن شاء محتبياً وإن شاء متربعاً وإن شاء على ركبتيه كما في التشهد. وقال زفر : يفترش رجله اليسرى في جميع صلاته والصحيح ما روي عن أبي حنيفة لأن عذر المرض أسقط عنه الأركان فلأن يسقط عن الهيئات أولى كذا في البدائع وفي الخلاصة والتجنيس والولوالجية : الفتوى على قول زفر لأن ذلك أيسر على المريض ولا يخفى ما فيه، بل الأيسر الخلاصة يستعين بهم في الإقامة والثبات جاز له الصلاة قاعد أنه يخاف على المريض زيادة الوجع في قيامه ولا يلحقه زيادة الوجع في الوضوء إلا أن يراد بالغير غير الخادم كما يشعر به ما نقلناه. تأمل. وتقدم في باب التيمم ما يوضحه فراجعه . عن

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa mentioned in the passage, what sitting posture should a sick person adopt during recitation and ruku'?
A) Cross-legged (tarbi')

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi for a sick person's sitting posture is to adopt iftirash throughout the prayer, based on later Hanafi fatwa.

Legal Inability and the Congregation Dispute in Sick Person's Prayer
Rulings on standing and sitting for the sick

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of legal inability (al-'ajz al-hukmi) to distinguish when a sick person may pray sitting, and state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding attending congregation when standing becomes difficult.

Core Idea
Legal inability excuses standing; but if you can stand at home, must you go to the mosque sitting?

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq presents a series of rulings on when a sick person may pray sitting. It introduces the concept of legal inability (al-‘ajz al-ḥukmī) and applies it to various scenarios including fasting, incontinence, pregnancy, and environmental hazards. The climax is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a person who can stand at home but becomes unable when going to the mosque: should he stay home and stand, or go and sit? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh individual obligations against communal rewards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle of legal inability
Find the term 'al-‘ajz al-ḥukmī' and note that it covers cases where a person is deemed legally unable to perform an act, even if physically possible under other conditions.
This is the key to understanding all subsequent rulings.
2
List the specific scenarios and their rulings
Go through the passage sequentially: fasting, inability to prostrate, incontinence, pregnant woman, fear of enemy, tent with mud, traveler on litter, sick rider. For each, note the ruling (pray sitting, stand, etc.) and the rationale.
Pay attention to the contrast: lying on back is never permissible if an alternative exists.
3
Analyze the reasoning behind each ruling
Identify the underlying principles: necessity (ḍarūrah), harm (ḍarar), combining rights (of Allah and of the child), and practicality.
These principles are also used in other fiqh chapters.
4
Focus on the congregation dispute
Locate the phrase 'ikhtalafa al-mashāyikh' and parse the two opinions: the most correct (al-aṣaḥḥ) is to go to the mosque sitting; but the fatwa in a previous chapter is contrary (i.e., pray at home standing).
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; both sides rely on valid evidence.
5
Determine the muftā bihī
The author indicates that the later relied-upon position (fatwa) overrides the earlier 'correct' view. Thus, the operative ruling is to pray at home standing.
This demonstrates the dynamic nature of tarjīḥ within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قائماً استلقى لا يجزئه ودخل تحت العجز الحكمي ما لو صام رمضان صلى قاعداً وإن أفطر صلى يصوم ويصلي قاعداً، وما لو عجز عن السجود وقدر على القيام فإنه لا يجب عليه القيام. وما لو صلى قائماً سلس بوله ولو صلى قاعداً لا فإنه يصلي قاعداً بخلاف ما لو كان لو قام أو قعد سال بوله ولو استلقى لا فإنه يصلي قاعداً ولا يستلقي لأنها مستلقياً لا تجوز عند الاختيار بحال كما لا تجوز مع الحدث فاستويا وتمامه في المحيط : وما لو كان في بطنها ولد فأخرجت إحدى يديه وتخاف خروج الوقت تصلي بحيث لا يلحق الولد ضرر لأن الجمع بين حق الله وحق الولد ممكن كما في التجنيس، وما لو خاف من العد وإن صلى قائماً أو كان في خباء لا يستطيع أن يقيم صلبه فيه وإن خرج لم يستطع أن يصلي من الطين والمطر أنه قاعداً ومن به أدنى علة وهو في طريق فخاف إن نزل عن المحمل للصلاة بقي في الطريق فإنه يجوز أن يصلي الفرائض على محمله وكذا المريض الراكب إذا لم يقدر على النزول ولا على من ينزله بخلاف ما لو قدر على من ينزله واختلف المشايخ فيما إذا كان يستطيع القيام لو صلى في بيته ولو خرج إلى الجماعة يعجز عن القيام والأصح أنه يخرج إلى الجماعة قاعداً. كذا في الولوالجية وقدمنا في باب صفة الصلاة أن الفتوى على خلافه .
Standing: if he lies on his back it does not suffice him. And included under the legal inability: if he fasts Ramadan, he prays sitting, and if he breaks the fast, he fasts and prays sitting. And what if he is unable to prostrate but able to stand, then standing is not obligatory upon him. And what if he prays standing and his urine flows, but if he prays sitting it does not flow, then he prays sitting. Contrary to the case where if he stands or sits his urine flows, but if he lies on his back it does not, then he prays sitting and does not lie, because lying on the back is not permissible at all when there is choice, just as it is not permissible with impurity, so they are equal. Its completion is in al-Muhit. And what if there is a child in her womb, and she brings out one of its hands and fears the departure of the time, she prays in such a way that no harm reaches the child, because combining the right of Allah and the right of the child is possible, as in al-Tajnis. And what if he fears an enemy if he prays standing, or he is in a tent where he cannot straighten his back, but if he goes out he cannot pray due to mud and rain, then he prays sitting. And one who has a slight ailment and is on a road, fearing that if he descends from the litter for prayer he will be left behind on the road, then it is permissible for him to pray the obligatory prayers on his litter. Likewise, a sick rider if he cannot descend nor find someone to help him descend, contrary to the case where he can find someone to help him descend. And the scholars differed regarding one who can stand if he prays at home, but if he goes out to the congregation he becomes unable to stand; the most correct is that he goes out to the congregation sitting. Thus in al-Walwaljiyyah, and we stated earlier in the chapter on the description of prayer that the fatwa is contrary to it.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings about when a sick person may deviate from standing in prayer. It begins by stating that lying on one's back is not acceptable if one has the ability to sit. Then it explains that 'legal inability' (al-'ajz al-hukmi) includes cases like fasting in Ramadan: if one is sick and prays sitting, that is valid, even if one breaks the fast later. Then it addresses specific scenarios: if a person can prostrate but cannot stand, standing is not obligatory. If a person's urine flows when standing but not when sitting, he must pray sitting. However, if urine flows whether standing or sitting but not when lying, he prays sitting rather than lying, because lying is not permitted when there is an alternative. The passage then covers a pregnant woman who fears for her child, a person fearing an enemy, a person in a tent with mud, a traveler on a litter, and a sick rider. A key point is the dispute about attending congregation: if a person can stand at home but cannot stand in the congregation, the correct view (al-asahh) is that he attends the congregation and prays sitting. However, the author notes that in the chapter on the description of prayer (Bāb Ṣifat al-Ṣalāh), the fatwa is contrary to this. This intra-Hanafi dispute shows that later authorities sometimes overrule earlier preferred views.

Key Terms
العجز الحكمي (al-'ajz al-hukmi): A legally recognized inability that permits a sick person to omit standing or other acts in prayer.
يخرج إلى الجماعة قاعداً (yakhruju ilā al-jamā‘ah qā‘idan): He goes out to the congregation and prays sitting, despite being able to stand at home.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fatwa (operative ruling) regarding a person who can stand at home but cannot stand when attending the mosque?
A) He should go to the mosque and pray sitting.
B) He should pray at home standing.
C) He should pray at home sitting.
D) He should delay the prayer until he can stand.

Key Takeaway
A sick person's obligation to stand is waived by legal inability, but the Hanafi school's later fatwa prioritizes standing at home over attending congregation when standing becomes impossible in the mosque.

Gestures and Sitting Posture for the Sick in Prayer
Rulings on gestures and sitting posture for sick

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making gestures (īmā') for ruku' and sujud when physically unable, and explain the dispute on the sitting posture between Abu Hanifa and Zufar, identifying the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Slight bending suffices for gestures; the sick may sit freely, but later fatwa prefers iftirash for ease.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rulings for a sick person who cannot bow or prostrate in prayer. It clarifies the minimal gesture required and addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute on the sitting posture during recitation and ruku'. Understanding these details ensures that the prayer of the sick remains valid while accommodating their condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the ruling is on making gestures (īmā') when one cannot bow (rukū') or prostrate (sujūd). The text states it is a substitute based on the capacity principle.
The ruling is derived from al-ṭā‘ah bi-ḥasab al-ṭāqah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: a narration from Shams al-A'imma al-Ḥalwānī that a slight lowering of the head for rukū' and then for sujūd suffices. Also consider the hadith from Ali (implied).
The narration is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for a wajib ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the narration establishes the minimal gesture: 'if he lowers his head slightly for rukū' and then for sujūd, it is permissible.' This indicates that extreme bending is not required.
The phrase 'شيئاً' (something) indicates a small amount.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on sitting posture
Examine the disagreement: Abu Hanifa allows any posture (cross-legged, on knees, etc.) while Zufar requires iftirāsh (spreading the left leg) throughout the prayer.
The ikhtilaf applies to recitation and rukū' positions; tashahhud is by consensus.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Khulāṣa, al-Tajnīs, and al-Walwaljiyya give fatwa on Zufar's view because it is easier for the patient, despite Abu Hanifa's view being considered 'asahh' (more correct).
The later preference shifts for practical ease (taysīr).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلي ويصلي : قوله: (ومومياً إن تعذر أي يصلي مومياً وهو قاعد إن تعذر الركوع والسجود لما قدمناه، ولأن الطاعة بحسب الطاقة. وفي المجتبى : وقد كان كيفية الإيماء بالركوع والسجود مشتبهاً على أنه يكفيه بعض الانحناء أم أقصى ما يمكنه إلى أن ظفرت بحمد الله على الرواية ما وهو ذكره شمس الأئمة الحلواني أن المومي إذا خفض رأسه للركوع شيئاً ثم للسجود جاز، ولو وضع بين يديه وسائد وألصق جبهته عليها ووجد أدنى الانحناء جاز عن الإيماء وإلا فلا. ومثله في تحفة الفقهاء وذكر أبو بكر إذا كان بجبهته وأنفه عذر يصلي بالإيماء ولا يلزمه تقريب الجبهة إلى الأرض بأقصى ما يمكنه وهذا نص في بابه ا هـ . ثم إذا صلى المريض قاعداً بركوع وسجود أو بإيماء كيف يقعد، أما في حال التشهد فإنه يجلس كما يجلس للتشهد بالإجماع، وأما في حالة القراءة وحال الركوع روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجلس كيف شاء من غير كراهة إن شاء محتبياً وإن شاء متربعاً وإن شاء على ركبتيه كما في التشهد. وقال زفر : يفترش رجله اليسرى في جميع صلاته والصحيح ما روي عن أبي حنيفة لأن عذر المرض أسقط عنه الأركان فلأن يسقط عن الهيئات أولى كذا في البدائع وفي الخلاصة والتجنيس والولوالجية : الفتوى على قول زفر لأن ذلك أيسر على المريض ولا يخفى ما فيه، بل الأيسر الخلاصة يستعين بهم في الإقامة والثبات جاز له الصلاة قاعد أنه يخاف على المريض زيادة الوجع في قيامه ولا يلحقه زيادة الوجع في الوضوء إلا أن يراد بالغير غير الخادم كما يشعر به ما نقلناه. تأمل. وتقدم في باب التيمم ما يوضحه فراجعه . عن
And he prays, and he prays: His statement: '(and making gestures if it is difficult)' meaning he prays making gestures while sitting if bowing and prostrating are difficult, as we have mentioned, and because obedience is according to capacity. And in al-Mujtaba: The manner of making gestures for bowing and prostrating was ambiguous, whether a slight bending suffices or the utmost possible, until by the grace of Allah I came upon the narration that Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani mentioned: that the gesture-maker, if he lowers his head slightly for bowing and then for prostrating, it is permissible. And if he places cushions before him and presses his forehead on them while making the slightest bending, it is permissible in lieu of gestures; otherwise not. The like is in Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'. And Abu Bakr mentioned: if he has an excuse on his forehead or nose, he prays with gestures, and it is not incumbent on him to bring his forehead as close to the ground as possible; this is an explicit ruling in its chapter. Then, if the sick person prays sitting with bowing and prostration or with gestures, how does he sit? As for the tashahhud, he sits as one sits for tashahhud by consensus. As for the recitation and the bowing, it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he sits however he wishes without dislike: if he wishes, cross-legged; if he wishes, with legs drawn up; if he wishes, on his knees like in tashahhud. Zufar said: he spreads his left leg in all his prayer. The correct is what is narrated from Abu Hanifa, because the excuse of illness has dropped the pillars, so it is more fitting to drop the postures. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Khulasa, al-Tajnis, and al-Walwaljiyya: the fatwa is on the statement of Zufar, because that is easier for the sick person, and its merit is not hidden. Rather, the easier: al-Khulasa: he seeks their help in standing and stability, it is permissible for him to pray sitting, because it is feared that standing will increase his pain, and he is not affected by increased pain in wudu, unless by 'others' is meant other than the servant, as suggested by what we have transmitted. Reflect. And what clarifies it preceded in the chapter on Tayammum, so refer to it. End.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of making gestures (īmā') in prayer for a sick person who cannot bow (rukū‘) or prostrate (sujūd). The commentator explains that the person sits and makes gestures with his head. The key proof is the principle that obedience is required according to one's capacity (al-ṭā‘ah bi-ḥasab al-ṭāqah). There was ambiguity about whether a slight bending suffices or one must bend as far as possible. The author clarifies that based on a narration from Shams al-A'imma al-Ḥalwānī, lowering the head slightly for rukū‘ and then more for sujūd is permissible. If cushions are placed and the forehead touches them with minimal bending, that substitutes for gestures. This is also found in Tuḥfat al-Fuqahā'. Abū Bakr adds that if there is an excuse on the forehead or nose, the person may use gestures without being required to bring the face as low as possible. The passage then addresses the sitting posture for a sick person who prays sitting with actual bowing/prostration or with gestures. During tashahhud, the sitting is according to the usual manner by consensus. For the recitation and rukū‘ positions, Abū Ḥanīfa allowed any sitting posture (cross-legged, on knees, etc.) without dislike, reasoning that since the pillars (arkān) are dropped due to illness, the postures (hay’āt) are even more deserving of being dropped. Zufar required the left leg to be spread (iftirāsh) throughout the prayer. The author states that the correct view (aṣ-ṣaḥīḥ) is Abū Ḥanīfa’s, citing al-Badā’i‘. However, later sources (al-Khulāṣa, al-Tajnīs, al-Walwaljiyya) say the fatwa is on Zufar’s view because it is easier for the sick person. This shows the later preference for ease. Finally, the passage includes a note from al-Khulāṣa about a sick person seeking help to stand: if he fears increased pain from standing, he may pray sitting; similarly, wuḍū’ does not cause increased pain unless the helper is a non-servant. The author directs the reader to the chapter on Tayammum for further clarification.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Gesturing with the head to replace bowing and prostration when physically unable.
مومي (mūmī): A person who performs īmā’ in prayer.
يفترش (yaftarish): To spread the left leg and sit on it (iftirāsh), a specific sitting posture in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later fatwa (al-muftā bihi), what sitting posture should a sick person adopt when praying sitting with gestures?
A) Any posture he wishes (cross-legged, etc.)
B) Iftirāsh (spreading the left leg)
C) Lying on his back
D) Standing

Key Takeaway
A slight gesture suffices; while Abu Hanifa allowed any sitting, the fatwa is on Zufar's iftirāsh for ease.

Obligation to Make Prostration Gesture Lower than Bowing
Hanafi ruling on sick person's ima' and prohibition of raising object to face.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the required difference between bowing and prostration gestures for the sick, and apply it to scenarios involving gesture equality or raising objects.

Core Idea
The prostration gesture must be lower than the bowing gesture; equality invalidates the prayer.

When a sick person cannot perform physical prayer postures, gesture (ima') substitutes for bowing and prostration. A critical condition in the Hanafi school is that the gesture for prostration must be visibly lower (closer to the ground) than the gesture for bowing. This lesson explains the basis of this ruling through hadith and the conditions for validity, including the prohibition of raising an object to the face.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The sick person's gesture (ima') replaces bowing and prostration. The ruling requires the prostration gesture to be lower than the bowing gesture.
This is considered wajib; omission invalidates the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from 'Ali and another from the Prophet explicitly commanding the prostration gesture to be lower.
The hadith is ahad, so it gives zanni evidence, but it is sufficient for obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'let him make his prostration lower' indicates obligation (amr yufid al-wujub) absent a contrary indicator.
No counter-indication exists; thus the ruling is wajib.
4
Note the condition regarding raising objects
Raising an object to the face does not count as gesture unless the head is lowered appropriately. If the head is lowered more than for bowing, it is valid; otherwise invalid.
The act of raising itself is makruh tahrimi, but it does not invalidate if the head movement is correct.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some scholars allow equality of gestures, but the Hanafi school insists on the distinct lowering based on the explicit hadith.
The practical difference: equality would invalidate in Hanafi, but may be valid in other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجعل سجوده أخفض ولا يرفع إلى وجهه شيئاً يسجد عليه فإن فعل وهو يخفض رأسه صح وإلا لا. قوله : (وجعل سجوده أخفض) أي أخفض من ركوعه لأنه قائم مقامهما فأخذ حكمهما، وعن علي رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال في صلاة المريض : إن لم يستطع أن يسجد أومأ وجعل سجوده أخفض من ركوعه. وروي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال من لم يقدر على السجود فليجعل سجوده ركوعاً وركوعه إيماء والركوع أخفض من الإيماء» كذا في البدائع. وظاهره كغيره أنه يلزمه جعل السجود أخفض من الركوع حتى لو سواهما لا يصح ويدل عليه أيضاً ما سيأتي قوله : (ولا يرفع إلى وجهه شيئاً يسجد عليه فإن فعل وهو يخفض رأسه صح وإلا لا أي وإن لم يخفض رأسه لم يجز لأن الفرض في حقه الإيماء ولم يوجد فإن لم يخفض فهو حرام لبطلان الصلاة المنهي عنه بقوله تعالى ولا تبطلوا أعمالكم [محمد : ٣٣] وأما نفس الرفع المذكور فمكروه، وصرح به في البدائع وغيره لما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم دخل على مريض يعوده فوجده يصلي كذلك فقال : إن قدرت أن تسجد على الأرض فاسجد وإلا فأوم برأسك. وروي أن عبد الله بن مسعود دخل على أخيه يعوده فوجده يصلي ويرفع إليه عود ذلك فيسجد عليه فنزع العود من يد من كان في يده وقال : هذا شيء عرض لكم الشيطان أوم بسجودك . وروي أن ابن عمر رأى ذلك من مريض فقال : أتتخذون مع الله آلهة؟ ا هـ . للكراهة في المحيط بنهيه عليه السلام عنه وهو يدل على كراهة التحريم. وأراد بخفض الرأس خفضها للركوع ثم للسجود أخفض من الركوع حتى لو سوى لم يصح كما ذكره الولوالجي في فتاواه. ولو رفع المريض شيئاً يسجد عليه ولم يقدر على الأرض لم يجز إلا أن يخفض برأسه لسجوده أكثر من ركوعه ثم يلزقه بجبينه فيجوز لأنه لما عجز عن السجود وجب عليه الإيماء والسجود على الشيء المرفوع ليس بالإيماء إلا إذا حرك رأسه فيجوز لوجود الإيماء لا لوجود السجود على ذلك الشيء ا هـ . وصححه في الخلاصة.
And he should make his prostration lower, and he should not raise to his face something to prostrate on. If he does so while lowering his head, it is valid; otherwise not. His statement: 'And he should make his prostration lower' means lower than his bowing, because it (the gesture) stands in place of both (bowing and prostration) and thus takes their ruling. And it is narrated from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding the prayer of the sick: 'If he cannot prostrate, let him gesture and make his prostration gesture lower than his bowing gesture.' And it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Whoever cannot prostrate, let him make his prostration a bowing and his bowing a gesture, and the bowing gesture should be lower than the prostration gesture.' This is in al-Bada'i'. Its apparent meaning, like other texts, is that it is obligatory for him to make prostration lower than bowing, so that if he makes them equal, it is not valid. This is also indicated by what will come in his statement: 'And he should not raise to his face something to prostrate on. If he does so while lowering his head, it is valid; otherwise not.' That is, if he does not lower his head, it is not permissible, because the obligation in his case is gesture, and it has not occurred. If he does not lower (his head), it is sinful, because the prayer becomes invalid, which is prohibited by Allah's statement: 'And do not invalidate your deeds' [Muhammad: 33]. As for the act of raising (the object) itself, it is disliked (makruh), as explicitly stated in al-Bada'i' and others. This is due to the report that the Prophet (peace be upon him) entered upon a sick person visiting him and found him praying like that, so he said: 'If you can prostrate on the ground, then prostrate; otherwise, gesture with your head.' And it is reported that 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud entered upon his brother visiting him and found him praying, raising a stick to his face to prostrate on, so he took the stick from his hand and said: 'This is something the devil has presented to you; gesture with your prostration.' And it is reported that Ibn 'Umar saw a sick person doing that and said: 'Do you take gods besides Allah?' This indicates dislike (karahah) in al-Muhit due to the Prophet's prohibition of it, which indicates prohibition-level dislike. By 'lowering the head' he means lowering it for bowing, then for prostration it should be lower than for bowing, so that if he makes them equal, it is not valid, as mentioned by al-Walwaliji in his fatwas. And if a sick person raises something to prostrate on and cannot (prostrate) on the ground, it is not permissible unless he lowers his head for his prostration more than his bowing and then attaches it (the raised object) to his forehead; then it is permissible, because when he is unable to prostrate, gesture is obligatory, and prostrating on a raised object is not gesture unless he moves his head; then it is permissible due to the presence of gesture, not due to the presence of prostration on that object. This is as stated and verified in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with proof. It addresses the prayer of a sick person who can perform gestures (ima') instead of actual bowing and prostration. The key ruling is that the gesture for prostration must be lower (closer to the ground) than the gesture for bowing. This is based on several hadith, including one from 'Ali and another from the Prophet. The commentators explain that if the sick person makes both gestures equal, the prayer is invalid. Additionally, the sick person is prohibited from raising an object (like a stone or piece of wood) to his face to prostrate on it; if he does so while also lowering his head appropriately, the prayer is valid because the gesture is still performed. However, if he does not lower his head, the prayer is invalid. The act of raising an object itself is considered makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) based on the Prophet's prohibition and the actions of the Companions. The text also clarifies that if the sick person cannot prostrate on the ground, he must gesture; raising an object to the face does not count as a valid prostration unless accompanied by a head movement that is more pronounced than the bowing gesture. This ruling ensures that the prayer maintains the required order and distinction between the postures.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā’): A gesture of the head or body to replace the physical postures of prayer when unable to perform them due to illness or impediment.
رفع (raf‘): The act of raising an object (like a stone or stick) to the face to prostrate on, which is makruh tahrimi in Hanafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sick person cannot prostrate on the ground but raises a cushion to his forehead and bows his head slightly (less than his bowing gesture), what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because he did not make the prostration gesture lower than the bowing gesture.
B) The prayer is valid because he prostrated on the cushion.
C) The prayer is valid only if the cushion is on the floor.
D) The prayer is invalid because he should have gestured with his nose.

Key Takeaway
The prostration gesture must be distinctly lower than the bowing gesture; equality or merely raising an object without proper head movement invalidates the prayer.

Ruling on Gesturing When Sitting is Impossible in Sick Prayer
Hanafi ruling on sick person's prayer posture hierarchy with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of postures for the sick person's prayer and apply the Hanafi ruling on gesturing when sitting is impossible.

Core Idea
When sitting is impossible, the sick person must gesture while lying on his back, then on his side; only if incapable of gesture does he delay.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling for a sick person who cannot sit during prayer. It establishes a clear sequence of postures based on capability, and addresses an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab discussion about the preferred method. The rule is rooted in the principle that obedience is according to ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the sick person is required to do (where the act of prayer fits) and what ruling applies: wajib (obligatory) to gesture when unable to sit.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the proof is zanni (ahad hadith).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: a hadith narrated by 'Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that indicates the sick person should gesture while lying on his back.
The hadith text is cut off in the passage but is identified as the proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling: it shows that the one lying on his back can face the qibla with his face, which is the goal, while lying on the side or back achieves the orientation.
The Hanafi position prefers lying on the back because the face is directed to the sky, but the feet are towards the qibla; the hadith supports this.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa himself considered the right side superior, and Imam al-Shafi'i also prefers the side based on a different hadith and the Quranic verse about the dying.
The passage discusses both intra-Hanafi (Abu Hanifa vs. the well-known view) and inter-madhhab (Shafi'i) differences.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude the operative ruling: the well-known (zahir al-riwayah) position is to lie on the back; if not possible, then on the side; if even gesture is impossible, delay the prayer.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and al-Kasani in al-Bada'i' adopt this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن تعذر القعود أومأ مستلقياً أو على جنبه وإلا أخرت ولم يوم بعينه. قوله : (وإن تعذر القعود أومأ مستلقياً أو على جنبه) لأن الطاعة الاستطاعة. بحسب الاستلقاء على القفا والاضطجاع على الجنب جواب الكتب المشهورة كالهداية وشروحها. وفي القنية : مريض اضطجع على جنبه وصلى وهو قادر على الاستلقاء، وقيل يجوز والأظهر أنه لا يجوز. وإن تعذر الاستلقاء يضطجع على شقه الأيمن أو الأيسر ووجهه إلى القبلة ا هـ . وهذا الأظهر خفي والأظهر الجواز. وقدم المصنف الاستلقاء لبيان الأفضل وهو جواب المشهور من الروايات وعن أبي حنيفة أن الأفضل أن يصلي على شقه الأيمن . أخذ به الشافعي لحديث عمران بن حصين السابق وللتصريح به في الآية، ولأن استقبال القبلة يحصل به، ولهذا يوضع في اللحد هكذا ليكون مستقبلاً للقبلة. فأما المستلقي يكون مستقبل السماء وإنما يستقبل القبلة رجلاه فقط ولنا ما روي عن عمر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال
And if sitting is impossible, he should gesture while lying on his back or on his side; otherwise, he delays (the prayer) and does not gesture with his eyes. His statement: 'And if sitting is impossible, he should gesture while lying on his back or on his side' because obedience is according to ability. The answer from the famous books like al-Hidayah and its commentaries is regarding lying on the back (supine) and lying on the side (lateral). In al-Quniya: A sick person who lies on his side and prays while he is able to lie on his back: it is said it is permissible, but the most apparent is that it is not permissible. And if lying on the back is impossible, he lies on his right side or left side with his face towards the qibla. This 'most apparent' view is obscure, and the most apparent view is that it is permissible. The author gave precedence to lying on the back to indicate it is superior, which is the answer of the well-known narrations. And from Abu Hanifa that the superior way is to pray on his right side. Al-Shafi'i took this due to the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn mentioned earlier and because it is explicitly mentioned in the verse, and because facing the qibla is achieved by it; therefore the deceased is placed in the grave in this way to face the qibla. As for the one lying on his back, he faces the sky, and only his feet face the qibla. And we have (as proof) what is narrated from 'Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said...
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with proof regarding the prayer of a sick person who cannot even sit. The ruling is that such a person should perform gestures (ima') while lying on his back (supine) or on his side (lateral), with the face towards the qibla. If even this is impossible—for example, if he cannot move his head at all—then he does not gesture with his eyes (i.e., no ima' with eyelids), but delays the prayer until he recovers. This is based on the principle that 'obedience is according to ability' (al-ta'a bi-qadr al-istita'a). The text discusses a difference of opinion: if the sick person can lie on his back but chooses to lie on his side, the most apparent view is that this is not permissible; however, another view allows it. The superior position according to Imam Abu Hanifa is to lie on the right side, facing the qibla, similar to how the deceased is placed in the grave. Imam al-Shafi'i also holds this view based on a hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn and the Quranic verse that mentions the dying person should be on his right side. The Hanafi response relies on a hadith from 'Umar (which is cut off here) to support that the sick person should gesture while lying on his back if possible. The passage shows the hierarchy of postures: standing > sitting > lying on back > lying on side > delay if unable to gesture.

Key Terms
مستلقيا (mustalqiyan): Lying on one's back, facing upward, with the soles of the feet towards the qibla.
على جنبه ('ala janbihi): Lying on one's side (right or left) with face towards the qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A sick person cannot sit for prayer and also cannot lie on his back. What should he do?
A) Gesture with his eyes and continue.
B) Lie on his side and gesture.
C) Delay the prayer until he recovers.
D) Perform the prayer in his mind without movement.

Key Takeaway
The sick person must gesture while lying on his back; if unable, on his side; otherwise, delay the prayer.

Posture of the Sick: Lying on Back with Gestures
Ruling with qiyas proof on sick person's prayer posture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sick person who cannot sit, explain the qiyas proof, and apply the ruling to cases of legal inability (e.g., doctor's orders).

Core Idea
When unable to sit, lying on back with gestures fulfills the obligation to face the qibla.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a sick person who cannot sit due to illness or medical necessity. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling: such a person should pray lying on his back, gesturing with his head for bowing and prostration. The proof is based on qiyas: facing the qibla is obligatory to the extent possible, and lying on the back allows the head gesture to be directed precisely towards the qibla, whereas lying on the side would cause deviation. The text also covers exceptional cases like legal inability (e.g., doctor's order) and provides recommended details for comfort and proper orientation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
State the rule: If a sick person cannot sit, he prays lying on his back, gesturing with his head (imā’) instead of rukū‘ and sujūd.
The ruling is found in the opening sentence: 'If he cannot sit, then on his back he gestures.'
2
Understand the qiyas proof
The proof is that facing the qibla is obligatory to the extent possible. On the back, the gesture points toward the qibla; on the side, it deviates. Deviation without necessity is not allowed.
The effective cause (illa) is the ability to direct the gesture towards the qibla.
3
Apply to edge cases
Consider legal inability: if a doctor forbids sitting (e.g., eye hemorrhage), the same ruling applies because the sanctity of limbs is like the sanctity of the soul. Also, if the patient cannot lie on his back (e.g., hemorrhoids), he prays on his side.
These examples are from al-Bada'i‘ and al-Khulasa.
4
Note the recommended details
Additional recommendations: raise the knees to avoid pointing feet to the qibla, place a pillow under the head to facilitate gestures, and orient the body according to the local qibla direction.
In Central Asia, head to east and feet to west; in Syria, head north, west on right, east on left.
5
Distinguish from other postures
Lying on the side is not permitted because the gesture would deviate from qibla. The only exception is if the patient cannot lie on his back due to medical necessity.
This distinction is crucial for correct practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة المريض الماء اللحد في المريض : إن لم يستطع قاعداً فعلى القفا يوميء إيماء، ولأن التوجه إلى القبلة بالقدر الممكن فرض وذلك في الاستلقاء لأن الإيماء هو تحريك الرأس فإذا صلى مستلقياً يقع إيماؤه إلى القبلة، وإذا صلى على الجنب يقع منحرفاً عنها ولا يجوز الانحراف عنها من غير ضرورة. وقيل : إن المرض الذي كان بعمران باسور فكان لا يستطيع أن يستلقي على قفاه. والمراد في الآية الاضطجاع يقال فلان وضع جنبه إذا نام وإن كان مستلقياً بخلاف الوضع في ا لأنه ليس على الميت فعل يجب توجيهه إلى القبلة ليوضع مستلقياً فكان الاستقبال في الوضع على الجنب. وأطلق في تعذر العقود فشمل التعذر الحكمي كما لو قدر على القعود ولكن بزغ من عينيه فأمره الطبيب أن يستلقي أياماً على ظهره ونهاه عن القعود والسجود أجزأه أن يستلقي ويصلي بالإيماء لأن حرمة الأعضاء كحرمة النفس. كذا في البدائع . وفي الخلاصة : وإذا لم يقدر على القعود صلى مضطجعاً على قفاه متوجهاً نحو القبلة ورأسه إلى المشرق ورجلاه إلى المغرب. وفي المجتبى : وينبغي للمستلقي أن ينصب ركبتيه إن قدر حتى لا يمد رجليه إلى القبلة. وفي العناية : يجعل وسادة تحت رأسه حتى يكون شبه القاعد ليتمكن من الإيماء بالركوع والسجود لأن حقيقة الاستلقاء تمنع الأصحاء عن الإيماء فكيف بالمرضى؟ قوله : (متوجها نحو القبلة ورأسه إلى المشرق الخ هذا إنما يتصور في بلادهم كبخارى وما والاها مما هو جهة المشرق فإن قبلتهم تكون إلى جهة المغرب، وأما في بلادنا الشامية فلا يتصور، بل إذا اضطجع على قفاه نحو القبلة يكون رأسه إلى الشمال والمغرب عن يمينة والمشرق عن يساره، وعلى
The Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Sick Person's Prayer. Water, the niche. Concerning the sick person: If he cannot (sit) while sitting, then on his back he gestures with his head. And because facing the qibla to the extent possible is obligatory, and that is in lying on the back because gesturing is moving the head. When he prays lying on his back, his gesture is towards the qibla, and when he prays on his side, his gesture is turned away from it, and turning away from it without necessity is not permissible. It was said: The illness that was in 'Imran was hemorrhoids, so he could not lie on his back. And what is meant in the verse is lying down; it is said: So-and-so placed his side when he slept, even if he was lying on his back, unlike the placement in... because for the deceased there is no action requiring him to be turned towards the qibla to be placed lying on his back, so facing the qibla is (achieved) by placing on the side. And he (the author) made absolute in the inability of contracts, so it includes legal inability, such as if he can sit but has a hemorrhage from his eyes and the doctor orders him to lie on his back for days and forbids sitting and prostrating; it is sufficient for him to lie and pray with gestures because the sanctity of the limbs is like the sanctity of the soul. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Khulasa: If he cannot sit, he prays lying on his back, facing the qibla, with his head towards the east and his feet towards the west. And in al-Mujtaba: It is recommended for the one lying on his back to raise his knees if he can so that he does not extend his legs towards the qibla. And in al-'Inaya: He should place a pillow under his head so that he is somewhat like a sitting person to be able to gesture for bowing and prostrating, because the reality of lying on the back prevents healthy people from gesturing, so how about the sick? His statement: (Facing the qibla and his head towards the east etc.) This is only conceivable in their lands like Bukhara and its environs, which are towards the east, for their qibla is towards the west. As for our Syrian lands, it is not conceivable; rather, if he lies on his back towards the qibla, his head is towards the north, the west on his right, and the east on his left, and on...
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prayer posture for a sick person who cannot sit. The author states the primary ruling: if unable to sit, the sick person lies on his back and performs gestures (ima') with his head. The proof is that facing the qibla is obligatory to the extent possible, and lying on the back allows the head gesture to be directed towards the qibla, whereas lying on the side would cause the gesture to deviate. The author then addresses an objection regarding a person who cannot lie on his back due to illness like hemorrhoids; such a person lies on his side. A further point: if a person can sit but is ordered by a doctor to lie down due to an eye condition, he prays lying on his back with gestures because the limbs' sanctity is like the soul's. This is from al-Bada'i'. Additional details from al-Khulasa specify positioning: head to east, feet to west (for regions where qibla is west). Al-Mujtaba recommends raising the knees. Al-'Inaya recommends a pillow under the head to facilitate gestures. A marginal note clarifies that the orientation described applies in Central Asia; in Syria (where qibla is south), the directions differ: head north, west on right, east on left.

Key Terms
إيماء (imā’): Gesturing with the head in place of bowing and prostrating when unable to do so physically.
القفا (al-qafā): The back of the neck, but here means lying on the back (istilqā’).
